Nikah — Marriage
advanced
10 min
Touching or Looking with Desire Establishes Marriage Prohibitions
Hanafi ruling with proof on hurmat al-musahara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hurmat al-musahara arising from mass bi-shahwa and nazar bi-shahwa, define the conditions that trigger it, and explain the Hanafi proof and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Touching or looking with desire, defined by physical arousal, makes marriage to certain relatives haram, even without actual intercourse.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a critical family law question: does touching a woman with desire, or looking at her private parts with desire, create permanent marriage prohibitions (hurmat al-musahara)? The Hanafi school says yes, based on the concept of da'i ila al-wat' (incitement to intercourse), while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi ruling, its precise definitions, the proofs from hadith and qiyas khafi, and the practical implications of the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What act triggers prohibition? Answer: touching with desire (mass bi-shahwa) or looking with desire (nazar bi-shahwa). The ruling: hurmat al-musahara is established — the man cannot marry the woman's mother or daughter, and vice versa.
The prohibition is specific to ascendants and descendants of the woman, as well as the man's father and son.
2
Define the conditions
What counts as 'with desire'? For touching, the male organ must become erect or increase in erection. For looking, it must be at the internal private part, typically when the woman is reclining.
The definitions are based on the correct view in the Hidayah; some scholars had alternative definitions.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof
The text uses istihsan based on da'i ila al-wat'. Touching and looking are causes that incite to intercourse, so out of precaution, they are treated like intercourse for this purpose. Also, hadith of Umm Hani and Ibn Umar directly support.
The hadith explicitly state the prohibition arising from looking and touching with desire.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that touching and looking are not equivalent to actual intercourse because they do not nullify fasting, break ihram, or require ghusl. Therefore, they cannot be annexed to intercourse.
This is a qiyas jali argument: since the legal effects differ, the annexation is invalid.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: we do not claim equivalence in all rulings; we only apply the ruling of prohibition in this specific context out of precaution, and the hadith confirms it.
This is a qiyas khafi (istihsan) approach, prioritizing textual evidence over strict analogy.

کسی عورت کو شہوت کے ساتھ چھونے کے بعد اس کے اصول و فروع سے نکاح کا حکم
و من مسته امرأة بشهوة حرمت عليه امها و ابنتها وقال الشافعى لاتحرم وعلى هذا الخلاف مسه امرأة بشهوة ونظره الى فرجها ونظرها الى ذكره عن شهوة له ان المس والنظر ليسا في معنى الدخول ولهذا لا يتعلق بهما فساد الصوم والاحرام ووجوب الاغتسال فلا يلحقان به ولنا ان اللمس والنظر سبب داع الى الوطى فيقام مقامه في موضع الاحتياط ثم ان المس بشهوة ان ينتشر الآلة او تزداد انتشارا هو الصحيح والمعتبر النظر الى الفرج الداخل ولا يتحقق ذلك الا عند اتكائها ولومس فانزل فقد قيل انه يوجب الحرمة والصحيح انه لايوجبها لانه بالانزال تبين انه غير مفض الى الوطى وعلى هذا اتيان المرأة في الدبر
ترجمہ وہ شخص جسکو کسی عورت نے مس کیا شہوت کے ساتھ تو اس مرد پر اس عورت کی ماں اور بیٹی حرام ہو گئیں۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ حرام نہیں ہوئی۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر مرد کا شہوت کے ساتھ عورت کو مس کرتا ہے۔ اور مرد کا عورت کی شرمگاہ کی طرف دیکھنا اور عورت کا مرد کی شرمگاہ کی طرف شہوت کے ساتھ دیکھنا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر دخول کے حکم میں نہیں ہیں اسی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے ساتھ فسادصوم ، فساد احرام اور وجوب انتسال متعلق نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا دونوں دخول کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میں اور نظر ایسا سبب ہے جو داعی الی الوطی ہے۔ پس احتیاط کے موقع میں وطی کے قائم مقام کیا جائے گا۔ پھر مس بشہوۃ یہ ہے کہ آلہ منتشر ہو جائے یا انتشار بڑھ جائے ، یہی صحیح ہے۔ اور معتبر فرج داخل کی جانب دیکھنا ہے اور یہ حق نہیں ہوگا، مگر ٹیک لگا کر بیٹھنے کی صورت میں ۔ اور اگر مس کیا پھر انزال ہو گیا تو کہا گیا کہ موجب حرمت ہوگا۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ موجب حرمت نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ انزال سے یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ وہ مس مفضی الی الوطی نہیں تھا، اور اسی اختلاف پر عورت کے مقعد میں آنا ہے۔ تشریح میں عام ہے عمد ا ہو یا خطاء یا ناسیا ، خوشی سے ہو یا بغیر خوشی ۔ اگر شہوت کیساتھ ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ یہ بات واضح رہے کہ یہاں میں حلال میں اختلاف بیان کرنا مقصود ہے مس حرام میں نہیں ۔ کیونکہ جب امام شافعی کے نزدیک ولی حرام موجب حرمت نہیں۔ تو مس حرام بدرجہ اولی موجب حرمت نہیں ہوگا ۔ ان کا اختلاف مس حلال میں ہے اور اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے ہندہ سے نکاح کے بعد وطی کرنے سے پہلے طلاق دیدی تو زید کیلئے ہندہ کی ماں حلال ہے، اور اگر طلاق سے پہلے زید و بندہ میں سے کسی نے دوسرے کو مس بشہوۃ کیا یا فرج و ذکر پر شہوت کے ساتھ نظر کی اور ولی نہیں کی ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوگئی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے مرد نے عورت کو مس کیا شہوت کے ساتھ یا مرد نے شہوت کے ساتھ عورت کی شرمگاہ کو دیکھایا عورت نے شہوت کے ساتھ مرد کی شرم گاہ کو دیکھا۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر دخول کے حکم میں نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جو احکام دخول کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتے ہیں ان دونوں کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتے۔ مثلا روزے کی حالت میں دخول مفسد صوم اور مفسد احرام ہے اور دخول سے غسل واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن میں بشہوۃ اور نظر بشہوۃ سے نہ روزہ ٹوتا ہے نہ احرام ٹوٹتا ہے اور نہ ہی غسل واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذامس اور نظر کو دخول کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس لئے کہ ملحق کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ الحق بہ کے معنی میں ہو۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر ایسے سبب ہیں جو داعی الی الوطنی ہیں۔ پس ہم نے احتیاطا داعی الی الولی کو ولی کے قائم مقام قرار دے کر اس پر وطی کا حکم لگا دیا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر سے اگر فساد صوم وغیرہ احکام ثابت ہو جاتے تو مس اور نظر بھی حقیقی ولی ہوتے ۔ حالانکہ ہم ان کو حقیقتہ ولی نہیں کہتے ۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید میں حدیث ام ہانی بھی ہے۔
عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم من نظر الى فرج امرأة حرمت عليه امها و بنتها
دوسری حدیث ہے: عن ابن عمر انه قال اذا جامع الرجل المرأة قبلها اولمسها بشهوة او نظر الى فرجها بشهوة حرمت على ابيه وابنه وحرمت عليه امها و ابنتها
عینی شرح هدایه
صاحب ہدایہ نے مس بشہوۃ کی تعریف کی ہے کہ آلہ منتشر ہو جائے جب کہ میں اور نظر سے پہلے منتشر نہیں تھا۔ اور اگر پہلے سے منتشر تھا تو انتشار بڑھ جائے ۔ تعریف کے سلسلہ میں یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ بعض مشائخ نے شہوت کی تعریف یہ کی ہے کہ مرد کا دل عورت کی طرف
The ruling of marriage with the ascendants and descendants of a woman after touching her with desire: And whoever is touched by a woman with desire, her mother and daughter become forbidden to him. And al-Shafi'i said: They do not become forbidden. And upon this difference is the case of a man touching a woman with desire, and his looking at her private part, and her looking at his penis with desire. For al-Shafi'i, touching and looking are not in the meaning of actual entry, and therefore nullification of fasting and ihram and obligation of ghusl are not attached to them, so they are not annexed to entry. And our proof is that touching and looking are a cause that incites to intercourse, so they are made to stand in its place in a situation of precaution. Then touching with desire is that the organ becomes erect or increases in erection; that is the correct view. And the considered looking is at the inside of the private part, and that cannot be realized except when she is leaning. And if he touched and then ejaculated, it has been said that it necessitates prohibition, but the correct view is that it does not necessitate it, because by the ejaculation it becomes clear that that touch was not conducive to intercourse. And upon this difference is entering the woman in the anus. Translation: The person who is touched by a woman with desire, then upon that man the woman's mother and daughter become forbidden. And Imam Shafi'i said they do not become forbidden. And upon this difference is the man touching a woman with desire, and the man looking at her private part, and the woman looking at his private part with desire. Al-Shafi'i's proof is that touching and looking are not in the meaning of actual entry, and therefore nullification of fasting, nullification of ihram, and obligation of ghusl are not attached to them. So both are not annexed to entry. And our proof is that touching and looking are a cause that incites to intercourse, so in a situation of precaution they are made to stand in the place of intercourse. Then touching with desire means that the organ becomes erect or erection increases; that is the correct view. And the considered looking is at the internal private part, and that is not realized except in the case of leaning. And if he touched and then ejaculated, it has been said that it necessitates prohibition, but the correct view is that it does not necessitate it, because by the ejaculation it becomes clear that the touch was not conducive to intercourse. And upon this difference is entering the woman in the anus. Explanation: It is general whether intentional or mistaken or forgetful, willingly or unwillingly. If it is with desire, then according to us the prohibition of musahara is established. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is not established. It should be clear that here the difference is intended regarding halal touching, not haram touching. Because when according to Imam Shafi'i haram intercourse does not necessitate prohibition, then haram touch a fortiori does not necessitate prohibition. Their difference is in halal touch. And the fruit of this difference is that if Zayd married Hind and divorced her before consummation, then for Zayd Hind's mother is halal. But if before divorce, one of them touched the other with desire or looked at private parts with desire and did not have intercourse, then according to us the prohibition of musahara is established, and Imam Shafi'i said it is not established. Similarly, the difference is in the case where a man touched a woman with desire, or a man looked at a woman's private part with desire, or a woman looked at a man's private part with desire. Al-Shafi'i's proof is that touching and looking are not in the ruling of entry, because the rulings that are attached to entry are not attached to them. For example, during fasting, entry nullifies the fast and nullifies ihram, and entry makes ghusl obligatory. But touching with desire and looking with desire do not break the fast, nor break ihram, nor make ghusl obligatory. Therefore touching and looking cannot be annexed to entry, because for annexation it is necessary that the annexed be in the meaning of the thing to which it is annexed. Our proof is that touching and looking are a cause that incites to intercourse, so we, out of precaution, have made the inciter to intercourse stand in the place of intercourse and applied the ruling of intercourse to it. The answer to Imam Shafi'i's proof: If touching and looking had established the rulings like nullification of fasting etc., then touching and looking would be real intercourse. But we do not say they are real intercourse. Supporting our school is the hadith of Umm Hani: From the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and daughter become forbidden to him.' Another hadith: From Ibn Umar that he said: 'When a man has intercourse with a woman, kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire, then his father and son become forbidden to her, and her mother and daughter become forbidden to him.' Commentary by 'Ayni on Hidayah: The author of Hidayah defined touching with desire as the organ becoming erect, when it was not erect before the touch or look, or if it was already erect, then the erection increases. This is the correct view regarding the definition. Some scholars defined desire as the man's heart inclining towards the woman.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the effect of touching or looking at a woman's private parts with desire on the prohibition of marriage (hurmat al-musahara). The Hanafi ruling: if a man touches a woman with desire (mass bi-shahwa), or looks at her private parts with desire, or a woman looks at his private parts with desire, then certain marriage prohibitions are established: the man is forbidden from marrying the woman's mother and daughter, and the woman is forbidden from marrying the man's father and son. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that such prohibitions are not established. The Hanafi proof: touching and looking are causes that incite to intercourse (da'i ila al-wat'), so out of precaution (ihtiyat), they are given the same ruling as actual intercourse regarding marriage prohibitions. The Shafi'i proof: touching and looking are not equivalent to actual intercourse because they do not nullify fasting or ihram, nor require ghusl, so they cannot be treated like intercourse. The Hanafi response: we are not equating them in all rulings, only in the specific context of marriage prohibitions out of precaution. The text further defines touching with desire as causing erection or increased erection. Looking with desire must be at the internal private part (which typically occurs during reclining). If ejaculation occurs from touching, some say it establishes prohibition, but the correct Hanafi view is that it does not, because ejaculation shows the touch was not really conducive to intercourse. The same difference applies to anal intercourse. The text clarifies that the dispute concerns halal touching (like between spouses or after marriage but before consummation), not haram touching (which is already forbidden). The practical application (thamar al-khilaf): if a husband divorces his wife before consummation, he may marry her mother. But if during the marriage (before divorce) they touched with desire or looked with desire, prohibition is established according to Hanafis, not Shafi'is. The text concludes by citing two hadith: one from Umm Hani and one from Ibn Umar, supporting the Hanafi view. Finally, it defines mass bi-shahwa as the organ becoming erect or increasing in erection, which is the correct view.

Key Terms
مس بشہوۃ (mass bi-shahwa): Touching with sexual desire; defined as causing the male organ to become erect or increase in erection.
نظر بشہوۃ (nazar bi-shahwa): Looking at the private parts (internal) with sexual desire; considered effective only when the woman is in a reclining position.
داعی الی الوطی (da'i ila al-wat'): Incitement to intercourse; the effective cause (illa) for equating touching/looking with actual intercourse in the context of prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct definition of 'mass bi-shahwa' (touching with desire) that establishes hurmat al-musahara?
A) Any physical contact between a man and woman.
B) Touching that causes the male organ to become erect or increase in erection.
C) Touching that leads to ejaculation.
D) Touching that breaks the fast.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes hurmat al-musahara through touching or looking with desire based on precaution and strong hadith evidence, a view distinct from Imam al-Shafi'i's position.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Touch and Look with Desire: Cause of Prohibition by Affinity
Inter-madhhab dispute with expanded definitions and sub-rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on touch and look with desire causing prohibition by affinity, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of داعی الی الوطی (cause leading to intercourse).

Core Idea
Acts leading to intercourse (داعی الی الوطی) are given the same ruling as intercourse for establishing marriage prohibitions.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is: whether touching or looking with desire (without actual intercourse) creates permanent marriage prohibitions between in-laws (حرمت مصاہرت). The Hanafi school, based on precaution and hadith evidence, holds that such acts are legally equivalent to intercourse for this specific purpose. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing that these acts do not carry other consequences of intercourse like breaking fast or requiring ghusl. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists extend rulings by considering the underlying cause (علت) and the principle of precaution (احتیاط).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: touch (مس) or look (نظر) with desire makes certain relatives permanently prohibited for marriage, just like actual intercourse. This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The prohibition is not on the act itself but on subsequent marriage to specified relatives.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that touch and look with desire do not cause any prohibition by affinity. His proof is based on the lack of other effects of intercourse.
The dispute is about 'halal' touch (e.g., between spouses), not unlawful touch.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues: if touch/look were equivalent to intercourse, they would break the fast, invalidate ihram, and require ghusl. Since they do not, they cannot be equated to intercourse for any ruling, including prohibition.
This is a qiyas argument based on the absence of concomitant effects.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that they do not claim actual equivalence (haqiqatan). Rather, they treat touch/look as equivalent only in the specific ruling of prohibition by affinity, because they are a cause leading to intercourse (داعی الی الوطی). Precaution (احتیاط) requires giving the same ruling for the cause as for the result in this context.
The annexation (الحاق) is partial and specific, not general.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: e.g., if a man touches his wife's mother with desire (or looks at her private part), according to Hanafis the mother becomes permanently prohibited for him; according to Shafi'is she does not. This affects real marriage possibilities.
The same applies to a man's father and son if a woman touches/looks with desire.

کتاب النکاح دونوں کے ساتھ فسادصوم ، فساد احرام اور وجوب انتسال متعلق نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا دونوں دخول کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میں اور نظر ایسا سبب ہے جو داعی الی الوطی ہے۔ پس احتیاط کے موقع میں وطی کے قائم مقام کیا جائے گا۔ پھر مس بشہوۃ یہ ہے کہ آلہ منتشر ہو جائے یا انتشار بڑھ جائے ، یہی صحیح ہے۔ اور معتبر فرج داخل کی جانب دیکھنا ہے اور یہ حق نہیں ہوگا، مگر ٹیک لگا کر بیٹھنے کی صورت میں ۔ اور اگر مس کیا پھر انزال ہو گیا تو کہا گیا کہ موجب حرمت ہوگا۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ موجب حرمت نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ انزال سے یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ وہ مس مفضی الی الوطی نہیں تھا، اور اسی اختلاف پر عورت کے مقعد میں آنا ہے۔ تشریح میں عام ہے عمد ا ہو یا خطاء یا ناسیا ، خوشی سے ہو یا بغیر خوشی ۔ اگر شہوت کیساتھ ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ یہ بات واضح رہے کہ یہاں میں حلال میں اختلاف بیان کرنا مقصود ہے مس حرام میں نہیں ۔ کیونکہ جب امام شافعی کے نزدیک ولی حرام موجب حرمت نہیں۔ تو مس حرام بدرجہ اولی موجب حرمت نہیں ہوگا ۔ ان کا اختلاف مس حلال میں ہے اور اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے ہندہ سے نکاح کے بعد وطی کرنے سے پہلے طلاق دیدی تو زید کیلئے ہندہ کی ماں حلال ہے، اور اگر طلاق سے پہلے زید و بندہ میں سے کسی نے دوسرے کو مس بشہوۃ کیا یا فرج و ذکر پر شہوت کے ساتھ نظر کی اور ولی نہیں کی ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوگئی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے مرد نے عورت کو مس کیا شہوت کے ساتھ یا مرد نے شہوت کے ساتھ عورت کی شرمگاہ کو دیکھایا عورت نے شہوت کے ساتھ مرد کی شرم گاہ کو دیکھا۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر دخول کے حکم میں نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جو احکام دخول کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتے ہیں ان دونوں کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتے۔ مثلا روزے کی حالت میں دخول مفسد صوم اور مفسد احرام ہے اور دخول سے غسل واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن میں بشہوۃ اور نظر بشہوۃ سے نہ روزہ ٹوتا ہے نہ احرام ٹوٹتا ہے اور نہ ہی غسل واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذامس اور نظر کو دخول کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس لئے کہ ملحق کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ الحق بہ کے معنی میں ہو۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر ایسے سبب ہیں جو داعی الی الوطنی ہیں۔ پس ہم نے احتیاطا داعی الی الولی کو ولی کے قائم مقام قرار دے کر اس پر وطی کا حکم لگا دیا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مس اور نظر سے اگر فساد صوم وغیرہ احکام ثابت ہو جاتے تو مس اور نظر بھی حقیقی ولی ہوتے ۔ حالانکہ ہم ان کو حقیقتہ ولی نہیں کہتے ۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید میں حدیث ام ہانی بھی ہے۔

عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم من نظر الى فرج امرأة حرمت عليه امها و بنتها

دوسری حدیث ہے: عن ابن عمر انه قال اذا جامع الرجل المرأة قبلها اولمسها بشهوة او نظر الى فرجها بشهوة حرمت على ابيه وابنه وحرمت عليه امها و ابنتها

عینی شرح هدایه

صاحب ہدایہ نے مس بشہوۃ کی تعریف کی ہے کہ آلہ منتشر ہو جائے جب کہ میں اور نظر سے پہلے منتشر نہیں تھا۔ اور اگر پہلے سے منتشر تھا تو انتشار بڑھ جائے ۔ تعریف کے سلسلہ میں یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ بعض مشائخ نے شہوت کی تعریف یہ کی ہے کہ مرد کا دل عورت کی طرف

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد چہارم
کتاب النکاح مائل ہو جائے اور جماع کی طرف رغبت ہو جائے۔ نظر الی فرج میں فرج داخل کی طرف دیکھنا معتبر ہے، فرج خارج کی طرف نہیں۔ اور فرج داخل کی طرف دیکھنا اس وقت متحقق ہوگا جبکہ عورت دیوار وغیرہ سے برہنہ ہو کر ٹیک لگا کر دونوں گھٹے کھڑے کر کے بیٹھے، چنانچہ اگر عورت سیدھی بیٹھی ہے یا کھڑی ہے یا ٹیک لگا کر پاؤں پھیلا کر میٹھی ہے پھر اس کی طرف دیکھا تو حرمت مصاہرت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر مس کیا پھر انزال ہو گیا تو حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ بعض کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ وجہ یہ کہ انزال معنی وطی کو موکد کرتا ہے، لہذا حرمت میں زیادتی ہی ہوگی۔ صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں حرمت مصاہرت ثابت نہیں ہو گی۔ اس لئے کہ میں بشہوۃ مفضی الی الوطی ہونے کی وجہ سے وطی کے قائم مقام تھا، اور انزال سے یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ یہ مس مفضی الی الوطی نہیں ہے ، لہذ اوٹی کے قائم مقام بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی حکم پر عورت کے مقعد میں وطی کرنا یعنی اگر عورت کے مقعد میں وطی کی اور انزال ہو گیا تو موجب حرمت نہیں اور اگر انزال نہیں ہوا تو موجب حرمت ہے۔
The Book of Marriage: With both (touch and look) the corruption of fasting, corruption of ihram, and obligation of ghusl are not connected. Therefore, both are not annexed to intercourse. Our proof is that touch and look are a cause that leads to intercourse. So out of precaution, they are made to stand in place of intercourse. Then touching with desire is that the organ becomes erect or its erection increases; this is correct. And what is considered is looking at the inner private part, and this is not achieved except in the posture of leaning back sitting. And if he touched and then ejaculated, some said it causes prohibition, but the correct view is that it does not cause prohibition because the ejaculation shows that the touch was not leading to intercourse. And upon this difference is the case of entering the woman's anus. The explanation is general: intentionally or mistakenly or forgetfully, willingly or unwillingly. If it is with desire, then according to us the prohibition of affinity is established. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is not established. It should be clear that the intended difference here is about permissible touch, not prohibited, because when permissible touch does not cause prohibition according to Imam al-Shafi'i, then prohibited touch would even more so not cause prohibition. Their difference is about permissible touch, and the fruit of this difference is that if Zayd married Hind and divorced her before intercourse, then for Zayd Hind's mother is permissible. If before the divorce, one of them touched the other with desire or looked at the private part and organ with desire and did not have intercourse, then according to us the prohibition of affinity is established, and Imam al-Shafi'i said it would not be established. Similarly, the difference is in the case where a man touched a woman with desire or a man looked at a woman's private part with desire, or a woman looked at a man's private part with desire.

Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that touch and look are not in the ruling of intercourse because the rulings that apply to intercourse do not apply to them. For example, during fasting, intercourse invalidates the fast and ihram, and intercourse makes ghusl obligatory. But from touching with desire and looking with desire, the fast is not broken, ihram is not broken, nor is ghusl obligatory. Therefore, touch and look cannot be annexed to intercourse because for annexation it is necessary that the annexed be in the meaning of that to which it is annexed. Our proof is that touch and look are a cause that leads to intercourse. So we out of precaution made that which leads to intercourse stand in place of intercourse and applied the ruling of intercourse to them. The response to Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that if from touch and look the rulings of corruption of fasting etc. were established, then touch and look would be actual intercourse. However, we do not say they are actual intercourse. Supporting our madhhab is the hadith of Umm Hani.

From the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and her daughter are prohibited for him.'

Another hadith: From Ibn Umar that he said: 'When a man has intercourse with a woman, or kisses her, or touches her with desire, or looks at her private part with desire, his father and his son become prohibited for her, and her mother and her daughter become prohibited for him.'

Ayni Sharh Hidayah

The author of Hidayah defined touching with desire as that the organ becomes erect when it was not erect before touch or look, or its erection increases. In the matter of definition, this is the correct statement. Some mashayikh defined desire as that the man's heart inclines towards the woman and he desires intercourse. In looking at the private part, looking at the inner private part is considered, not the outer. And looking at the inner private part is realized when the woman, being naked, leans back with both knees raised. So if the woman is sitting upright or standing, or leaning back with legs spread, then looking does not establish prohibition. One case is if he touched and then ejaculated, does prohibition become established or not? Some are of the opinion that in this case prohibition is established because ejaculation reinforces the meaning of intercourse, so it only increases prohibition. The correct view is that prohibition is not established because the touch with desire was made to stand in place of intercourse due to being a means leading to intercourse, and from the ejaculation it became apparent that this touch was not leading to intercourse, so it will not stand in place of intercourse. Upon the same ruling is intercourse in the anus of a woman: if one has intercourse in the anus and ejaculates, it does not cause prohibition; if he does not ejaculate, it causes prohibition.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether touching (مس) or looking (نظر) with desire (شہوت) causes prohibition by affinity (حرمت مصاہرت). The commentary expands on definitions and sub-rulings. The Hanafi position, based on precaution (احتیاط) and the principle that acts leading to intercourse (داعی الی الوطی) are given the same ruling as intercourse for the purpose of establishing marriage prohibitions, holds that touch or look with desire makes certain relatives permanently prohibited. The Shafi'i position argues that since touch and look do not invalidate fasting, break ihram, or necessitate ghusl, they cannot be equated to intercourse. The Hanafi response distinguishes between actual intercourse and a legal annexation based on the cause. The text then defines touching with desire as causing erection or increased erection, and looking at the inner private part requires a specific posture. A further sub-ruling: if touch is followed by ejaculation, the correct view is that prohibition is not established because the ejaculation shows the touch was not leading to intercourse. Similarly, intercourse in the anus only causes prohibition if no ejaculation occurs.

Key Terms
مس بشہوۃ (mas bi shahwah): Touching with desire; defined as the organ becoming erect or its erection increasing.
نظر بشہوۃ (nazar bi shahwah): Looking with desire at the private part (فرج داخل) of the opposite sex.
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat musaharah): The prohibition of marriage due to affinity relations (e.g., a man marrying his wife's mother or daughter).
داعی الی الوطی (da'i ila al-wati): That which leads or incites to intercourse, such as touching or looking with desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct ruling if a man touches his wife's mother with desire but does not ejaculate?
A) No prohibition arises because there was no intercourse.
B) The man becomes prohibited from marrying his wife's mother (his mother-in-law).
C) The man must perform ghusl.
D) The man's marriage to his wife becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, touching or looking with desire is legally equivalent to intercourse for establishing affinity prohibitions, based on the principle that the cause leading to a result takes the same ruling by way of precaution.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Marrying Sister During Iddah of Revocable or Irrevocable Divorce
Inter-madhhab dispute on marrying sister during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits marrying the sister of a divorced wife during her iddah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of remaining legal effects of marriage.

Core Idea
A divorce does not immediately sever all marriage effects; the iddah keeps the bond partially alive, barring the sister's marriage.

You've learned that combining two sisters in marriage is prohibited. But what if one wife is divorced? When does her iddah end the prohibition? The Hanafi school holds that during iddah, the original marriage is still legally relevant, so her sister remains forbidden. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees for irrevocable divorces. Let's explore the proof and nuance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister during iddah after both revocable and irrevocable divorce.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i allows it if the iddah is from a bain or third divorce.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: the qati' (divorce) severs the marriage completely, and the application of hadd for intercourse supports this.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi counter: the marriage remains for some rulings (nafaqa, farash), the qati' is delayed, and the hadd texts are reconciled through partial severance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis prohibit the marriage during iddah, Shafi'is allow it after bain/third talaq.

ایک عورت کو طلاق بائن یا رجعی دی تو اس کی بہن سے نکاح اسوقت کر سکتا ہے جبکہ اس کی عدت ختم ہو جائے .... امام شافعی کا نقطۂ نظر

و اذا طلق امرأته طلاقا بائنا او رجعيا لم يجزله ان يتزوج باختها حتى تنقضى عدتها وقال الشافعى ان كانت العدة عن طلاق بائن اوثلث يجوز لانقطاع النكاح بالكلية اعمالا للقاطع ولهذا لووطيها مع العلم بالحرمة جب الحدولنا ان نكاح الأولى قائم لبقاء احكامه كالنفقة والمنع والفراش والقاطع تاخر عمله ولهذا بقى القيد والحد لا يجب على اشارة كتاب الطلاق وعلى عبارة كتاب الحدود يجب لان الملك قدزال في حق الحل فيتحقق الزناء ولم يرتفع فى حق ماذكرنا فيصير جامعا

ترجمہ اور اگر اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دے دے طلاق بائن یار جعی تو اس مرد کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس کی بہن سے نکاح کرے یہاں تک کہ اس معدہ کی عدت گذر جائے ۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اگر وہ عورت طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقوں کی عدت میں ہو تو جائز ہے۔ بالکلیہ نکاح کے منقطع ہونے کی وجہ سے قاطع طلاق کو عمل دیتے ہوئے ۔ اور اسی وجہ سے اگر اس مطلقہ بائنہ سے وطی کی حرمت کو جاتے ہو نے ولی کی تو حد واجب ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہلی کا نکاح باقی ہے احکام نکاح کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے ، جیسے نفقہ اور منع عن الخروج اور فراش اور قاطع کا عمل مؤخر ہو گیا، اسی وجہ سے قید نکاح باقی ہے۔ اور حال یہ ہے کہ کتاب الطلاق میں اشارہ نکلتا ہے کہ حد واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ اور کتاب الحدود میں صراحت ہے کہ حد واجب ہوگی، اس لئے کہ ملک وطی کے حلال ہونے کے حق میں زائل ہوگئی پس زنا متحقق ہوگا۔ اور امور مذکورہ کے حق میں ملک مرتفع نہیں ہوئی ، پس جامع بین الا حسین ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن یا طلاق رجعی دی سواب یہ شخص اس معدہ کی بہن سے زمانہ عدت میں نکاح کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ احناف کا مذہب تو یہ ہے کہ نکاح جائز نہیں۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اگر وہ عورت طلاق بائن یا تین طلاق کی وجہ سے عدت میں ہے تو اس کی بہن سے نکاح جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قاطع نکاح یعنی طلاق کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے نکاح بالکلیہ منقطع ہو گیا، اس لئے کہ جب
If a woman is given a revocable (bain) or irrevocable (raj'i) divorce, he can marry her sister only when her iddah expires.... Imam al-Shafi'i's viewpoint: And when he divorces his wife an irrevocable (bain) or revocable (raj'i) divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry her sister until her iddah expires. Al-Shafi'i said: If the iddah is from an irrevocable divorce or a third divorce, it is permissible because the marriage is completely severed, applying the effect of the severing. For this reason, if he has intercourse with her knowingly of the prohibition, the hadd punishment is obligatory. Our proof is that the first marriage remains due to the continuation of its rulings, such as maintenance, prohibition from leaving the house, and the marriage bed. The severing (qati') is delayed in its operation, so the bond of marriage remains. And it is stated in the Book of Talaq that the hadd is not obligatory, while in the Book of Hudud it is explicitly stated that the hadd is obligatory because the ownership of permissible intercourse is removed, so zina is realized, but it is not removed in the matters we mentioned, so it becomes a combination. Explanation of the issue: A person gave his wife a bain or raj'i divorce, then can he marry her sister during the iddah? The Hanafi madhhab says it is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i said that if the woman is in iddah due to a bain or three divorces, then marrying her sister is permissible. The gist of Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that due to the presence of the severing (talaq), the marriage is completely severed, because when...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a man can marry his wife's sister during the wife's iddah after a revocable (رجعی) or irrevocable (بائن) divorce. The Hanafi position is that it is not permissible until the iddah expires because the original marriage is considered ongoing in its legal effects (such as maintenance, prohibition from remarrying, and the marital bed) even after the divorce. Therefore, the woman during iddah is still like a wife in some respects, and marrying her sister would combine two sisters in marriage, which is prohibited. The Shafi'i position distinguishes: if the divorce is irrevocable (bain or third), the marriage is completely severed, so there is no harm in marrying the sister immediately. They support this by arguing that if the man knowingly has intercourse with the divorced woman during iddah, the hadd punishment for zina applies, indicating the marriage is fully ended. The Hanafi response notes an apparent contradiction in the Hanafi texts: in Kitab al-Talaq it says no hadd, while in Kitab al-Hudud it says hadd applies. The reconciliation is that ownership of permissible intercourse is removed (so zina is possible), but other rulings of marriage remain (so it is not full zina), thus the punishment may not apply. This shows the marriage is not completely severed. Hence, marrying the sister is not allowed.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying. In this context, it is the period during which a divorcée cannot remarry.
قاطع (qati'): The severer; here referring to divorce (talaq) which severs the marriage bond.
نکاح اولی قائم (nikah ula qa'im): The first marriage is considered ongoing in its legal effects during iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a man marry his wife's sister during the wife's iddah after an irrevocable (bain) divorce?
A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, it is not permissible until the iddah expires.
C) Yes, but only if the wife consents.
D) No, it is never permissible even after iddah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a divorced wife remains legally connected to her husband during iddah, making it impermissible to marry her sister until the iddah ends.

Establishing Prohibition of Marriage by Looking and Touching: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Conditions for prohibition via looking/touching and dispute on ejaculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for prohibition of marriage through in-law relationship via looking and touching, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ejaculation.

Core Idea
Lustful touch establishes prohibition only if it leads to intercourse; ejaculation breaks that equivalence.

This passage clarifies the specific conditions under which looking at or touching a person of the opposite sex can create a permanent prohibition of marriage with their relatives (musāharat). It also addresses a subtle dispute within the Hanafi school about the role of ejaculation in cases of lustful touch and anal intercourse. Understanding these details is essential for correctly applying the rulings on mahramiyyah.

Guided Path
1
State the conditions for looking
Identify the required posture for the woman and what part must be visible for looking to establish prohibition.
The posture must reveal the inner private part (فرج داخل).
2
Explain the qiyas for touch
Understand why lustful touch without ejaculation is treated as equivalent to incomplete intercourse for establishing prohibition.
The illa is 'leading to intercourse' (مفضی الی الوطی).
3
Analyze the dispute on ejaculation
Present both views: some hold ejaculation reinforces prohibition, while the correct view says it breaks equivalence.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the same rule to anal intercourse
Extend the same reasoning: without ejaculation, it establishes prohibition; with ejaculation, it does not.
Consistency in the school's methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مائل ہو جائے اور جماع کی طرف رغبت ہو جائے۔ نظر الی فرج میں فرج داخل کی طرف دیکھنا معتبر ہے، فرج خارج کی طرف نہیں۔ اور فرج داخل کی طرف دیکھنا اس وقت متحقق ہوگا جبکہ عورت دیوار وغیرہ سے برہنہ ہو کر ٹیک لگا کر دونوں گھٹے کھڑے کر کے بیٹھے، چنانچہ اگر عورت سیدھی بیٹھی ہے یا کھڑی ہے یا ٹیک لگا کر پاؤں پھیلا کر میٹھی ہے پھر اس کی طرف دیکھا تو حرمت مصاہرت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر مس کیا پھر انزال ہو گیا تو حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ بعض کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ وجہ یہ کہ انزال معنی وطی کو موکد کرتا ہے، لہذا حرمت میں زیادتی ہی ہوگی۔ صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں حرمت مصاہرت ثابت نہیں ہو گی۔ اس لئے کہ میں بشہوۃ مفضی الی الوطی ہونے کی وجہ سے وطی کے قائم مقام تھا، اور انزال سے یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ یہ مس مفضی الی الوطی نہیں ہے ، لہذ اوٹی کے قائم مقام بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی حکم پر عورت کے مقعد میں وطی کرنا یعنی اگر عورت کے مقعد میں وطی کی اور انزال ہو گیا تو موجب حرمت نہیں اور اگر انزال نہیں ہوا تو موجب حرمت ہے۔
He becomes inclined and desires intercourse. Looking at the private part: looking at the inner private part is considered, not the outer. And looking at the inner private part is realized when the woman, naked against a wall etc., sits leaning with both knees raised. So if the woman is sitting straight, or standing, or leaning with legs spread, and he looks at her, then the prohibition of in-law marriage is not established. Another case: if he touched and then ejaculated, does the prohibition of in-law marriage become established? Some opine that in this case also the prohibition is established. The reason is that ejaculation reinforces the meaning of intercourse, so the prohibition would only increase. The correct view is that in this case the prohibition is not established. Because the touch was with desire leading to intercourse, so it stood in place of intercourse, but the ejaculation shows that this touch was not leading to intercourse, so it also does not stand in place of intercourse. The same ruling applies to anal intercourse: if he has anal intercourse with a woman and ejaculates, it does not cause prohibition; if he does not ejaculate, it does cause prohibition.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions under which looking at a woman or touching her establishes the prohibition of marriage through in-law relationship (حرمت مصاہرت). The author begins by specifying that only looking at the inner private part (فرج داخل) is considered, not the outer. He describes the specific posture that reveals the inner part: the woman must be naked, leaning against something with both knees raised. If she is in any other position, looking does not establish prohibition. Then he discusses the case of touching (مس) with desire. If a man touches a woman with desire and then ejaculates, some scholars argue that the prohibition is established because ejaculation strengthens the analogy to intercourse. However, the correct Hanafi position is that prohibition is not established. The reasoning is that the touch was initially considered equivalent to intercourse because it was leading to it (مفضی الی الوطی), but the fact that ejaculation occurred shows that the touch itself was not actually leading to intercourse (since the desire was satisfied by the touch alone), so it loses its equivalence. Finally, the same rule applies to anal intercourse: if it is performed without ejaculation, it establishes prohibition (like incomplete intercourse), but with ejaculation, it does not (because the act is already completed and does not require equivalence).

Key Terms
مصاہرت (musāharat): In-law relationship; prohibition of marriage between a man and certain female relatives of his wife.
مس بشہوۃ (massun bi-shahwah): Lustful touch; touch with sexual desire.
مفضی الی الوطی (mufḍī ilā al-waṭʾ): Leading to intercourse; an act that directly results in or is intended to result in intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man touches a woman with desire and then ejaculates, is the prohibition of marriage through in-law relationship (حرمت مصاہرت) established?
A) Yes, because ejaculation reinforces the meaning of intercourse.
B) No, because the ejaculation shows the touch was not leading to intercourse.
C) Yes, if the touch was with desire.
D) No, unless the touch was without desire.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires specific conditions for the prohibition of marriage through in-law relationship; lustful touch only creates prohibition if it leads to intercourse, and ejaculation breaks that equivalence.

Nikah — Marriage

Marrying the Sister of a Divorced Woman During Her Iddah
Inter-madhhab dispute on marrying a divorced woman's sister during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school forbids marrying the sister of a divorced woman during iddah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A marriage persists partially during iddah; thus marrying the sister is combining two sisters, even after irrevocable divorce.

Should a man be allowed to marry his ex-wife's sister while the ex-wife is still in her waiting period? At first glance, an irrevocable divorce seems to sever all ties. But the Hanafi school looks deeper: certain duties and rights remain, so the marriage is not fully over. This lesson uncovers the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position and contrasts it with Imam al-Shafi'i's view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate the Hanafi ruling: a man cannot marry the sister of his divorced wife until her iddah expires, whether the divorce is revocable or irrevocable.
This applies to both talaq raj'i and talaq ba'in.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Identify Imam al-Shafi'i as the opponent. He holds that if the divorce is irrevocable (bain or third), the marriage is completely severed, so marrying the sister is permissible.
Shafi'i distinguishes between revocable and irrevocable divorce.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that the marriage is completely severed because the severance (qati') has occurred. His evidence: if the man has intercourse with the divorced woman knowing it is haram, the hadd punishment becomes obligatory, which would not apply if the marriage were still in effect.
Hadd is used as an indicator of complete dissolution.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts: 1) The obligation of hadd is itself disputed (some texts indicate it is not wajib). 2) Even if hadd is wajib, it only shows that the ownership of intercourse is removed, but other marriage rulings (nafaqah, restriction, farash) remain. Thus the marriage continues partially.
The Hanafis invoke the concept of 'marriage from one aspect' (min wajh).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis forbid marrying the sister in all cases; Shafi'is permit it after an irrevocable divorce. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi within the Hanafi school.
The difference affects fatwa in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

و اذا طلق امرأته طلاقا بائنا او رجعيا لم يجزله ان يتزوج باختها حتى تنقضى عدتها وقال الشافعى ان كانت العدة عن طلاق بائن اوثلث يجوز لانقطاع النكاح بالكلية اعمالا للقاطع ولهذا لووطيها مع العلم بالحرمة جب الحدولنا ان نكاح الأولى قائم لبقاء احكامه كالنفقة والمنع والفراش والقاطع تاخر عمله ولهذا بقى القيد والحد لا يجب على اشارة كتاب الطلاق وعلى عبارة كتاب الحدود يجب لان الملك قدزال في حق الحل فيتحقق الزناء ولم يرتفع فى حق ماذكرنا فيصير جامعا

قاطع پایا گیا تو اس کا اثر بھی یقینا متفق ہوگا۔ نکاح کے بالکلیہ منقطع ہونے کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر شخص حرام سمجھ کر معتدہ سے وطی کر لے تو حد واجب ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ معدہ کا نکاح باقی ہے، اس لئے کہ نکاح کے بعض احکام باقی ہیں، مثلا عدت کے زمانہ میں شوہر پر اسی طرح نفقہ واجب ہوگا جس طرح منکوحہ ہونے کی حالت میں تھا۔ اور شوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ گھر سے نکلنے پر پابندی لگا دے۔ اسی طرح اگر دو سال کے اندر اندر بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو فراش ہونے کی وجہ سے اسی شخص سے نسب بھی ثابت ہوگا۔ اور رہی یہ بات کہ قاطع نکاح پایا گیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قاطع کاعمل انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے مؤخر ہو گیا حکم نکاح کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس کا جواب کہ وطی کرنے سے حد واجب ہوتی ہے، اولاً تو ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ اس وطی پر حد واجب ہوگی ، جیسا کہ مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق میں اشارہ ملتا ہے اور اگر تعلیم بھی کر لیں تو حد واجب ہوگی جیسا کہ مبسوط کی کتاب الحدود میں صراحنا موجود ہے، تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ ولی کے حلال ہونے کے حق میں ملک نکاح زائل ہوگئی ، لہذا یہ ولی زنا ہوگی اور امور مذکورہ کے حق میں ملک زائل نہیں ہوتی ، پس نکاح من وجہ باقی ہے اور من وجہ غیر باقی ۔ اور جب من وجہ نکاح باقی ہے تو یہ شخص اس معدہ کی بہن سے نکاح کر کے جامع بین الا حتین فی النکاح ہوگا اور نکاح میں جمع بین الاختین نا جائز ہے، اگر چہ نکاح فی الجملہ ہو۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
If a man gives his wife a revocable or irrevocable divorce, he cannot marry her sister until her iddah expires... Imam al-Shafi'i's view: And if he divorces his wife with an irrevocable or revocable divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry her sister until her iddah expires. Al-Shafi'i said: if the iddah is from an irrevocable or third divorce, it is permissible because the marriage is completely severed, applying the severance. For this reason, if he has intercourse with her knowing the prohibition, the prescribed punishment (hadd) becomes obligatory. Our proof is that the first marriage persists due to the continuation of its rulings, such as maintenance, restriction, and the marriage bed. The severance's effect is delayed. Hence the restriction remains. It is indicated in the Book of Divorce that hadd is not obligatory, but in the Book of Hudud it is explicitly stated that it is obligatory, because the ownership of intercourse is removed in terms of permissibility, so adultery is realized, but it is not removed in terms of the matters we mentioned, so it becomes a combination. ... Explanation: The issue is: a man gives his wife a revocable or irrevocable divorce; can he marry her sister during the iddah? The Hanafi school says no. Imam Shafi'i said: if she is in iddah due to irrevocable or third divorce, it is permissible. The gist of Shafi'i's proof is that the divorce (severance) has occurred, so the marriage is completely severed. The evidence for complete severance is that if he has intercourse with the woman in iddah knowing it is prohibited, hadd becomes obligatory. Our proof is that the marriage of the woman in iddah still exists because some rulings of marriage remain: maintenance is obligatory on the husband just as before, he has the right to restrict her from leaving the house, and if a child is born within two years, lineage is established due to the marriage bed. As for the argument that the severance has occurred, we respond that the effect of the severance is delayed until the end of iddah due to the remaining rulings of marriage. As for the argument that hadd becomes obligatory due to intercourse, first we do not accept that hadd is obligatory in this case, as indicated in al-Mabsut's Book of Divorce. And if we do accept it (for the sake of argument), then we say: the ownership of marriage has been removed in terms of permissibility of intercourse, so this intercourse is adultery, but it has not been removed in terms of the matters mentioned, so the marriage remains from one aspect and not from another. Since the marriage remains from one aspect, this man marrying the sister makes him combine two sisters in marriage, which is prohibited even if the marriage is partial. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether a man may marry the sister of his divorced wife during the latter's iddah period. The Hanafi position is clear: it is not permissible, whether the divorce is revocable (رجعی) or irrevocable (بائن). The reason is that the marriage is still legally in effect for certain purposes: the husband must provide maintenance, can restrict her movement, and any child born within two years is attributed to him. Thus, marrying the sister would combine two sisters in marriage simultaneously. Imam Shafi'i, however, distinguishes between revocable and irrevocable divorce. In his view, if the divorce is irrevocable (bain or third talaq), the marriage is completely severed, so there is no impediment to marrying the sister. He supports this by arguing that if the man has intercourse with the divorced woman knowing it is haram, he incurs the hadd punishment, which would not apply if the marriage were still in effect. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, they note that in the Book of Divorce in al-Mabsut, it is indicated that hadd is not obligatory, suggesting inconsistency in Shafi'i's proof. Second, even if hadd were obligatory, that does not mean the marriage is completely severed; rather, the ownership of intercourse (ملک الوطی) is removed for permissibility, but the other rights and obligations remain. Hence the marriage persists partially, and the prohibition of combining two sisters remains valid. This shows the importance of the legal concept that a marriage can be partially ongoing ('من وجہ') even after divorce, as long as its effects continue.

Key Terms
عدت (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband, during which she cannot remarry.
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bāʾin): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
قاطع نکاح (qāṭiʿ al-nikāḥ): The severance of marriage; a factor that terminates the marriage contract completely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible for a man to marry the sister of his ex-wife during the ex-wife's iddah after an irrevocable divorce?
A) Yes, because the marriage is completely severed.
B) No, because some rulings of marriage persist.
C) Yes, if he has not consummated the marriage.
D) No, only if the divorce was revocable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the iddah period after divorce preserves certain marital effects, making it impermissible to marry the divorced woman's sister until the iddah expires.

Marriage Between Owner and Owned: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling and rational proof for prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage between owner and owned, explain the rationale based on the conflict between ownership and marital benefits, and identify the objection regarding a slave's marriage to a free woman.

Core Idea
Ownership and marriage are incompatible — a master cannot marry his slave because marital benefits require equality, not subjugation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a clear prohibition: a master cannot marry his own slave-girl, nor can a woman marry her own male slave. The ruling is based on a rational legal analysis (dalil aqli) that identifies a fundamental conflict between the rights of ownership (mālikiyyah) and the mutual benefits required by marriage (thamarat al-nikāḥ). The text also anticipates an objection: if ownership blocks marriage, then how can a male slave marry a free woman? The passage ends before providing the Hanafi response, inviting you to complete the analysis using usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State precisely what is being ruled upon: a master marrying his slave-girl, or a woman marrying her male slave. The hukm is that the marriage is batil (invalid) and prohibited. This applies whether the ownership is full or partial.
2
Trace the Hanafi rationale (dalil aqli)
The text gives a rational proof: marriage was legislated for shared benefits (mahr, nafaqah, sexual rights, companionship, etc.). Ownership (milk) gives the master unilateral control over the owned person. Thus, the two relationships cannot coexist because the owned person cannot be simultaneously a free spouse with mutual rights.
This is a māni' (preventer) reasoning: ownership prevents the realization of marital benefits on a shared basis.
3
Apply the rationale to both scenarios
Check the ruling for both: (1) a master and his full slave-girl; (2) a woman and her full slave. Also consider partial ownership: the prohibition applies even if the owner owns only part of the slave. The conflict arises from the very nature of ownership, not its extent.
Partial ownership means the other co-owners have a share, so the marriage still involves a conflict of interests with the co-owner.
4
Recognize the objection and identify the gap
The text raises an objection: if ownership contradicts marriage, then a male slave who marries a free woman also combines ownership (the master's rights over the slave) with the marriage relationship. The text ends here. You need to infer the Hanafi response: a slave is capable of marriage because his ownership by the master does not directly create a conflict between the spouses; the slave's wife does not own him, so the marital benefits are not negated. The master's rights over the slave are limited and do not override the marriage's essential equality between the spouses.
The full response is found in other sources: the slave's marriage is valid because the conflict is not between the spouses themselves; the master's ownership is a third-party right that does not destroy the mutual rights of the spouses.

و لا يتزوج المولى امته ولا المرأة عبدها لان النكاح ما شرع الامثمر ثمرات مشتركة بين المتناكحين والمملوكية تنافى المالكية فيمتنع وقوع الثمرة على الشركة
ترجمہ مولیٰ اپنی باندی سے نکاح نہ کرے اور نہ عورت اپنے غلام سے، اس لئے کہ نکاح مشروع نہیں ہوا مگر ایسے ثمرات کے ساتھ مشمر ہو کر جوز وجین کے درمیان مشترک ہیں اور مملوکیت مالکیت ۔ نافی ہے، پس شرکت پر ثمرہ کا حصول ممتنع ہو گا۔
تشریح مولی اپنی باندی سے نکاح نہ کرے، باندی کے کل کا مالک ہو یا بعض کا۔ اسی طرح عورت اپنے غلام سے نکاح نہ کرے، عورت پورے غلام کی مالک ہو یا بعض کی۔ دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح ممنوع ہے۔ اگر مالک اور مملوک رہتے ہوئے نکاح کیا تو باطل ہوگا ائمہ اربعہ اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح ایسے منافع اور فوائد کے پیش نظر مشروع کیا گیا جو دونوں میاں بیوی کے درمیان مشترک ہیں ، بعض منافع عورت کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں، مثلاً عورت کیلئے مہر ، کسوہ نفقہ واجب ہوگا اور مرد پر حکما ولی بھی واجب ہوگی۔ بغیر عورت کی رضامندی کے مرد کیلئے عزل جائز نہیں ، مرد کے مقطوع الذکر اور منین ہونے کی صورت میں عورت کو خیار شیخ بھی حاصل ہوگا۔ اور بعض منافع مرد کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں مثلاً نکاح کے بعد مرد کو عورت کے نفس پر قدرت کا حاصل ہونا ، اور عورت کا مرد کے مکان میں قیام کرنا، اندرونِ خانہ کام کرنا مثلا کھانا پکانا، کپڑے دھونا، بچوں کی تربیت کرنا، بچوں کو دودھ پلانا خلاصہ یہ کہ مذکورہ نکاح کی دونوں صورتوں میں ما مالکیت اور مملوکیت کا جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا، حالانکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان منافات ہے۔ کیونکہ مالکیت مقتضی ہے قاہریت کی اور مملوکیت مقتضی ہے مقہوریت کی اور ان دونوں کی تنافی میں کوئی شبہ نہیں۔ بس جب ایسا ہے تو شرکت پر ثمرہ کا حصول ممتنع ہوگا۔ اس پر ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر مملوکیت مالکیت کے منافی ہے تو پھر ملوک کا نکاح بالکل درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ جب مملوک کسی آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرے گا تو ناکج ہونے کی وجہ سے مالکیت بھی ثابت ہو گی ، لہذا اس صورت میں بھی مالکیت اور مملوکیت کا جمع ہونا لازم آیا۔
And the master does not marry his slave-girl, nor the woman her slave, because marriage was legislated only to produce fruits that are shared between the spouses, and ownership contradicts ownership, so the occurrence of the fruit on the basis of partnership is impossible. Translation: The master should not marry his slave-girl, nor the woman her slave, because marriage was legislated only with such fruits that are shared between the spouses, and ownership contradicts ownership, so the occurrence of the fruit on partnership is impossible. Explanation: The master should not marry his slave-girl, whether he owns all of her or part of her. Likewise, a woman should not marry her slave, whether she owns all of him or part of him. In both cases, marriage is prohibited. If they contract marriage while still owner and owned, it is batil (invalid). All four imams hold this view. The evidence is that marriage was legislated for mutual benefits and advantages that are shared between husband and wife. Some benefits go to the woman, such as mahr, clothing, maintenance become obligatory for her, and the man is also obliged to have intercourse with her. He cannot practice coitus interruptus without her consent. If the man has a severed penis or is impotent, the woman has the option of separation (khiyar al-shaykh). And some benefits go to the man, such as obtaining power over the woman's person after marriage, the woman residing in the man's house, doing household work like cooking, washing clothes, training children, breastfeeding. In short, in both mentioned cases of marriage, ownership and being owned would necessarily be combined, although there is a contradiction between the two. Because ownership necessitates domination, and being owned necessitates subjugation, and there is no doubt about their contradiction. So when that is the case, the occurrence of the fruit on partnership is impossible. There is an objection: if being owned contradicts ownership, then the marriage of a male slave to a free woman should also not be valid at all, because when a slave marries a free woman, due to being a slave, ownership (of the slave by his master) also exists, so in that case too, ownership and being owned would necessarily be combined.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of a master marrying his slave-girl, and a woman marrying her male slave. The ruling applies whether the ownership is full or partial. All four imams agree on this ruling. The reason (حکمت) is that marriage is designed to produce mutual benefits and rights that are shared between husband and wife, such as maintenance, inheritance, mutual sexual rights, etc. However, ownership (ملک) implies subjugation and control, which is incompatible with the equality required in marriage. When the owner marries the owned, the owner would already have rights over the owned that conflict with the marital rights. For example, the husband owes maintenance, but if he is the owner, he already has obligations? Actually the conflict is that the owned person cannot simultaneously be a spouse with rights and an owned property. The text then raises an objection: if ownership is incompatible with marriage, then how can a male slave marry a free woman? In that case, the slave's owner gains some rights over the wife? The text is cut off, so the answer is not provided in this window. The full discussion would likely explain that in the case of a slave marrying a free woman, the slave's ownership by his master does not directly conflict with the marital relationship because the marriage benefits are not shared between the master and the slave; rather, the slave is capable of having marital rights and duties despite being owned. The objection is a common point for further clarification.

Key Terms
مملوکیت (mamlūkiyyah): The state of being owned as a slave.
مالکیت (mālikiyyah): Ownership; the legal relationship of a master over a slave.
ثمرات نکاح (thamarat al-nikāḥ): The fruits or benefits of marriage, such as mahr, nafaqah, sexual rights, companionship, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Valid and permissible.
C) Batil (invalid).
D) Fasid (corrupt).

Key Takeaway
Marriage between an owner and the owned is batil because ownership subjugates, while marriage requires mutual equality between spouses.

Prohibition of Marrying a Sister during Revocable Iddah
Hanafi response to the objection that marriage is completely severed during revocable iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits marrying the sister of a woman in revocable iddah, and evaluate the opposing argument using the principle of partial continuity of nikah.

Core Idea
Marriage partially remains during revocable iddah, so marrying the wife's sister is as haram as marrying her while married.

This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and some other scholars (possibly Shafi'i) regarding the permissibility of marrying the sister of a woman during the woman's revocable iddah. The opponent argues that revocable divorce completely severs the marriage, citing the application of hadd for intercourse. The Hanafi school responds with a nuanced view: nikah continues partially, as evidenced by remaining rights like nafaqah and lineage by firash. Therefore, combining two sisters in marriage remains prohibited. This lesson will walk you through the logical structure of the Hanafi argument and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What exactly is being contested? The core question is whether a man can marry the sister of his wife while the wife is in revocable iddah.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is haram because the first nikah partially remains. List the effects that continue: nafaqah, restriction of movement, and firash for lineage.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
3
Understand the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that revocable divorce is a qati' (severance) and that if intercourse occurs during iddah, hadd applies, proving the marriage is completely ended.
This is based on the idea that hadd only applies when there is no marriage.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond with two points: (1) The qati' is deferred until the iddah ends, (2) hadd does not negate partial ownership; it only indicates that intercourse is not permissible, but other marital effects remain.
They distinguish between ownership of nikah for intercourse and for other purposes.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis forbid marrying the sister during revocable iddah; other schools may permit it. This directly affects fatwa and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاطع پایا گیا تو اس کا اثر بھی یقینا متفق ہوگا۔ نکاح کے بالکلیہ منقطع ہونے کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر شخص حرام سمجھ کر معتدہ سے وطی کر لے تو حد واجب ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ معتدہ کا نکاح باقی ہے، اس لئے کہ نکاح کے بعض احکام باقی ہیں، مثلا عدت کے زمانہ میں شوہر پر اسی طرح نفقہ واجب ہوگا جس طرح منکوحہ ہونے کی حالت میں تھا۔ اور شوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ گھر سے نکلنے پر پابندی لگا دے۔ اسی طرح اگر دو سال کے اندر اندر بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو فراش ہونے کی وجہ سے اسی شخص سے نسب بھی ثابت ہوگا۔ اور رہی یہ بات کہ قاطع نکاح پایا گیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قاطع کا عمل انقضاء عدت تک کے لئے مؤخر ہو گیا حکم نکاح کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس کا جواب کہ وطی کرنے سے حد واجب ہوتی ہے، اولاً تو ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ اس وطی پر حد واجب ہوگی ، جیسا کہ مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق میں اشارہ ملتا ہے اور اگر تسلیم بھی کر لیں تو حد واجب ہوگی جیسا کہ مبسوط کی کتاب الحدود میں صراحنا موجود ہے، تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ وطی کے حلال ہونے کے حق میں ملک نکاح زائل ہوگیا، لہذا یہ وطی زنا ہوگی اور امور مذکورہ کے حق میں ملک زائل نہیں ہوتی، پس نکاح من وجہ باقی ہے اور من وجہ غیر باقی۔ اور جب من وجہ نکاح باقی ہے تو یہ شخص اس معتدہ کی بہن سے نکاح کر کے جامع بین الأختین فی النکاح ہوگا اور نکاح میں جمع بین الأختین ناجائز ہے، اگرچہ نکاح فی الجملہ ہو۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
If a severance (qati') is found, its effect will certainly be agreed upon. Another proof for the complete termination of marriage is that if a person, thinking it forbidden, has intercourse with a woman in iddah, then hadd becomes obligatory. Our proof is that the marriage of the woman in iddah remains, because some rulings of marriage remain, for example, during the period of iddah, maintenance (nafaqah) is obligatory upon the husband just as it was when she was a wife. And the husband has the authority to restrict her from leaving the house. Similarly, if a child is born within two years, lineage is established from him due to the marital bed (firash). And as for the claim that a severance (qati') is found, the answer is that the action of the severance is deferred until the expiry of the iddah due to the remaining ruling of marriage. And as for the answer that hadd becomes obligatory from intercourse, firstly we do not accept that hadd becomes obligatory for this intercourse, as indicated in al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Talaq, and if we do accept, then hadd becomes obligatory as explicitly found in al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Hudud, then we will reply that in terms of the permissibility of intercourse, the ownership of marriage is removed, so this intercourse becomes adultery, but in terms of the mentioned matters, ownership is not removed. Thus marriage partially remains and partially does not. And when marriage partially remains, this person, by marrying the sister of this woman in iddah, becomes one who combines two sisters in marriage, and combining two sisters in marriage is impermissible, even if the marriage is partial. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a man can marry the sister of his wife during the wife's revocable iddah (iddah raj'iyyah). The opponent argues that the revocable divorce completely severs the marriage. As proof, they claim that if a man commits zina with the woman in iddah, thinking it unlawful, then hadd (the fixed punishment for zina) is applied, which would not happen if marriage still existed. The Hanafi school responds with a multi-faceted argument. First, they assert that nikah remains partially intact because several of its effects persist: nafaqah (maintenance) is still due, the husband can restrict her movement, and if she gives birth within two years of separation, the child's lineage is attributed to him (based on the principle of firash). Second, they clarify that the 'qati'' (the act that would normally sever marriage) does not take immediate effect; rather, its operation is postponed until the iddah expires. As for the hadd objection, the Hanafis present a nuanced answer: either they deny that hadd applies (citing a reference from al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Talaq), or if hadd does apply (as per another section of al-Mabsut), they explain that ownership of marriage is removed only in the specific context of permissibility of intercourse—making the act zina—but ownership remains intact for other purposes such as nafaqah and lineage. Therefore, nikah exists 'min wajh' (from one perspective) and does not exist 'min wajh' (from another). Since nikah partially exists, marrying the wife's sister while she is in iddah results in 'jama' bayn al-ukhtayn' (combining two sisters), which is categorically impermissible in Islam even if the first nikah is only partial. This ruling is mufta bihi based on the Hanafi understanding of the continuity of nikah during revocable iddah.

Key Terms
معتدہ (mu'taddah): A woman who is in the waiting period (iddah) after a revocable or irrevocable divorce or death of husband.
قاطع (qati'): An act or event that severs the marriage; here it refers to the revocable divorce itself, which normally severs but during iddah is deferred.
جمع بین الأختین (jama' bayn al-ukhtayn): The act of marrying two sisters simultaneously or during the same period; this is prohibited by Quran 4:23.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must pay mahr again
B) The wife must observe hijab only for strangers
C) The husband owes nafaqah and can restrict her movement
D) The wife can remarry immediately

Key Takeaway
During revocable iddah, nikah partially remains, so marrying the wife's sister is haram as it combines two sisters in marriage.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Master Marrying His Slave-Girl
Ruling and proof that a master cannot marry his slave-girl and a mistress cannot marry her slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a master cannot marry his slave-girl (or a mistress her slave), explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the mutual benefits of marriage, and identify that such a marriage is batil (void) and not makruh.

Core Idea
A master cannot marry his slave-girl because mutual marriage benefits are incompatible with ownership, making the contract void (batil).

In this passage, al-Marghinani presents a ruling agreed upon by all four Sunni imams: a man cannot marry his female slave, nor a woman her male slave. The ruling is not merely prohibited but renders the marriage contract void ab initio. The proof derives from the very purpose of marriage – mutual rights and obligations – which cannot be realized when one spouse fully owns the other. We will unpack this reasoning and also explore an objection concerning a slave's marriage to a free person, which is allowed despite a similar apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: a master marrying his own slave-girl, and a mistress marrying her own slave. State the hukm level: batil (void) according to all four imams.
The prohibition applies whether ownership is full or partial.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: marriage was legislated to produce mutual benefits (thamarāt mushtarakah) between spouses. Servitude (mamlūkiyyah) contradicts ownership (mālikiyyah), preventing the realization of shared benefits.
This is a ta'līl (teleological reasoning) based on the maqāṣid of marriage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
Explain how the proof yields the ruling. Because ownership gives one party dominance over the other, the required equality in mutual benefits cannot occur. Thus the marriage cannot fulfill its purpose and is invalid.
The key phrase: 'al-mamlūkiyyah tunāfī al-mālikiyyah'.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Although the main ruling is consensus (ijmā'), a potential objection arises: if ownership contradicts marriage, then a slave's marriage to a free woman should also be invalid because the free wife gains ownership rights (mahr, nafaqah) over the slave. Identify this objection.
The objector uses strict qiyas.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjīḥ
The Hanafi response: the slave's marriage is allowed by istiḥsān due to necessity (ḍarūrah) – slaves need to marry to avoid sin. Strict qiyas would have invalidated it, but necessity creates an exception. This does not contradict the original ruling.
Thus the principle 'al-ḍarūrah tubīḥ al-maḥẓūrāt' applies in a limited sense.
