مولی کیلئے اپنی باندی سے اور ملکہ کیلئے اپنے غلام سے نکاح کرنے کا حکم و لا يتزوج المولى امته ولا المرأة عبدها لان النكاح ما شرع الامثمر ثمرات مشتركة بين المتناكحين والمملوكية تنافى المالكية فيمتنع وقوع الثمرة على الشركة ترجمہ مولیٰ اپنی باندی سے نکاح نہ کرے اور نہ عورت اپنے غلام سے، اس لئے کہ نکاح مشروع نہیں ہوا مگر ایسے ثمرات کے ساتھ مثمر ہو کر دو زوجین کے درمیان مشترک ہیں اور مملوکیت مالکیت کی نافی ہے، پس شرکت پر ثمرہ کا حصول ممتنع ہو گا۔ تشریح مولی اپنی باندی سے نکاح نہ کرے، باندی کے کل کا مالک ہو یا بعض کا۔ اسی طرح عورت اپنے غلام سے نکاح نہ کرے، عورت پورے غلام کی مالک ہو یا بعض کی۔ دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح ممنوع ہے۔ اگر مالک اور مملوک رہتے ہوئے نکاح کیا تو باطل ہوگا ائمہ اربعہ اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح ایسے منافع اور فوائد کے پیش نظر مشروع کیا گیا جو دونوں میاں بیوی کے درمیان مشترک ہیں، بعض منافع عورت کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں، مثلاً عورت کیلئے مہر، کسوۃ، نفقہ واجب ہوگا اور مرد پر حکماً وطی بھی واجب ہوگی۔ بغیر عورت کی رضامندی کے مرد کیلئے عزل جائز نہیں، مرد کے مقطوع الذکر اور منین ہونے کی صورت میں عورت کو خیار شیخ بھی حاصل ہوگا۔ اور بعض منافع مرد کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں مثلاً نکاح کے بعد مرد کو عورت کے نفس پر قدرت کا حاصل ہونا، اور عورت کا مرد کے مکان میں قیام کرنا، اندرونِ خانہ کام کرنا مثلا کھانا پکانا، کپڑے دھونا، بچوں کی تربیت کرنا، بچوں کو دودھ پلانا خلاصہ یہ کہ مذکورہ نکاح کی دونوں صورتوں میں ما مالکیت اور مملوکیت کا جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا، حالانکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان منافات ہے۔ کیونکہ مالکیت مقتضی ہے قاہریت کی اور مملوکیت مقتضی ہے مقہوریت کی اور ان دونوں کی تنافی میں کوئی شبہ نہیں۔ بس جب ایسا ہے تو شرکت پر ثمرہ کا حصول ممتنع ہوگا۔ اس پر ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر مملوکیت مالکیت کے منافی ہے تو پھر مملوک کا نکاح بالکل درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ جب مملوک کسی آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرے گا تو نکاح ہونے کی وجہ سے مالکیت بھی ثابت ہو گی، لہذا اس صورت میں بھی مالکیت اور مملوکیت کا جمع ہونا لازم آیا۔ جواب: قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہی ہے کہ مملوک کا نکاح مطلقا درست نہ ہو لیکن ضرورت کی وجہ سے خلاف قیاس جائز قرار دے دیا ہے۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ)
Ruling of a master marrying his slave-girl and a mistress marrying her slave: And a master should not marry his slave-girl and a woman should not marry her slave, because marriage was legislated only to be fruitful with benefits shared between the spouses, and servitude (mamlukiyyah) contradicts ownership (malikiyyah), so the realization of benefits in partnership is prevented. Translation: A master should not marry his slave-girl, and a woman should not marry her slave, because marriage was not legislated except to be fruitful with benefits shared between the two spouses, and servitude negates ownership, so the occurrence of benefits in partnership is impossible. Commentary: A master should not marry his slave-girl, whether he owns all of her or part of her. Similarly, a woman should not marry her slave, whether she owns all of him or part of him. In both cases, marriage is prohibited. If with owner and owned status remaining they marry, it will be invalid (batil); the four imams hold this. The proof is that marriage was legislated with a view to such benefits and advantages that are shared between the husband and wife. Some benefits go to the woman: for example, for the woman, mahr, clothing, and nafaqah become obligatory, and upon the man, intercourse legally becomes obligatory. Without the woman's consent, 'azl (coitus interruptus) is not permissible for the man. In case the man is maktu' al-dhakar (penis severed) or majbub (castrated), the woman has the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh). And some benefits go to the man: for example, after marriage, the man gains power over the woman's person, and the woman resides in the man's house, does housework like cooking, washing clothes, training children, nursing children. In summary, in both mentioned cases of marriage, ownership and servitude would necessarily be combined, although there is contradiction between them, because ownership requires dominance (qahiriyyah) and servitude requires subjugation (maqhuriyyah), and there is no doubt about their incompatibility. So when this is the case, the realization of benefits in partnership is impossible. There is an objection to this: if servitude contradicts ownership, then a slave's marriage should be absolutely invalid, because when a slave marries a free woman, due to the marriage, ownership is also established (the wife owns the husband in some respects?), so here also ownership and servitude would be combined. Answer: The requirement of qiyas (analogy) is that a slave's marriage should be absolutely invalid, but due to necessity (darurah), it has been declared valid contrary to qiyas. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah)
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a master cannot marry his own slave-girl, nor can a mistress marry her own slave. The text is a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah. It begins by stating the ruling in Arabic: 'Wa la yatazawwaju al-mawla ammatahu wa la al-mar'atu 'abdaha' — the master should not marry his slave-girl, nor the woman her slave. The reason given is that the objectives (thamarāt) of marriage are mutual benefits shared between spouses, but the relationship of ownership (mālikiyyah) and servitude (mamlūkiyyah) are contradictory. Since the master/person already has full ownership rights over the slave, the shared benefits of marriage cannot be realized. The Urdu commentary expands: the prohibition applies whether the ownership is full or partial (e.g., co-owned). If such a marriage is contracted despite the prohibition, it is bāṭil (void) and not merely invalid. This is the position of all four Sunni imams — ijmā'. The proof is that marriage was legislated to facilitate mutual benefits: the wife receives mahr, maintenance (nafaqah), and clothing; the husband is obligated to have intercourse with her; she has the right to prevent 'azl; she has khiyar al-bulugh if the husband is impotent or castrated. On the other hand, the husband gains authority over her and she lives in his house, performs domestic work, etc. If the owner marries his owned slave, these benefits become one-sided or impossible because the owner already has power over the slave. The commentator then addresses an objection: if ownership is incompatible, then how can a male slave marry a free woman? In that case, the free woman becomes his wife and thus gains certain ownership rights over him (like mahr, nafaqah), so ownership and servitude would also be combined. The Hanafi answer is that, by strict qiyas (analogy), the slave's marriage would be invalid, but it is permitted due to necessity (darurah) — slaves need to marry to avoid sin, and society requires it. Thus, the slave's marriage is an exception based on istihsān.

Key Terms
مولى (mawla): A master who owns a slave; here specifically a male owner of a female slave.
أمة (ammah): A female slave owned by a master.
مملوکیت (mamlukiyyah): The state of being owned as a slave; legal servitude.
ثمرات نکاح (thamarāt al-nikāḥ): The fruits/benefits of marriage: mutual rights and obligations such as mahr, nafaqah, sexual intimacy, companionship, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a master marries his own slave-girl while still owning her?
A) The marriage is valid but makruh
B) The marriage is batil (void) and must be annulled
C) The marriage is valid if the slave-girl consents
D) The marriage is valid only if the master sets her free first

Key Takeaway
A master cannot marry his own slave (or vice versa) because the necessary mutual benefits of marriage are impossible under an ownership relationship, making the contract void.

Ruling on Marrying Kitabiyyah, Majusiyyah, and Sabians
Quranic and Hadith proofs for permissible and impermissible marriages with women of other faiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying women from the People of the Book, Zoroastrians, and Sabians, and identify the primary evidence (Quran and Hadith) for each.

Core Idea
Marriage with Kitabiyyah is permissible; with Majusiyyah it is haram; with Sabians it depends on their beliefs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on marriage with women of different faiths. The rulings are derived from explicit Quranic verses and a Prophetic hadith that distinguishes between the People of the Book and other non-Muslims. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for applying nikah law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for each category
List the three categories of women (Kitabiyyah, Majusiyyah, Sabians) and state the ruling for each as given in the text.
Free Kitabiyyah is jayiz; Majusiyyah is haram; Sabians depend on beliefs.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
Identify the Quranic verse or hadith cited as proof for each category.
Kitabiyyah: Quran 5:5; Majusiyyah: Hadith; Idolaters: Quran 2:221; Sabians: conditional.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling – which word or phrase indicates permissibility or prohibition.
For Kitabiyyah, 'uhilla lakum' indicates permission; for Majus, explicit exception 'wa la nankihu nisa'ahum'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on Sabians
The passage mentions disagreement among imams regarding Sabians due to confusion about their actual beliefs.
The Hanafi position distinguishes Sabians with a revealed book from star-worshippers.

Ruling of marriage with Kitabiyyah (People of the Book). And it is permissible to marry Kitabiyyah because of the saying of Allah Most High: 'And [lawful to you are] chaste women from those who were given the Scripture' i.e., the chaste. And there is no difference between a free Kitabiyyah and a slave Kitabiyyah, as will be explained if Allah wills. Translation: And it is permissible to marry Kitabiyyah women because of the saying of Allah Most High: '...the verse' i.e., lawful to you are chaste women from among the People of the Book, and there is no difference between a free Kitabiyyah and a slave Kitabiyyah. Commentary: Kitabiyyat is the plural of Kitabiyyah; masculine is Kitabi. A Kitabi is a person who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a (revealed) book. There is no disagreement among the four imams regarding marriage with a free Kitabiyyah; there is disagreement regarding marriage with a slave Kitabiyyah, which will be mentioned later. The proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Lawful to you are the chaste women from among the People of the Book.' The condition of chastity is mentioned habitually, not a condition for permissibility. Marriage with Majusiyyah (Zoroastrians) and Wathaniyyah (idolaters) is prohibited. Ruling of marriage with Sabians: And it is not permissible to marry Majusiyyah because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Treat them as you treat the People of the Book, except that you do not marry their women nor eat their slaughtered animals.' He said: And not the idolaters because of the saying of Allah Most High: 'do not marry polytheist women until they believe.' And it is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in a religion and acknowledge a book, because they are from the People of the Book. And if they worship the stars and have no book, then marrying them is not permissible because they are polytheists. The disagreement reported regarding them is due to confusion about their religion. So each imam responded according to what appeared correct to him. And the same applies to their slaughtered animals. Commentary: Marrying fire-worshipping women is unanimously impermissible; the proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you deal with the People of the Book...'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage rules on the permissibility of marrying women from various religious communities. The section begins with the ruling on Kitabiyyah (Jewish and Christian women). The author quotes the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5) which permits marriage with chaste women from the People of the Book. All four imams agree that a free Kitabiyyah is permissible to marry. The text notes that the condition of 'chastity' in the verse is descriptive, not a legal condition for validity—meaning that even if a Kitabiyyah is not known to be chaste, the marriage is still valid (though it may be makruh). There is no difference between a free and a slave Kitabiyyah, but disagreement exists regarding slave Kitabiyyah, which will be discussed later. Next, the passage addresses Majusiyyah (Zoroastrians/fire-worshippers). Marriage with them is explicitly forbidden based on a hadith: 'Treat them as you treat the People of the Book, except that you do not marry their women nor eat their slaughtered animals.' This hadith distinguishes between social dealings and marriage/dietary rulings. Similarly, marriage with Wathaniyyah (idolaters) is forbidden by the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:221) 'do not marry polytheist women until they believe.' Finally, the ruling on Sabians (Ṣābi'ūn) is nuanced. If they are among those who believe in a revealed religion (often identified with a prophet and a book, such as the Mandaeans or some groups considered People of the Book), then marriage is permissible. If they worship stars and have no revealed book, they are considered polytheists and marriage is impermissible. The commentators note that the disagreement among scholars regarding Sabians is due to confusion about their actual beliefs; each scholar ruled according to what he believed to be correct. This also applies to the permissibility of eating their slaughtered animals. The passage ends with a commentary stating that fire-worshippers (Majus) are universally agreed to be impermissible for marriage, citing the same hadith.

Key Terms
کتابی (kitabi): A person who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a revealed scripture (e.g., Jews, Christians).
مجوسی (majusi): Zoroastrian; fire-worshipper; considered non-Ahl al-Kitab with special treatment but not marriage or slaughtered meat.
صابی (sabi): Sabian; a follower of a religion that claims a revealed book; ruling depends on actual beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marriage with Kitabiyyah is permissible, with Majusiyyah it is haram, and with Sabians it depends on their beliefs.

Marriage of a Slave: Qiyas vs. Necessity
Brief note on slave marriage ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slave marriage and explain why it is an exception to qiyas.

Core Idea
Qiyas would bar slave marriage, but necessity permits it.

In Hanafi fiqh, the marriage of a slave is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas. This passage from a commentary on al-Hidayah encapsulates that principle, showing how necessity can transform a default ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling from qiyas
The act is the marriage of a slave (mamluk). According to qiyas, the ruling would be that such a marriage is absolutely invalid.
Qiyas here likely analogizes a slave to someone without full legal capacity.
2
Understand the exception based on necessity
The text states that despite qiyas, the marriage has been declared permissible (ja'iz) due to necessity (darurah). Identify the necessity: the need for procreation and social stability.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference).
3
Recognize the underlying principle
The passage highlights that legal rulings can be overridden by higher objectives when strict analogy would cause hardship.
This principle is widespread in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Memorize the ruling as an anchor
This passage serves as a memorization anchor: a concise statement of a key exception to qiyas.
Use it to recall the interplay between qiyas and istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب ... قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہی ہے کہ مملوک کا نکاح مطلقا درست نہ ہو لیکن ضرورت کی وجہ سے خلاف قیاس جائز قرار دے دیا ہے۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ)
The answer... The requirement of analogy (qiyas) is that the marriage of a slave is absolutely not valid, but due to necessity, it has been declared permissible contrary to analogy. (Mueeni Sharh Hidayah)
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a principle: Although qiyas would dictate that a slave's marriage is invalid, the Hanafi school has made it permissible due to necessity. This is an example of istihsan. Note that this note is from a commentary, not the main text of Hidayah. The exact ruling on slave marriage is detailed elsewhere.

Key Terms
مملوک (mamluk): A male slave owned by another person.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, departing from qiyas for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a slave's marriage due to necessity, overriding the negative analogy (qiyas) that would otherwise invalidate it.

Marriage with Kitabiyyat: Ruling and Proof from Quran
Ruling on marrying Kitabiyyat with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying Kitabiyyat and explain how Quran 5:5 provides the proof, while identifying that the mention of chastity is descriptive.

Core Idea
Marriage with Kitabiyyat is permissible by explicit Quranic text; the condition of chastity is descriptive, not a prerequisite for validity.

In this passage, the author establishes the permissibility of marrying Kitabiyyat (Jewish and Christian women) based on a clear Quranic verse. He also clarifies that the word 'al-muhsanat' (chaste) in the verse is not a condition but a habitual description. This ruling is agreed upon for free Kitabiyyat, with a later discussion on slave Kitabiyyat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marriage with a Kitabiyyah (a woman from the People of the Book). The ruling is permissibility (jaiz).
The text begins with 'ويجوز تزوج الكتابيات' — it is permissible to marry Kitabiyyat.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 5:5, specifically the phrase 'wal-muhsanatu minalladheena ootoo al-kitaba' (the chaste women from those who were given the Book).
The author quotes the relevant part of the verse.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase explicitly permits marriage with chaste Kitabiyyat. The imperative 'ahilla' (made lawful) indicates permissibility. The Hanafi school takes this as a definitive proof (qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah).
The verse does not qualify the permission with any additional conditions beyond the woman being from the People of the Book.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is consensus among the four Imams on the permissibility of marrying a free Kitabiyyah. However, there is disagreement on marrying a slave Kitabiyyah, which the author promises to address later.
The passage highlights that the disagreement is only on slave women, not on free ones.
5
Evaluate the significance of 'chastity'
The author emphasizes that the mention of 'al-muhsanat' (chaste) is descriptive (waqf al-'adat) and not a condition for validity. The marriage is still valid even if the woman is not known to be chaste.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding: chastity is not a prerequisite.

And it is permissible to marry the Kitabiyyat due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Book before you' (Quran 5:5) i.e., the chaste ones. Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on marrying women of the Book (Jews and Christians). The Hanafi school permits it based on Quran 5:5. The definition of 'Kitabi' is given as one who believes in a prophet and a revealed book. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
کتابیہ (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (Jew or Christian) who believes in a prophet and a revealed book.
محصنات (muhsanat): Chaste women, but here mentioned as a description not a condition.

Prohibition of Marrying Magian and Idolatress Women
Ruling prohibiting marriage to Magian and idolatress women with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of marriage to Magian and idolatress women, cite the proofs, and explain the scope of the hadith exception.

Core Idea
Magians are treated like People of the Book except for marriage and slaughter—both are prohibited.

Marriage in Islam is a sacred bond, but not all unions are permissible. This ruling addresses two categories of women: Magians (Zoroastrians) and idolatresses. Understanding the precise proofs is crucial for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited categories
The text names 'Majusiyyat' (Magian women) and 'Wathaniyyat' (idolatress women). State each clearly.
Magians are fire-worshippers; idolatresses are polytheists.
2
Examine the proof for Magians
The hadith commands treating Magians like People of the Book, but excepts marriage and eating their slaughtered meat. This exception indicates prohibition.
The hadith is reported through multiple chains.
3
Examine the proof for idolatresses
Quran 2:221 directly forbids marriage to polytheistic women until they believe. This is a clear and explicit prohibition.
The verse uses the imperative 'la tankihu'.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school considers this prohibition unanimous and established by qat'i dalala (clear meaning).
No disagreement among the Sahibayn.

And it is not permissible to marry Majusiyyat (Magian women) because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Treat them like the People of the Book, except for marrying their women and eating their slaughtered meat.' He said: And neither idolatress women, because of the saying of Allah Most High: 'And do not marry the polytheistic women until they believe.' And it is not permissible to marry idolatress women due to the verse 'Wa la tankihul mushrikati' (do not marry polytheistic women). The proof is the hadith: deal with Magians as with the People of the Book, except for marrying their women and eating their slaughtered meat. The conclusion: do not marry Magian women and do not eat their slaughtered meat; besides that, treat them like the People of the Book in giving aman and taking jizya. This hadith is narrated through multiple chains. And also marriage to idolatress women is impermissible, the proof is the Quranic verse that do not marry polytheistic women.

Commentary
This passage prohibits marriage to Magian (Zoroastrian) and idolatress (polytheistic) women. For Magians, the proof is a hadith commanding to treat them like the People of the Book except in two matters: marrying their women and eating their slaughtered meat. This is a clear prohibition. For idolatress women, the proof is Quran 2:221 which explicitly prohibits marrying polytheistic women until they believe. The commentary notes that this prohibition is unanimous regarding fire-worshippers.

وثنیہ (wathaniyyah): An idolatress woman, worshipper of idols.

Marriage with Sabian Women: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute over Definition
Intra-Hanafi dispute based on definition of Sabian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn held different rulings on marrying Sabian women and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The ruling on marrying Sabian women depends entirely on how 'Sabian' is defined.

This lesson examines a famous intra-Hanafi dispute about marriage to Sabian women. The difference does not stem from a disagreement on the general principle of marrying People of the Book, but from a different understanding of who qualifies as a Sabian. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how definitions affect rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the act under dispute: marriage to Sabian women. The ruling varies by definition.
2
State each position
Imam Abu Hanifa: permissible. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): not permissible.
Both are Hanafi positions, so this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the definitional basis
Abu Hanifa defines a Sabian as one who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a heavenly book. Sahibayn define a Sabian as a star-worshipper with no book.
4
Connect definition to ruling
Abu Hanifa's definition makes Sabians Ahl al-Kitab, so marriage permissible. Sahibayn's definition makes them polytheists, so marriage impermissible.
The ruling follows from categorization.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Sabian woman's beliefs are unclear, the qadi must ascertain them. Many later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view for caution.

Source Text

ويجوز تزوج الصابيات ان كانوا يؤمنون بدين ويقرون بكتاب لانهم من اهل الكتاب وان كانوا يعبدون الكواكب ولا كتاب لهم لم تجز مناكحتهم لانهم مشركون والخلاف المنقول فيه محمول على اشتباه مذهبهم فكل اجاب على ما وقع عندهم وعلى هذا حال ذبيحتهم
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے صابیہ عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا، اگر وہ کسی دین پر ایمان رکھتی ہوں اور کتاب کا اقرار کرتی ہوں ،اس لئے کہ وہ اہل کتاب میں سے ہیں ۔اور اگر ستاروں کو پوجتی ہیں اور ان کے پاس کوئی آسمانی کتاب بھی نہیں تو ان کو نکاح میں لینا جائز نہیں کیونکہ وہ مشرک ہیں اور اختلاف جو اس بارے میں منقول ہے ان کے مذہب کے مشتبہ ہونے پر محمول ہے۔ پس ہر ایک امام نے اس کے مطابق جواب دیا جو اس کے نزدیک حق معلوم ہوا اور اسی اختلاف پر ان کے ذبیحہ کا حال ہے۔
صابیہ عورتوں سے نکاح کے جواز و عدم جواز میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ جواز کے قائل ہیں اور صاحبین عدم جواز کے۔ درحقیقت یہ اختلاف صابی کی تعریف و تفسیر میں ہے۔ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ صابی وہ ہے جو انبیاء میں سے کسی نبی پر ایمان رکھتا ہو اور کسی آسمانی کتاب کا اقرار کرتا ہو۔ پس اس وقت صابی اہل کتاب میں سے ہوگا، اور اہل کتاب کی عورتوں سے نکاح جائز ہے لہذا صابیہ سے بھی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ صابی ستاروں کی پرستش کرتا ہے اور کسی آسمانی کتاب کا اقرار نہیں کرتا۔ پس یہ بت پرستوں کے حکم میں ہوگا ، جس طرح بت پرست سے نکاح جائز نہیں اسی طرح صابیہ عورت سے بھی نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
And it is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in a religion and acknowledge a book, because they are from the People of the Book. And if they worship the stars and have no book, then marriage to them is not permissible because they are polytheists. And the disagreement narrated about this is based on the confusion about their school. So each Imam answered according to what was established with him. And the same disagreement applies to their slaughtered meat. Explanation: There is disagreement regarding the permissibility of marrying Sabian women. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it permissible, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it impermissible. In reality, this disagreement is about the definition and interpretation of 'Sabian'. Imam Abu Hanifa says: A Sabian is one who believes in a prophet among the prophets and acknowledges a heavenly book. Then he is from the People of the Book, and marriage to the women of the People of the Book is permissible, so marriage to Sabian women is permissible. The Sahibayn say: A Sabian worships the stars and does not acknowledge any heavenly book. So he is in the ruling of idolaters; just as marriage to an idolater is not permissible, so marriage to a Sabian woman is not permissible.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding marriage to Sabian women. The text first states the general ruling: it depends on whether they are considered People of the Book or polytheists. Then it explains the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa defines a Sabian as one who believes in a prophet and a book, hence they are People of the Book and marriage is permissible. The Sahibayn define a Sabian as a star-worshipper with no book, hence they are polytheists and marriage is impermissible. This is a classic example of how differing definitions of a term lead to different rulings. The mufta bihi position is not stated here, but often the Sahibayn's view is preferred in later Hanafi fatwa due to caution.

Key Terms
صابیہ (sabiyyah): A Sabian woman; the definition is disputed among the imams.
ذبیحہ (dhabihah): The meat of an animal slaughtered by a Sabian; the same dispute applies to its permissibility.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi disputes often arise from differing definitions; the thamarah al-khilaf here is that the same factual situation can yield opposite rulings depending on the definition used.

Marriage While in Ihram: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of marriage during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marriage in ihram, identify the Shafi'i objection, and explain the Hanafi response using the hadith of Maymunah and the reinterpretation of the prohibition hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while muhrim proves the contract is valid; the prohibition hadith refers to intercourse, not the contract.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether a marriage contract is valid while one or both parties are in the state of ihram. The Hanafi school permits it, citing the Prophet's own action, while the Shafi'i school (and others) prohibit it based on a specific hadith. You will learn how the Hanafis reconcile the evidence and the practical implications for Muslims performing Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: marriage contract is valid (ja'iz) for both muhrim and muhrimah, and for a muhrim acting as guardian.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik, Ahmad) hold it is invalid based on the hadith: 'La yankihu al-muhrimu wa la yunkahu' (The muhrim should not marry nor give in marriage).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret the hadith as referring to sexual intercourse (wat'), not the contract itself, using the linguistic ambiguity of 'yankihu'.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is the authentic narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was muhrim – an actual action that takes precedence over a possible interpretation.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi fiqh the contract is valid but consummation must be delayed until after exiting ihram; in Shafi'i the contract itself is invalid and must be renewed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز للمحرم والمحرمة ان يتزوجا فى حالة الاحرام وقال الشافعى لا يجوز وتزويج الولى المحرم وليته على هذا الخلاف له قوله عليه السلام لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح ولنا ماروى انه عليه السلام تزوج بميمونة و هو محرم و ما رواه محمول على الوطى
ترجمہ اور محرم اور حرمہ کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ دونوں نکاح کریں حالت احرام میں اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ حالت احرام میں نکاح جائز نہیں۔ اور ولی محرم کا اپنی مولیہ کا نکاح کرانا اسی اختلاف پر ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل قول رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے نہ نکاح کرے محرم اور نہ نکاح کرائے (اپنے غیر کا)۔ ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے کہ روایت کیا گیا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نکاح کیا (حضرت) میمونہ سے حالانکہ آپ محرم تھے ۔ اور وہ حدیث جس کو روایت کیا امام شافعی نے محمول ہے وطی پر ۔
تشریح احرام والی عورت ہو یا مرد، حالت احرام میں نکاح کرنا جائز ہے ہمارے نزدیک۔ امام شافعی نا جائز کہتے ہیں۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں ۔ اسی طرح محرم کسی کا ولی بن کر نکاح کرائے تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے، امام شافعی کے نزدیک ناجائز۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان "لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح" اسی حدیث میں پہلا يَنكِحُ بفتح الياء ہے (ضرب سے ) اور دوسرا بضم الیاء ہے انکاح سے۔ اول کے معنی نکاح کرنا دوسرے کے معنی نکاح کرانا دوسرے کا ۔ جیسے طعم کھانا کھانا اور اطعام کھانا کھلانا۔ تو اب حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ محرم نہ اپنا نکاح کرے اور نہ ولی بن کر دوسرے کا نکاح کرائے۔ مسلم اور ابوداؤد کی روایت میں "ولا يخطب" کا اضافہ ہے، یعنی حالت احرام میں منگنی بھی نہ کرے۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ حالت احرام میں نکاح کرنا اور نکاح کرانا دونوں ممنوع ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ابن عباس نے روایت کیا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے محرم ہونے کی حالت میں نکاح کیا اور امام بخاری نے اضافہ کیا ہے وبنى بها و هو حلال و ماتت بسرف، یعنی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا حالانکہ
He said: And it is permissible for a male and female muhrim (one in ihram) to marry each other in the state of ihram. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible. And the marriage conducted by a muhrim guardian of his ward is likewise subject to this difference. His (al-Shafi'i's) proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The muhrim should not marry nor be married (as a guardian).' Our proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was muhrim, and that narration (of al-Shafi'i) is interpreted as referring to sexual intercourse. Explanation: In our view, marriage in ihram is permissible for both men and women. Imam al-Shafi'i deems it impermissible, and Malik and Ahmad agree with him. Similarly, if a muhrim acts as a guardian in marriage, it is permissible in our view, impermissible in Shafi'i's view. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith 'la yankihu al-muhrimu wa la yunkahu': the first 'yankihu' with fatha on ya means to marry, the second with damma on ya means to give in marriage. So the hadith means the muhrim should not marry nor give someone in marriage. In Muslim and Abu Dawud, there is an addition 'wa la yakhtubu' (nor propose). This hadith proves that marriage and giving in marriage are prohibited in ihram. Our proof is that Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was muhrim, and al-Bukhari added: 'and he consummated the marriage when he became halal, and she died at Saraf.'
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding marriage while in the state of ihram. The Hanafi school permits it, based on the authentic incident of the Prophet (peace be upon him) marrying Maymunah while he was muhrim. The Shafi'i school (and others) prohibit it based on the hadith 'la yankihu al-muhrimu wa la yunkahu'. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition in that hadith refers to sexual intercourse (wat'), not the marriage contract itself. The Urdu commentary explains the linguistic difference in the verb forms. The passage also clarifies that the same ruling applies to a muhrim acting as a guardian. The Hanafi position is that the contract is valid, though consummation is prohibited until after ihram.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
وطی (wat'): Sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) the marriage contract
B) sexual intercourse
C) betrothal
D) divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage in ihram, interpreting the prohibition hadith as referring to intercourse, and relying on the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah as stronger evidence.

Marriage to Sabian Women: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Sabian women's marriageability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on marrying Sabian women, identify the definitional dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sabian women's marriageability depends on definition: Abu Hanifa sees them as Ahl al-Kitab; Sahibayn as polytheists.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute on marrying Sabian women. The ruling hinges entirely on the definition of a Sabian: does he belong to the People of the Book or is he a star worshipper akin to polytheists? This lesson unpacks the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and clarifies the practical consequence of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding marriage to Sabian women.
Abu Hanifa: permissible; Sahibayn: impermissible.
2
Pinpoint the definitional root
Recognize that the dispute is not about a different ruling on the same category, but about the very definition of 'Sabian' – is he a kitabi or a polytheist?
Abu Hanifa defines Sabian as believing in a prophet and a heavenly book; Sahibayn define as star worshipper without a book.
3
Trace the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Explain how Abu Hanifa's definition leads to permissibility: if Sabian is Ahl al-Kitab, then Quranic permission (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5) to marry kitabi women applies.
Quranic permission for kitabi women is the basis.
4
Trace the reasoning of the Sahibayn
Explain how the Sahibayn's definition leads to prohibition: if Sabian is a polytheist, then Quranic prohibition (Surah al-Baqarah 2:221) applies.
Quranic prohibition of marrying polytheist women is the basis.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference: a marriage to a Sabian woman is valid according to Abu Hanifa, invalid according to Sahibayn. Note that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, though this passage does not explicitly state it.
The difference is purely definitional; the legal consequence is opposite rulings.

کتاب النكاح ہو مجوس کے ساتھ وہی معاملہ کر وسوائے اس کے کہ مجوس کی عورتوں سے نکاح کرو اور ان کا ذبیحہ کھاؤ۔ حاصل یہ کہ مجوس کی عورتوں سے نکاح نہ کرو اور ان کے ذبیحہ کو نہ کھاؤ، اس کے علاوہ امان دینے اور جزیہ لینے میں اہل کتاب کا سا معاملہ کرو۔ یہ حدیث شریف مختلف طرق سے مروی ہے۔ اور بت پرست عورتوں سے بھی نکاح کرنا نا جائز ہے، دلیل قرآن کی آیت ہے کہ شرک کرنے والی عورتوں سے نکاح مت کرو۔ صابیہ عورتوں سے نکاح کے جواز و عدم جواز میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ جواز کے قائل ہیں اور صاحبین عدم جواز کے۔ درحقیقت یہ اختلاف صابی کی تعریف و تفسیر میں ہے۔ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ صابی وہ ہے جو انبیاء میں سے کسی نبی پر ایمان رکھتا ہو اور کسی آسمانی کتاب کا اقرار کرتا ہو۔ پس اس وقت صابی اہل کتاب میں سے ہوگا، اور اہل کتاب کی عورتوں سے نکاح جائز ہے لہذا صابیہ سے بھی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ صابی ستاروں کی پرستش کرتا ہے اور کسی آسمانی کتاب کا اقرار نہیں کرتا۔ پس یہ بت پرستوں کے حکم میں ہوگا ، جس طرح بت پرست سے نکاح جائز نہیں اسی طرح صابیہ عورت سے بھی نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
And the dealing with the Majus is like that except that you do not marry their women and do not eat their slaughtered meat. The summary is: do not marry the women of the Majus and do not eat their slaughtered meat, besides that, in granting aman and taking jizya, deal with them as with the People of the Book. This noble hadith is narrated through multiple chains. And marrying idolatrous women is also impermissible, the evidence is the verse of the Quran: 'Do not marry polytheistic women.' Regarding marrying Sabian women, there is a difference of opinion on permissibility. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible, while the Sahibayn hold it is impermissible. In reality, this difference is due to the definition and interpretation of Sabian. Imam Abu Hanifa says the Sabian is one who believes in some prophet from the prophets and acknowledges a heavenly book. Then, at that time, the Sabian would be from the People of the Book, and marrying the women of the People of the Book is permissible, so marrying a Sabian woman would also be permissible. The Sahibayn say that the Sabian worships stars and does not acknowledge any heavenly book. So, he would be in the ruling of idol worshippers, just as marrying an idolatress is not permissible, likewise marrying a Sabian woman is not permissible.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of marrying women from the Majus (Zoroastrians) and Sabians. The author begins by stating the ruling regarding Majus: they are treated like the People of the Book in matters of aman and jizya, but their women are not to be married and their slaughtered meat is not to be eaten. This is based on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Then, for polytheist women, the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah: 221) is cited as prohibition. The main discussion is on Sabian women, where there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Imam Abu Hanifa considers Sabians to be a type of Ahl al-Kitab because they believe in some prophets and acknowledge a divine book. Therefore, marriage to their women is permissible. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) define Sabians as star worshippers without any heavenly book, placing them in the category of polytheists, thus prohibiting marriage. The difference stems from the definition of 'Sabian'. The Hanafi position according to Imam Abu Hanifa allows it, but the Sahibayn's view is more restrictive. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is typically that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it is more expansive and based on a broader definition.

Key Terms
صابی (Ṣābi’): A person who according to Abu Hanifa believes in some prophet and acknowledges a heavenly book; according to Sahibayn, a star worshipper without a book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is marriage to a Sabian woman not permissible?
A) Because Sabians are considered Ahl al-Kitab.
B) Because Sabians worship stars and do not acknowledge any heavenly book.
C) Because Sabians are idol worshippers.
D) Because Sabians deny all prophets.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on marrying Sabian women is not uniform in the Hanafi school; it depends entirely on the definition of a Sabian.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage of a Muhrim: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on marriage during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marriage in ihram, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and explain the Hanafi response using the interpretation of 'nikah' and the hierarchy of evidence.

Core Idea
Marriage in ihram is valid for Hanafis; the Shafi'i prohibition is interpreted as referring to intercourse, not the contract.

This passage examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a person in the state of ihram can validly contract a marriage. The Hanafi school, following the action of the Prophet in marrying Maymunah while in ihram, permits it. The Shafi'i school, along with Malik and Ahmad, prohibits it based on a prophetic command. Understanding this dispute requires analyzing the evidence and the interpretive methods each school employs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its basis
State the ruling: marriage in ihram is permissible and valid. The primary evidence is the prophetic action (fi'li hadith) of the Prophet marrying Maymunah while he was a muhrim.
This is a direct sunnah action.
2
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
The Shafi'i school (and Malik and Ahmad) hold it is impermissible. Their evidence is the prophetic command: 'The muhrim should not marry nor should he give in marriage' (qawli hadith).
This is a verbal prohibition.
3
Analyze the Hanafi responses to the Shafi'i hadith
Two interpretations: (a) the word 'nikah' in the prohibition means sexual intercourse, not the marriage contract, so the prohibition applies to intercourse; (b) the prohibition is tanzihi (disliked) rather than tahrimi (unlawful), so the marriage is still valid.
Both responses preserve the validity of the contract.
4
Examine the qiyas argument
The Hanafis also use analogy: marriage is like other contracts (e.g., sale), and other contracts are permissible in ihram, so marriage should be permissible.
This strengthens the Hanafi position with rational consistency.
5
Evaluate the tarjih mentioned in the text
The text notes that the Shafi'i view is considered stronger by some because a verbal hadith (qawli) takes precedence over an action hadith (fi'li) when they conflict. However, the Hanafi position remains the relied-upon (mufta bihi) within the Hanafi school.
Even with a potential weakness in evidence, the school's stance is maintained due to supporting factors.

هو محرم و ما رواه محمول على الوطى ترجمہ اور محرم اور حرمہ کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ دونوں نکاح کریں حالت احرام میں اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ حالت احرام میں نکاح جائز نہیں۔ اور ولی محرم کا اپنی مولیہ کا فرمان " لا يـنـكـح الـمـحـرم و لا ينكح " اسی حدیث میں پہلا يَنكِحُ بفتح الياء ہے (ضرب سے ) اور دوسرا بضم الیاء ہے انکاح سے۔ اول کے معنی نکاح کرنا دوسرے کے معنی نکاح کرانا دوسرے کا ۔ جیسے طعم کھانا کھانا اور اطعام کھانا کھلانا۔ تو اب حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ محرم نہ اپنا نکاح کرے اور نہ ولی بن کر دوسرے کا نکاح کرائے۔ مسلم اور ابوداؤد کی روایت میں ولا یہ خطب کا اضافہ ہے، یعنی حالت احرام میں منگنی بھی نہ کرے۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ حالت احرام میں نکاح کرنا اور نکاح کرانا دونوں ممنوع ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ابن عباس نے روایت کیا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے محرم ہونے کی حالت میں نکاح کیا اور امام بخاری نے اضافہ کیا ہے وبنى بها و هو حلال و ماتت بسرف، یعنی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا حالانکہ آپ محرم تھے اور ان کے ساتھ زفاف کیا حالانکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم حلال تھے ، اور حضرت میمونہ کا انتقال مقام سرف میں ہوا ۔ بعض حضرات نے لطیفہ کے طور پر بیان کیا ہے کہ حضرت میمونہ کی شادی بھی مقام سرف میں ہوئی ، شب زفاف بھی مقام سرف ہی میں گزاری اور حضرت میمونہ کا انتقال بھی مقام سرف میں ہوا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے بحالت احترام نکاح کیا۔ امام شافعی کے روایت کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں نکاح کے لغوی معنی ( وطی ) مراد ہے۔ اب حدیث کا ترجمہ ہوگا کہ محرم نہ وطی کرے اور نہ محرمہ کو ولی پر قدرت دے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں نہی تنزیہی مراد ہے تحریمی نہیں ۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ احرام کی حالت میں نکاح کرنا اور نکاح کمرانا مناسب نہیں اگر کر لیا تو منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید قیاس سے بھی ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ نکاح دوسرے عقود بیع و شراء وغیرہ کے مانند ہے۔ جس طرح بیج وغیرہ میں ایجاب و قبول ہوتا ہے اسی طرح نکاح میں بھی ایجاب و قبول کا تلفظ ہوتا ہے، بس حالت احرام میں جس طرح دوسرے عقود جائز ہیں، اسی طرح نکاح بھی جائز ہوگا۔ انصاف کی بات یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام شافعی کا مذہب قوی ہے۔ کیونکہ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث قولی اور احناف کی پیش کردہ فعلی ، اور تعارض حدیثین کے وقت حدیث قولی مقدم ہوتی ہے حدیث فعلی پر۔ اس کے علاوہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حضرت میمونہ سے احرام کی حالت میں نکاح کرنا مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ خود حضرت میمونہ بنت الحارث فرماتی ہیں کہ " مجھ سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نکاح کیا اور ہم دونوں حلال تھے مسلم، ابوداؤد، ترمذی، ابن ماجہ نے اس حدیث کو روایت کیا ہے۔
He said: It is permissible for the muhrim and the muhrima to marry each other in the state of ihram. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible. And the marriage of a muhrim guardian of his ward is subject to the same difference. His evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The muhrim should not marry nor should he give in marriage.' Our evidence is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was a muhrim, and what he narrated is interpreted as referring to sexual intercourse. Translation: And it is permissible for the muhrim and the muhrima to marry in the state of ihram, and Imam al-Shafi'i said that marriage in the state of ihram is not permissible. And the marriage of a muhrim guardian of his ward is subject to the same difference. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'The muhrim should not marry nor should he give in marriage (on behalf of others).' Our evidence is the hadith narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was a muhrim. And the hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i is interpreted as referring to sexual intercourse. Explanation: Whether the muhrim is a man or woman, marriage in the state of ihram is permissible according to us. Imam al-Shafi'i declares it impermissible. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Similarly, a muhrim acting as a guardian to give a woman in marriage is permissible according to us, and impermissible according to al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the prophetic command: 'The muhrim should not marry nor should he give in marriage.' In this hadith, the first verb is 'yanikihu' (with fatha on ya) from the root 'nakaha' meaning to marry, and the second is 'yunikihu' (with damma on ya) from 'ankaha' meaning to give in marriage. So the meaning is: the muhrim should neither marry himself nor give another in marriage as a guardian. In the narration of Muslim and Abu Dawud, there is an addition 'nor should he propose', meaning he should not even get engaged in the state of ihram. This hadith proves that both marrying and giving in marriage are prohibited in ihram. Our evidence is that Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah (may Allah be pleased with her) while in the state of ihram, and al-Bukhari added: 'and he consummated the marriage with her while he was halal (out of ihram), and she died at Sarif.' That is, the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was a muhrim and consummated the marriage while halal, and she died at Sarif. Some have whimsically noted that Maymunah's marriage, wedding night, and death all occurred at Sarif. This hadith shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Maymunah in the state of ihram. The response to the hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i is that the word 'nikah' in that hadith is used in its literal meaning of sexual intercourse. So the meaning becomes: the muhrim should not have sexual intercourse nor should he give the muhrima authority over the guardian. A second response is that the prohibition in the hadith is tanzihi (disliked) not tahrimi (unlawful). So the meaning is that marrying and giving in marriage in ihram is not appropriate, but if done, the marriage is valid. Our school is also supported by qiyas (analogy) because marriage is like other contracts such as sale and purchase. Just as offer and acceptance are spoken in sale, similarly in marriage, offer and acceptance are spoken. So just as other contracts are permissible in ihram, marriage will also be permissible. But the fair thing is that Imam al-Shafi'i's school is stronger because his evidence is a verbal hadith (qawli) while the Hanafi evidence is a verbal action (fi'li), and when there is a conflict between hadiths, the verbal hadith takes precedence over the action hadith. Additionally, the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah in ihram is disputed. Indeed, Maymunah bint al-Harith herself said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married me while we were both halal.' Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah narrated this hadith.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school regarding the permissibility of marriage for a person in the state of ihram (muhrim). The Hanafi position, supported by Abu Hanifa, is that marriage in ihram is valid and permissible, based on the prophetic action of the Prophet marrying Maymunah while he was a muhrim. The Shafi'i school, along with Malik and Ahmad, prohibits it, citing the prophetic hadith: 'The muhrim should not marry nor should he give in marriage.' The Hanafi response interprets the word 'nikah' in the prohibition hadith as meaning sexual intercourse (wat'), thus the prohibition applies to intercourse, not marriage itself. Alternatively, they argue that the prohibition is only tanzihi (disliked), not tahrimi (unlawful), so if a marriage is performed, it is valid. The Hanafis also use qiyas, comparing marriage to other contracts like sale, which are permissible during ihram. The text notes that while the Hanafi position has support, some consider the Shafi'i position stronger because a verbal hadith takes precedence over an action hadith when they conflict. Additionally, there is a narration from Maymunah herself that she and the Prophet were both halal at the time of marriage, creating further ikhtilaf. This dispute has practical implications: according to Hanafis, a muhrim can validly marry, while according to Shafi'is, such a marriage would be invalid.

Key Terms
محرم (Muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ritual consecration (ihram) for Hajj or Umrah.
نكاح (Nikāḥ): In this passage, it is used both for marriage contract and for sexual intercourse; the Hanafis argue it means intercourse in the Shafi'i hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith is weak.
B) The word 'nikah' in the hadith means sexual intercourse, not the marriage contract.
C) The hadith is abrogated.
D) The hadith applies only to women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage during ihram, interpreting the contradictory hadith as referring to intercourse, while the Shafi'i school prohibits it based on the verbal command; this ikhtilaf illustrates the role of linguistic interpretation and evidence hierarchy in fiqh.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage of a Free Man to a Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i/Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on free man marrying a Kitabiyya slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a free man to marry a Kitabiyya slave woman and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding necessity.

Core Idea
Hanafi: marriage to a slave woman is absolutely permissible; Shafi'i: only Muslim slave women, and only when necessary.

In this passage, we encounter a classic inter-madhhab disagreement over the permissibility of a free man marrying a Kitabiyya (Jewish or Christian) slave woman. The Hanafi school holds that such a marriage is absolutely permissible, while the Shafi'i school (along with the Maliki school) restricts it to Muslim slave women and only under necessity. The dispute hinges on whether the underlying cause (muqtada) is general or restricted by necessity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school deems it absolutely permissible for a free man to marry any slave woman, Muslim or Kitabiyya.
The permissibility is mutlaq (unrestricted).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Shafi'i (and Maliki) require darurah (necessity) for marrying a slave woman, and this necessity is fulfilled by Muslim slave women, not Kitabiyya.
They argue that marrying a Kitabiyya slave woman exposes offspring to slavery unnecessarily.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the cause (muqtada) is general; marrying a slave woman is refraining from obtaining free offspring, not enslaving them. One may choose not to have free offspring just as one may choose not to have children.
The illa is the desire for offspring, not necessarily free offspring.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the marriage is valid and produces legal effects; under Shafi'i law, it is invalid.
This affects the status of the marriage contract and the children.

ويجوز تزوج الامة مسلمة كانت أو كتابية وقال الشافعى لايجوز للحران يتزوج بامة كتابية لان جواز نکاح الاماء ضرورى عنده لمافيه من تعريض الجزء على الرق وقد اندفعت الضرورة بالمسلمة ولهذا جعل طول الحرة مانعامنه وعندنا الجواز مطلق لاطلاق المتقضى وفيه امتناع عن تحصيل الجزء الحرلا ارقاقه وله ان لا يحصل الاصل فيكون له ان لا يحصل الوصف ترجمہ اور جائز ہے باندی سے نکاح کرنا مسلمان ہو باندی یا کتابیہ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ آزاد کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ کتابیہ باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کرے۔ اس لئے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک باندیوں سے نکاح کا جواز ضرورۃ ثابت ہے۔ کیونکہ باندی سے نکاح کرنے میں اپنے جز کو رقیت پر پیش کرنا ہے اور ضرورت پوری ہو گئی مسلمان باندی ہے ۔ اسی وجہ سے قدرت علی الحرہ کو نکاح امتہ سے مانع بتایا گیا ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک جواز مطلق ہے مقتضی کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور باندی سے نکاح میں آزاد جز کو حاصل کرنے سے رکنا ہے نہ کہ اسکور قیق بنانا اور اس کیلئے اجازت ہے کہ وہ اصل کو حاصل نہ کرے لہذا اسکو اس کی بھی اجازت ہوگی کہ وہ وصف کو حاصل نہ کرے۔ تشریح باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کے جواز و عدم جواز میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ ہمارے نزدیک مطلق باندی سے نکاح جائز ہے مسلمان ہو یا کتابیہ۔ امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ کتابیہ باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں۔ امام مالک بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام
And it is permissible to marry a slave woman, whether she is Muslim or Kitabiyya. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for a free man to marry a Kitabiyya slave woman, because according to him the permissibility of marrying slave women is established by necessity. Because in marrying a slave woman, there is subjecting one's part (offspring) to slavery, and the necessity is fulfilled by the Muslim slave woman. For this reason, the ability to marry a free woman is made an impediment to marrying a slave woman. According to us, the permissibility is absolute due to the absolute nature of the cause (muqtada). And in marrying a slave woman, there is refraining from obtaining a free part, not enslaving it. And he has the permission not to obtain the origin (asl), so he also has the permission not to obtain the attribute (wasf). Translation: And it is permissible to marry a slave woman, whether she is Muslim or Kitabiyya. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for a free man to marry a Kitabiyya slave woman, because according to Imam al-Shafi'i the permissibility of marrying slave women is proven by necessity. Since in marrying a slave woman, there is subjecting one's part to slavery, and the necessity is fulfilled by the Muslim slave woman. For this reason, the ability to marry a free woman is made an impediment to marrying a slave woman. And according to us, the permissibility is absolute due to the absolute nature of the cause. And in marrying a slave woman, there is refraining from obtaining a free part, not enslaving it. And he has the permission not to obtain the origin, so he also has the permission not to obtain the attribute. Explanation: There is a difference of opinion on the permissibility of marrying a slave woman. According to us, it is absolutely permissible to marry any slave woman, whether Muslim or Kitabiyya. Imam al-Shafi'i's view is that marrying a Kitabiyya slave woman is not permissible. Imam Malik also holds this view. And in one narration, Imam...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of a free man marrying a slave woman (amah). The Hanafi position is that it is absolutely permissible, whether the slave woman is Muslim or Kitabiyya (from the People of the Book). The Shafi'i position, also held by Malik, is that while a free man may marry a Muslim slave woman if necessary (due to inability to afford a free woman), he may not marry a Kitabiyya slave woman. The reasoning is Shafi'i's argument: the permissibility of marrying a slave woman is based on necessity (darurah) because it exposes one's offspring to slavery (since the child follows the mother's status), and the necessity is already fulfilled by the availability of Muslim slave women. The Hanafi counter-argument is that the permissibility is absolute (mujaz mutlaq) because the underlying principle (muqtada) is general. Marrying a slave woman is not seeking to enslave one's offspring; rather, it is a choice to not obtain a free offspring. Just as a free man may choose not to have children at all (by abstaining from marriage), he may also choose to have children through a slave woman. The text notes that the Hanafi view is that the cause (illa) is simply the desire for offspring, not necessarily free offspring. This dispute has practical implications: according to Hanafis, a free man can validly marry a Kitabiyya slave woman; according to Shafi'is, such a marriage is invalid.

Key Terms
امة كتابية (Amah Kitābiyya): A slave woman who is Jewish or Christian (from the People of the Book).
ضرورة (Ḍarūrah): Necessity; according to Shafi'i, the permissibility to marry a slave woman is restricted to cases of necessity (e.g., inability to afford a free woman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible for a free man to marry a Kitabiyya slave woman?
A) Because Kitabiyya slave women are like free Kitabiyya women.
B) Because the permissibility is absolute and not restricted by necessity.
C) Because all slave women are considered free for marriage.
D) Because the Prophet married a Kitabiyya slave woman.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds absolute permissibility for a free man to marry any slave woman, Muslim or Kitabiyya, without necessity, because the cause of marriage is general.

Marriage in Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on marriage in ihram and evaluate the Shafi'i objection using hadith reconciliation and qiyas.

Core Idea
Marriage in ihram is valid but disliked, as supported by the Prophet's action and analogy to other contracts.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: can a person in ihram (muhrim) validly enter into a marriage contract? The Hanafi school holds that it is valid, albeit makruh tanzihi, based on the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah and qiyas with other contracts. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing a verbal prohibition. We will analyse both proofs and see how the Hanafi school reconciles the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: marriage in ihram is valid and binding, though performing it is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The contract itself is sahih; the prohibition is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that marriage in ihram is invalid (batil).
The Shafi'i school relies on a qawli hadith: 'A muhrim should not marry nor give in marriage.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i hadith is a verbal statement of the Prophet, which is given precedence over actions in case of conflict.
Qawli hadith is considered stronger than fi'li in Hanafi usul, but here the Hanafis reinterpret it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Two responses: (1) The word 'nikah' in the hadith means intercourse, not the contract; (2) The prohibition is tanzihi (disliked) not tahrimi. Additionally, qiyas with sale and purchase supports validity.
The Hanafis also cite Maymunah's own hadith that they were halal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis consider the marriage valid and binding; Shafi'is consider it void and must be annulled.
This affects the legality of the marriage and the rights of the spouses.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چهارم
کتاب النکاح آپ محرم تھے اور ان کے ساتھ زفاف کیا حالانکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم حلال تھے ، اور حضرت میمونہ کا انتقال مقام سرف میں ہوا ۔ بعض حضرات نے لطیفہ کے طور پر بیان کیا ہے کہ حضرت میمونہ کی شادی بھی مقام سرف میں ہوئی ، شب زفاف بھی مقام سرف ہی میں گزاری اور حضرت
میمونہ کا انتقال بھی مقام سرف میں ہوا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے بحالت احترام نکاح کیا۔ امام شافعی کے روایت کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں نکاح کے لغوی معنی ( وطی ) مراد ہے۔ اب حدیث کا ترجمہ ہوگا کہ محرم نہ وطی کرے اور نہ محرمہ کو ولی پر قدرت دے۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں نہی تنزیہی مراد ہے تحریمی نہیں ۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ احرام کی حالت میں نکاح کرنا اور نکاح کمرانا مناسب نہیں اگر کر لیا تو منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید قیاس سے بھی ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ نکاح دوسرے عقود بیع و شراء وغیرہ کے مانند ہے۔ جس طرح بیج وغیرہ میں ایجاب و قبول ہوتا ہے اسی طرح نکاح میں بھی ایجاب و قبول کا تلفظ ہوتا ہے، بس حالت احرام میں جس طرح دوسرے عقود جائز ہیں، اسی طرح نکاح بھی جائز ہوگا۔ انصاف کی بات یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام شافعی کا مذہب قوی ہے۔ کیونکہ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث قولی اور احناف کی پیش کردہ فعلی ، اور تعارض حدیثین کے وقت حدیث قولی مقدم ہوتی ہے حدیث فعلی پر۔ اس کے علاوہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حضرت میمونہ سے احرام کی حالت میں نکاح کرنا مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ خود حضرت میمونہ بنت الحارث فرماتی ہیں کہ ” مجھ سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نکاح کیا اور ہم دونوں حلال تھے مسلم، ابوداؤد، ترمذی، ابن ماجہ نے اس حدیث کو روایت کیا ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary Hidayah Volume 4, Book of Nikah. You (the Prophet) were in ihram and had a wedding with her (Maymunah) while you were halal, and Maymunah died in Saraf. Some people have mentioned as a subtle point that Maymunah's marriage was in Saraf, the wedding night was also in Saraf, and her death was also in Saraf. From this hadith it is known that the Prophet married Maymunah while in the state of ihram. The answer to the hadith narrated by Imam Shafi'i is that in this hadith the linguistic meaning of nikah (intercourse) is intended. So the translation of the hadith would be: A muhrim should not have intercourse nor give power to a guardian. The second answer is that the prohibition in the hadith is tanzihi (disliked) not tahrimi (prohibited). So the meaning is that marrying and solemnizing marriage in ihram is not appropriate, but if done, it will be valid. Our school is also supported by qiyas, because marriage is like other contracts such as sale and purchase. Just as in sale there is offer and acceptance, similarly in marriage there is utterance of offer and acceptance. So just as other contracts are permissible in ihram, so is marriage. The fair thing is that Imam Shafi'i's school is strong, because his hadith is qawli (verbal) while the Hanafis present a fi'li (action) hadith, and when hadiths conflict, the qawli is given precedence over the fi'li. Moreover, the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah in ihram is disputed. Indeed, Maymunah bint al-Harith herself says: 'The Prophet married me while we were both halal.' Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah narrated this hadith.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that marriage in ihram is valid, despite the Shafi'i opposition. The commentator gives two responses to Shafi'i's hadith: (1) The word "nikah" in the hadith means intercourse, not contract; (2) The prohibition is merely disliked, not forbidden. Then qiyas with other contracts. Finally, a seeming concession that Shafi'i's view is strong because his evidence is a verbal hadith, and the Hanafi evidence is an action hadith, and actions are less definitive. However, the commentator also quotes Maymunah's own statement that they were halal, which supports the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): Person in the state of ihram (pilgrim's consecration)
نکاح (nikah): Marriage contract
حدیث قولی (hadith qawli): A hadith that is a verbal statement of the Prophet
نہی تنزیہی (nahy tanzihi): A prohibition that indicates dislikedness (makruh) rather than prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person in ihram performing a marriage contract?
A) It is invalid and not binding.
B) It is valid and binding, but disliked.
C) It is only valid if done before ihram.
D) It is makruh tahrimi and invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules marriage in ihram as valid but disliked, based on prophetic action and legal analogy, while the Shafi'i school rules it invalid based on a verbal prohibition.

Marrying a Kitabiyyah Slave Woman: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains the differing opinions on marrying a Jewish or Christian slave woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marrying a Kitabiyyah slave woman, explain the Shafi'i opposing argument, and apply the Hanafi response using Quranic evidence and the principle of 'azl.

Core Idea
Hanafi: marrying any slave woman is absolutely permissible; Shafi'i: only Muslim slave women due to necessity.

The marriage of a free man to a slave woman is a classic point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both schools permit marriage to a Muslim slave woman under certain conditions, they diverge sharply on the Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian) slave woman. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning on both sides, focusing on how the Hanafi school establishes absolute permission based on general Quranic commands and counters the Shafi'i necessity-based argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
State clearly that the Hanafi school permits a free man to marry any slave woman, Muslim or Kitabiyyah, without restriction.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the Shafi'i Position
The Shafi'i school (and Malik, Ahmad in one narration) prohibits marrying a Kitabiyyah slave woman. Understand their reasoning: permissibility of marrying slave women is due to necessity (darurah), and necessity is satisfied by Muslim slave women.
They rely on the mafhum mukhalif of the Quranic verse about believing slave girls.
3
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis argue that the general Quranic verses (e.g., 'Marry what is lawful for you of women') are absolute, not conditional on necessity. The fear of enslaving offspring can be avoided through 'azl (coitus interruptus).
The mafhum mukhalif is interpreted as indicating preference, not prohibition.
4
Apply the Ruling
In practice, a Hanafi may marry a Kitabiyyah slave woman, and the marriage is valid. The Shafi'i would consider such a marriage invalid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

آزاد مومنہ سے نکاح کی قدرت نہ رکھے ہو وہ آپس کی مومنہ باندیوں میں سے کسی سے نکاح کرلے۔ آیت کا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہوگا کہ اگر آزاد مسلمان عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کی قدرت ہے تو مسلمان باندی سے بھی نکاح کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا آیت میں افضل اور اولی کو بیان کیا گیا ہے یعنی طول حرہ کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح بہتر نہیں لیکن کر لیا تو منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندیوں کے ساتھ نکاح کا جواز مطلق ہے۔ مقتضی نکاح کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے مثلاً فانكحوا ماطاب لكم من النساء اور احل لكم ما وراء ذلكم ۔ ان آیات میں مطلق نساء سے نکاح کے جواز کو عام رکھا گیا ہے، آزاد سے ہو یا باندی سے۔
رہا امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ باندی سے نکاح کرنا اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا ہے۔ سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے باندی سے نکاح کرنے میں اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا مقصود نہیں، بلکہ آزاد جز کو حاصل کرنے سے رکنا ہے اور شریعت نے اس کو اس بات کی اجازت دی ہے کہ اصل جز ہی کو حاصل نہ کرے۔ یعنی عورت کی رضامندی سے عزل کر دے تا کہ اصل بچہ ہی پیدا نہ ہو۔ لہذا وصف حریت کو حاصل نہ کرنے کی اجازت بدرجہ اولی ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Ruling on marrying a slave woman, Muslim or Kitabiyyah... Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint. And it is permissible to marry a slave woman whether Muslim or Kitabiyyah. Imam Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for a free man to marry a Kitabiyyah slave woman because permissibility of marrying slave women according to him is due to necessity, because it involves subjecting one's part to slavery, and the necessity is fulfilled by a Muslim slave woman. For this reason, ability to marry a free woman is made a preventer from marrying a slave woman. In our view, permissibility is absolute due to the absolute nature of the initiating cause, and in marrying a slave woman there is abstention from obtaining a free part, not subjecting it to slavery. And he has permission not to obtain the origin, so he also has permission not to obtain the quality. Explanation: There is disagreement about the permissibility of marrying a slave woman. According to us, it is absolutely permissible, whether Muslim or Kitabiyyah. Imam Shafi'i's school says that marrying a Kitabiyyah slave woman is not permissible. Imam Malik also holds this view. In one narration, Imam Ahmad also holds this view. Imam Shafi'i's argument is that the permissibility of marrying slave women is established by necessity, because the meaning of marrying a slave woman is that one intends to make one's part a slave. For the offspring from another's slave woman will also be owned by that other in shari'ah. And making a slave is essentially destruction, so one intends to destroy one's part. And making one's part a slave, i.e., destroying, is prohibited. Therefore, marrying a slave woman should be impermissible. But due to severe need, it was declared permissible out of necessity. Since it is established that marrying slave women is permissible by necessity, and the rule is that what is established by necessity is limited to the extent of necessity. And necessity is fulfilled by marrying a Muslim slave woman, so there is no need to marry a Kitabiyyah. For this reason, Imam Shafi'i made ability to marry a free woman a preventer from marrying a slave woman. The verse: 'And whoever among you does not have the means to marry free believing women, then from what your right hands possess of your believing slave girls...' The implication (mafhum mukhalif) is that if one has the ability to marry a free Muslim woman, then permission to marry a Muslim slave woman is also not given. The answer to this is that the verse states what is better and preferable, i.e., when one has the means to marry a free woman, marrying a slave woman is not better, but if he does it, it will be valid. Our argument is that the permissibility of marrying slave women is absolute due to the absolute nature of the evidence for marriage, such as 'Marry what is lawful for you of women' and 'Permitted to you are those beyond that.' In these verses, the permissibility of marriage is general for all women, whether free or slave. As for Imam Shafi'i's statement that marrying a slave woman is making one's part a slave, the answer is that in marrying a slave woman, the intention is not to make one's part a slave, but rather to abstain from obtaining a free part, and shari'ah has allowed him not to obtain the origin part at all, i.e., he may practice coitus interruptus with the wife's consent so that no child is born. Therefore, not obtaining the quality of freedom is even more permissible. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on marrying slave women, specifically addressing the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding Kitabiyyah slave women. Hanafis permit marrying any slave woman, Muslim or Kitabiyyah, based on general Quranic verses. Shafi'is restrict permission to Muslim slave women because they view the permissibility of marrying slave women as arising from necessity, and necessity is fulfilled by Muslim slaves. The Hanafi response refutes Shafi'i's reasoning by arguing that the Quranic verses are absolute, not conditional on necessity, and that the fear of enslaving one's offspring can be avoided through 'azl (coitus interruptus). The passage also addresses the mafhum mukhalif of the Quranic verse, interpreting it as indicating preference rather than prohibition.

Key Terms
باندی (bandi): Slave woman
کتابیہ (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (Jew or Christian)
ضرورۃ (darurah): Necessity that makes the prohibited permissible
مقتضی (muqtada): The initiating cause or evidence for a ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a free man marrying a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian) slave woman?
A) It is haram and invalid.
B) It is permissible but makruh.
C) It is permissible and valid.
D) It is only permissible if he cannot afford a free Muslim woman.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis permit marriage to a Kitabiyyah slave woman based on absolute Quranic commands, while Shafi'is restrict it to Muslim slave women due to the principle of necessity.

Nikah — Marriage
