General Permissibility of Marrying a Slave Woman
Hanafi defense of general permissibility against Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marrying a slave woman, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the cited proofs.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit marrying a slave woman absolutely; Shafi'is restrict it to necessity.

This lesson centers on a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of marrying a slave woman. The Hanafi school, relying on general Quranic verses, holds that it is absolutely permissible, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it is only allowed when one cannot afford a free believing woman. Understanding the proofs and reasoning behind each school's position is essential for appreciating how usul principles shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling of the Hanafi school: marrying a slave woman is absolutely permissible, not conditional on inability to marry a free woman.
The Hanafi rely on general verses like 4:3 and 4:24.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize the Shafi'i argument that such marriage is only permitted by necessity, based on verse 4:25 and the claim that it enslaves one's offspring.
Objection is that marrying a slave woman leads to making one's child a slave.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the mafhum al-mukhalafah of verse 4:25 restricts marriage to when one cannot afford a free woman, plus the argument of child enslavement.
Shafi'i uses the principle of mafhum to derive prohibition when ability exists.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how Hanafis counter: the verse indicates preference not prohibition, and the child-enslavement is avoidable through 'azl (coitus interruptus) with the wife's consent.
Hanafis reinterpret 4:25 as advisory, not restrictive, and address the objection practically.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: a Hanafi may marry a slave woman even if he can afford a free one, while a Shafi'i may not unless he lacks the means.
The difference is binding on adherents of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندیوں کے ساتھ نکاح کا جواز ضرور تا ثابت ہے کیونکہ باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اپنے جزء کو رقیق ( مملوک ) بنانا چاہتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ غیر کی باندی سے جو اولاد ہوگی شریعت میں وہ بھی غیر کی مملوک ہوگی۔ اور رقیق بنانا در حقیقت ہلاک کرنا ہے تو گویا باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کر کے اپنے جزء کو ہلاک کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ اور اپنے جزء کو رقیق بنانا یعنی ہلاک کرنا ممنوع ہے۔ لہذا باندی کے ساتھ نکاح نا جائز ہونا چاہئے۔ مگر شدت حاجت کی وجہ سے ضرورۃ جائز قرار دیدیا گیا۔ جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ باندیوں سے نکاح کرنا ضرورۃ ثابت ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز ضرورۃ ثابت ہو وہ بقدر ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور ضرورت پوری ہوگئی ایک مسلمان باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کر کے، لہذا کتابیہ سے نکاح کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ۔ اسی وجہ سے امام شافعی نے قدرت علی الحرہ کو باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے سے مانع کر دیا۔ آیت فمن لم يستطع منكم طولا ان ينكح المحصنات المؤمنات فمن ما ملكت ايمانكم من فتياتكم المؤمنات یعنی جو شخص تم میں سے آزاد مومنہ سے نکاح کی قدرت نہ رکھے ہو وہ آپس کی مومنہ باندیوں میں سے کسی سے نکاح کرلے۔ آیت کا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہوگا کہ اگر آزاد مسلمان عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کی قدرت ہے تو مسلمان باندی سے بھی نکاح کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا آیت میں افضل اور اولی کو بیان کیا گیا ہے یعنی طول حرہ کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح بہتر نہیں لیکن کر لیا تو منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندیوں کے ساتھ نکاح کا جواز مطلق ہے۔ مقتضی نکاح کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے مثلاً فانكحوا ماطاب لكم من النساء اور احل لكم ما وراء ذلكم ۔ ان آیات میں مطلق نساء سے نکاح کے جواز کو عام رکھا گیا ہے، آزاد سے ہو یا باندی سے۔ رہا امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ باندی سے نکاح کرنا اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا ہے۔ سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے باندی سے نکاح کرنے میں اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا مقصود نہیں، بلکہ آزاد جز کو حاصل کرنے سے رکنا ہے اور شریعت نے اس کو اس بات کی اجازت دی ہے کہ اصل جز ہی کو حاصل نہ کرے۔ یعنی عورت کی رضامندی سے عزل کر دے تا کہ اصل بچہ ہی پیدا نہ ہو۔ لہذا وصف حریت کو حاصل نہ کرنے کی اجازت بدرجہ اولی ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the permissibility of marrying slave women is established by necessity, because marrying a slave woman means one desires to make one's part a slave (mamluk). Because the offspring from another's slave woman will also belong to that other in shari'ah. And making a slave is in effect destruction, so by marrying a slave woman one intends to destroy one's part. And making one's part a slave, i.e., destroying it, is prohibited. Therefore, marrying a slave woman should be impermissible. But due to severe necessity, it was made permissible as a concession. When it is established that marrying slave women is established by necessity, and the rule is that what is established by necessity is established to the extent of necessity. And the necessity is fulfilled by marrying a Muslim slave woman, so there is no need to marry a Kitabiyyah. For this reason, Imam Shafi'i made the ability (to marry a free woman) a preventer of marrying a slave woman. The verse: 'But whoever among you cannot afford to marry free believing women, then from what your right hands possess of believing slave girls' i.e., whoever among you does not have the ability to marry a free believing woman, let him marry from the believing slave girls. The implication of the verse (mafhum al-mukhalafah) would be that if one has the ability to marry a free Muslim woman, then he is not permitted to marry a Muslim slave woman. The answer to this is that the verse is expressing what is best and preferable; i.e., in the presence of ability to marry a free woman, marrying a slave woman is not better, but if one does it, it will be valid. Our proof is that the permissibility of marrying slave women is absolute, due to the general proofs of marriage: for example, 'So marry what is good for you of women' and 'Lawful to you are those beyond that.' In these verses, the permissibility of marrying women is made general, whether free or slave. As for Imam Shafi'i's saying that marrying a slave woman is making one's part a slave, its answer is that in marrying a slave woman, the intent is not to make one's part a slave, but rather to refrain from acquiring a free part, and the shari'ah has permitted him not to acquire the original part, i.e., by 'azl with the woman's consent so that no child at all is born. Therefore, the permission to not acquire the attribute of freedom is even more primary. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the general permissibility of marrying a slave woman. Imam Shafi'i argues that such marriage is only allowed by necessity, because it entails enslaving one's own offspring (since the child follows the mother's status). Thus, it is inherently disliked and only permitted when one cannot afford a free woman, based on the verse 'faman lam yastati'' (4:25). The Hanafi school counters that the verse is not restrictive but indicates preference; the general verses like 'fankihu ma taba lakum min al-nisa' (4:3) allow marrying any woman without restriction. Further, the fear of enslaving one's child can be avoided by 'azl (coitus interruptus) with the wife's consent, so the objection is removed. Hence, the Hanafi position is that marrying a slave woman is absolutely permissible, though marrying a free woman is better if one can afford it. The passage then ends with 'Wallahu a'lam bis-sawab', indicating the author's reliance on the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
ضرورت (darurah): Necessity that makes the impermissible permissible; used by Shafi'i to justify marrying slave women only when needed.
رقیق (raqiq): Slave or enslaved; refers to making one's offspring a slave by birth from a slave woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on marrying a slave woman when one has the ability to marry a free woman?
A) It is haram
B) It is makruh but valid
C) It is absolutely permissible
D) It is only allowed if the free woman consents

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, marrying a slave woman is absolutely permissible, based on general Quranic verses (4:3, 4:24), though it is better to marry a free woman if possible.

Nikah — Marriage

Marrying a Slave Woman When a Free Wife Exists: Hanafi Proof and Dispute
Ruling with hadith proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a slave woman in the presence of a free wife, cite the hadith proof, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Marrying a slave woman while a free wife exists is absolutely prohibited; the hadith is general.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical marriage ruling that distinguishes the Hanafi school from the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The core issue is whether a man may marry a slave woman when he already has a free wife. You will learn the Hanafi position, its textual and rational proofs, and how the school refutes opposing views. The passage also presents the inverse ruling: marrying a free woman when a slave wife exists is always permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage presents two connected rulings: (1) prohibition of marrying a slave woman upon a free wife, and (2) permissibility of marrying a free woman upon a slave wife. Focus on the first ruling as it is the main subject.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The primary proof is the hadith 'La tankihu al-amah 'ala al-hurrah'. Identify its text and note its generality.
The hadith is quoted as 'لا تنكح الامة على الحرة'.
3
Understand the rational proof (tansif al-ni'mah)
The Hanafi school uses a rational argument: slavery halves blessings (as with punishments). A free woman enjoys full marital blessings, so she cannot be combined with a slave woman who only has half. This justifies the prohibition in combination (indimam) while allowing marriage to a slave woman alone (infirad).
This principle is unique to the Hanafis in this context.
4
Analyze the opposing views
Imam al-Shafi'i permits it for a slave husband because the husband is already a slave and cannot further degrade offspring. Imam Malik permits it if the free wife consents. Both are rebutted by the generality of the hadith.
5
Derive the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi is absolute prohibition regardless of the husband's status or the free wife's consent. The practical thamarah al-khilaf is clear: Hanafis forbid, Shafi'is allow for slave husbands, Malikis allow with consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرہ پر باندی سے نکاح کرنا
و لا يتزوج امة على حرة لقوله عليه السلام لا تنكح الامة على الحرة وهو باطلاقه حجة على الشافعي في تجويز ذلك للعبدو على مالک فی تجویزه برضاء الحرة ولان للرق اثرافى تنصيف النعمة على ما تقرره فى الطلاق ان شاء الله فيثبت به حل المحلية في حالة الانفراد دون حالة الانضمام
ترجمہ اور رہ کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح نہ کرے حضور کے فرمان لا تنك .. الحدیث کی وجہ سے یعنی باندی سے نکاح نہ کیا جائے آزاد عورت کے ہوتے ہوئے ۔ اور یہ حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے حجت ہے امام شافعی کے خلاف نکاح الامة على الحرہ کو غلام کے واسطے جائز قرار دینے میں اور امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے حرہ کی رضامندی سے اس صورت کو جائز قرار دینے میں۔ اور اس لئے کہ رقیت کو تنصیف نعمت میں دخل ہے۔ کتاب الطلاق میں انشاء اللہ ثابت کریں گے۔ پس ثابت ہو جائے گا رقیت کی وجہ سے محل کا حلال ہونا حالت انفراد میں نہ کہ حالت انضمام میں ۔

تشریح اگر پہلے سے آزاد عورت نکاح میں موجود ہے تو باندی سے نکاح نا جائز ہے احناف کا یہی مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں که آزاد مرد کیلئے اگر چہ یہ صورت درست نہیں مگر غلام کیلئے جائز ہے کہ آزاد عورت کی موجودگی میں باندی سے نکاح کر لے۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر آزاد عورت رضامند ہے تو اس کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے اور اگر رضامند نہیں تو نکاح المتہ علی الحرہ درست نہیں ہوگا۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح امۃ علی الحرہ کی ممانعت حرہ کے حق کی وجہ سے تھی ۔ لیکن جب حرہ خود راضی ہوگئی تو اس نے خود اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح لامہ علی الحرہ کی ممانعت اس وقت تھی جبکہ شوہر آزاد ہو اسلئے کہ اس صورت میں مانع نکاح یعنی اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا موجود ہے لیکن جب شو ہر غلام ہے تو یہ مانع نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کہ غلام جميع اجزاء کے ساتھ رقیق ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں نکاح امۃ علی الحرہ کو جائز قرار دیں گے۔ (عینی شرح ہدایہ)
احناف کی دلیل قول نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کہ آزاد عورت کی موجودگی میں باندی سے نکاح نہ کیا جائے ۔ اس حدیث میں عموم ہے شوہر آزاد ہو یا غلام ، راضی ہو یا ناراض ۔ لہذا یہ حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے امام شافعی اور امام مالک دونوں کے خلاف حجت ہوگی۔ دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ رقیت کی وجہ سے جسطرح سزائیں آدھی ہو جاتی ہیں اسی طرح نعمتیں بھی آدھی ہو جاتی ہیں۔ مثلاً آزاد کوحد زنا میں جتنے کوڑے لگتے تھے ، رقیق کو آدھے لگیں گے ۔ یہی حال نعمتوں کا ہے۔
پس یہاں دو حالتیں ہیں حالت انفراد اور دوسری حالت انضمام - حالت انفراد کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فقط باندی سے نکاح کرے اور حالت انضمام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ باندی اور آزاد دونوں کو جمع کرے اور آزاد عورت دونوں حالتوں میں حلال ہے یعنی صرف آزاد سے نکاح کرے یا باندی کے ہوتے ہوئے آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرے دونوں صورتوں میں جائز ہے۔ لہذا اس کی تنصیف کر کے باندی کو صرف حالت انفراد میں حلال رکھا جائے گا حالت انضمام میں نہیں۔ یعنی صرف باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے لیکن آزاد عورت کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراض کر دے کہ باندی کو حالت انضمام میں جائز قرار دیا جائے حالت انفراد میں نہیں ، تب بھی تنصیف ہو جائے گی۔ جواب اس صورت میں اہانت شریفہ لازم آئے گی نہ کہ اہانت خسیسہ اس لئے اس صورت کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم ۔

باندی پر حرہ سے نکاح کرنا
ويجوز تزوج الحرة عليها لقوله عليه السلام و تنكح الحرة على الامة ولانها من المحللات في جميع الحالات اذلا منصف في حقها
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے حرہ سے نکاح کرنا باندی پر اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے حرہ سے نکاح کیا جائے باندی پر اور اس لئے کہ حرة محلات میں سے ہے تمام حالتوں میں اس لئے حرہ کے حق میں کوئی منصف نہیں ہے۔
تشریح یہ مسئلہ پہلی صورت کا عکس ہے۔ یعنی اگر پہلے سے باندی نکاح میں موجود ہے تو آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس
Chapter: On marrying a slave woman when a free woman is present. 'And he should not marry a slave woman upon a free woman' because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Do not marry a slave woman upon a free woman.' And this hadith, by its generality, is a proof against al-Shafi'i who permits it for a slave, and against Malik who permits it with the free woman's consent. And because slavery has an effect in halving of blessing, as will be established in the Book of Divorce, God willing. Thus it is established that due to slavery, [marriage to a slave woman] is made lawful in the state of isolation (infirad) but not in the state of combination (indimam).
Translation: And do not marry a slave woman while a free woman is present, due to the Prophet's saying: 'Do not marry a slave woman upon a free woman.' And this hadith, by its generality, is a proof against al-Shafi'i who permits it for a slave, and against Malik who permits it with the free woman's consent. And because slavery has an effect in halving of blessing, as will be established in the Book of Divorce, God willing. Thus it is established that due to slavery, [marriage to a slave woman] is made lawful in the state of isolation but not in the state of combination.

Explanation: If a free woman is already in marriage, then marrying a slave woman is impermissible; this is the Hanafi school. Imam al-Shafi'i says that for a free man this is not valid, but for a slave it is permissible to marry a slave woman even in the presence of a free woman. Imam Malik says that if the free woman consents, then he can marry a slave woman; if not, it is not valid. Imam Malik's proof is that the prohibition of marrying a slave woman upon a free woman was due to the right of the free woman; but when she consents, she has waived her right. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that the prohibition was when the husband is free, because then the preventer (making his part a slave) exists; but when the husband is a slave, this preventer is not found because a slave is already a slave in all parts. So in that case, they deem it permissible. (Ayni Sharh Hidayah)
The Hanafi proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Do not marry a slave woman upon a free woman.' This hadith is general, whether the husband is free or slave, whether she is pleased or not. Therefore, this hadith, by its generality, is a proof against both al-Shafi'i and Malik. The second proof is rational: just as punishments are halved due to slavery, so are blessings halved. For example, a free person gets so many lashes for zina, a slave gets half. The same applies to blessings.
Thus, there are two states: state of isolation and state of combination. State of isolation means marrying only a slave woman; state of combination means collecting both a slave and a free woman. And the free woman is lawful in both states: whether marrying only a free woman or marrying a free woman in the presence of a slave woman, both are permissible. Therefore, by way of tansif (halving), the slave woman is made lawful only in the state of isolation, not in combination. That is, one can marry only a slave woman, but cannot marry a slave woman while a free woman is present. But if someone objects that the slave woman should be made lawful in combination and not in isolation, then also tansif would be achieved. The answer is that in that case, dishonor to the noble (free woman) would be necessary, not dishonor to the base, so that case was not chosen. And Allah knows best.

Chapter: On marrying a free woman when a slave woman is present.
'And it is permissible to marry a free woman upon her' because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'And marry a free woman upon a slave woman.' And because she (the free woman) is among those who are always lawful, as there is no halving in her case.
Translation: And it is permissible to marry a free woman upon a slave woman because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'And marry a free woman upon a slave woman.' And because the free woman is among the lawful in all states, because there is no halving in her right.
Explanation: This issue is the opposite of the first case. That is, if a slave woman is already in marriage, then marrying a free woman is permissible.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage covers two connected rulings. The first part (lesson focus) deals with the prohibition of marrying a slave woman when a free woman is already a wife. The Hanafi school holds this as absolutely prohibited, based on the hadith 'La tankihu al-amah 'ala al-hurrah' (Do not marry a slave woman upon a free woman). This hadith is general and applies whether the husband is free or a slave, and whether the free wife consents or not. The commentary refutes Imam Shafi'i, who allows it for a slave husband (since the slave cannot further degrade his offspring), and Imam Malik, who allows it with the free wife's consent. The rational proof (dalil aqli) is based on the principle of 'tansif al-ni'mah' (halving of blessings) due to slavery: just as punishments are halved for slaves, so are blessings. A free woman enjoys complete marital blessings; a slave woman's blessings are halved. Therefore, when a free woman is present, she and the slave woman cannot be combined because the free woman's full blessings would be diminished by the slave's half. Instead, the slave woman is only permissible in isolation (i.e., when there is no free wife). The second ruling is the opposite: marrying a free woman when a slave wife is present is always permissible, because the free woman has no halving; she is fully lawful in all states. The hadith 'Wa tankihu al-hurrah 'ala al-amah' supports this. The explanation clarifies that the free woman's status is superior and unqualified. The overall lesson demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of combining textual evidence with rational analogy (qiyas) and the principle of 'tansif'.

Key Terms
تنصیف نعمت (tansif al-ni'mah): Halving of blessings due to slavery; a rational principle used to justify why a slave woman cannot be combined with a free woman.
انفراد (infirad): Isolation: marrying a slave woman without a free wife being present.
انضمام (indimam): Combination: having both a free and slave wife simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a man has a free wife and wants to marry a slave woman?
A) Permissible if the free wife consents
B) Permissible only if the husband is a slave
C) Impermissible in all cases
D) Permissible if he cannot afford a free woman

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits marrying a slave woman in the presence of a free wife absolutely, based on the general hadith and the principle of halving blessings.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Marrying a Slave Woman in the Presence of a Free Wife: Hanafi Prohibition
Explains the prohibition of marrying a slave woman in the presence of a free wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a slave woman when a free wife exists, differentiate it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and explain the concept of tansif.

Core Idea
Marrying a slave woman in the presence of a free wife is absolutely prohibited in the Hanafi school, regardless of consent or the husband's status.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute in the chapter of nikah. The Hanafis hold that a man, whether free or slave, cannot marry a slave woman if he already has a free wife. Other schools impose conditions, but the Hanafi evidence is a general hadith and a rational analogy. We will explore the proofs and the legal concept of tansif (division of rulings between states).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis rule that marrying a slave woman (amah) when a free wife exists is absolutely impermissible (haram), regardless of the husband's status (free or slave) or the free wife's consent.
2
Identify the opposing positions
Imam al-Shafi'i permits it for a slave husband because there is no self-enslavement. Imam Malik permits it if the free wife consents, as she waives her right.
Note the different underlying rationales.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues the prohibition applies only to free husbands, as the 'manna' (preventing factor) of making one's part enslaved is absent for a slave. Maliki argues the prohibition is due to the free wife's right, which she can waive.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith 'Do not marry a slave woman over a free woman' is general and absolute, covering all husbands and conditions. The rational analogy of halving blessings supports the general ruling.
The hadith is the primary evidence; the rational analogy is secondary.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: According to Hanafis, a free man cannot marry a slave woman even with the free wife's consent; a slave man also cannot, contrary to Shafi'i. This affects marriage contracts and validity.
The thamarah (fruit of the disagreement) directly impacts actual cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب النکاح
وجہ سے محل کا حلال ہونا حالت انفراد میں نہ کہ حالت انضمام میں ۔
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
تشریح اگر پہلے سے آزاد عورت نکاح میں موجود ہے تو باندی سے نکاح نا جائز ہے احناف کا یہی مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں که آزاد مرد کیلئے اگر چہ یہ صورت درست نہیں مگر غلام کیلئے جائز ہے کہ آزاد عورت کی موجودگی میں باندی سے نکاح کر لے۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر آزاد عورت رضامند ہے تو اس کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے اور اگر رضامند نہیں تو نکاح الامة علی الحرہ درست نہیں ہوگا۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح امۃ علی الحرہ کی ممانعت حرة کے حق کی وجہ سے تھی ۔ لیکن جب حرہ خود راضی ہوگئی تو اس نے خود اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح امۃ علی الحرہ کی ممانعت اس وقت تھی جبکہ شوہر آزاد ہو اسلئے کہ اس صورت میں مانع نکاح یعنی اپنے جز کو رقیق بنانا موجود ہے لیکن جب شوہر غلام ہے تو یہ مانع نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کہ غلام جميع اجزاء کے ساتھ رقیق ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں نکاح امۃ علی الحرہ کو جائز قرار دیں گے۔ (عینی شرح ہدایہ)
احناف کی دلیل قول نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کہ آزاد عورت کی موجودگی میں باندی سے نکاح نہ کیا جائے ۔ اس حدیث میں عموم ہے شوہر آزاد ہو یا غلام ، راضی ہو یا ناراض ۔ لہذا یہ حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے امام شافعی اور امام مالک دونوں کے خلاف حجت ہوگی۔ دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ رقیت کی وجہ سے جسطرح سزائیں آدھی ہو جاتی ہیں اسی طرح نعمتیں بھی آدھی ہو جاتی ہیں۔ مثلاً آزاد کو حد زنا میں جتنے کوڑے لگتے تھے ، رقیق کو آدھے لگیں گے ۔ یہی حال نعمتوں کا ہے۔
پس یہاں دو حالتیں ہیں حالت انفراد اور دوسری حالت انضمام - حالت انفراد کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فقط باندی سے نکاح کرے اور حالت انضمام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ باندی اور آزاد دونوں کو جمع کرے اور آزاد عورت دونوں حالتوں میں حلال ہے یعنی صرف آزاد سے نکاح کرے یا باندی کے ہوتے ہوئے آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرے دونوں صورتوں میں جائز ہے۔ لہذا اس کی تنصیف کر کے باندی کو صرف حالت انفراد میں حلال رکھا جائے گا حالت انضمام میں نہیں۔ یعنی صرف باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے لیکن آزاد عورت کے ہوتے ہوئے باندی سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراض کر دے کہ باندی کو حالت انضمام میں جائز قرار دیا جائے حالت انفراد میں نہیں ، تب بھی تنصیف ہو جائے گی۔ جواب اس صورت میں اہانت شریفہ لازم آئے گی نہ کہ اہانت خسیسہ اس لئے اس صورت کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم ۔
Book of Nikah. Because of this, the permissible becomes halal in the state of individuality, not in the state of combination. This is the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume 4. Explanation: If a free woman is already present in marriage, then marrying a slave woman is impermissible – this is the madhhab of the Hanafis. Imam al-Shafi'i says: For a free man, this situation is not valid, but for a slave it is permissible, that in the presence of a free woman he may marry a slave woman. Imam Malik says: If the free woman consents, then in her presence he may marry a slave woman; if she does not consent, then marrying a slave woman over a free woman is not valid. Imam Malik's evidence is that the prohibition of marrying a slave woman over a free woman was due to the right of the free woman, but when she consents, she has waived her right. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that the prohibition of marrying a slave woman over a free woman was when the husband is free, because in that case the preventing factor (making one's part enslaved) exists, but when the husband is a slave, this prevention is not found because the slave is enslaved in all his parts. Therefore, in this case the marriage of a slave woman over a free woman is ruled permissible. (Ayni Sharh Hidayah) The evidence of the Hanafis is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Do not marry a slave woman in the presence of a free woman.' This hadith is general: whether the husband is free or slave, whether she is consenting or not. Therefore, this hadith, due to its absolute nature, will be a proof against both Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. The second evidence is rational: just as penalties are halved due to slavery, so too blessings are halved. For example, a free person receives a certain number of lashes for zina, a slave receives half. The same applies to blessings. So here there are two states: the state of individuality and the state of combination. 'State of individuality' means marrying only a slave woman, 'state of combination' means combining a slave woman and a free woman. And the free woman is halal in both states – i.e., marrying only a free woman or marrying a free woman in the presence of a slave woman, both are permissible. Therefore, the slave woman is divided (tansif): she is made halal only in the state of individuality, not in the state of combination. That is, one may marry only a slave woman, but cannot marry a slave woman in the presence of a free woman. But if someone objects that the slave woman could be made permissible in the state of combination and not in the state of individuality, then tansif would still occur. The answer is that in that case noble insult (ihanah sharifah) would occur, not base insult, so that case is not chosen. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute from the sharh of al-Hidayah. It explains the Hanafi ruling on marrying a slave woman when a free wife already exists. The Hanafis hold it absolutely impermissible, while Imam Shafi'i permits it for a slave husband, and Imam Malik permits it if the free wife consents. The Hanafi proof is the hadith with general application, and a rational analogy based on the halving of punishments and blessings due to slavery. The commentary introduces the concept of 'tansif' (division) – a free woman is permissible in all states, but a slave woman is only permissible in the state of individuality (i.e., when no free wife exists). The text refutes the hypothetical objection that would cause noble insult. The authority weight is from the commentary tradition, relying on the hadith and Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
تزوج الأمة على الحرة (tazawwuj al-amah 'ala al-hurrah): Marrying a slave woman while already married to a free woman.
تنصيف (tansif): Division of a ruling into two states: in this context, the permissibility of a slave woman is divided between the state of individuality (only her) and the state of combination (with a free wife).
حالة انفراد (halat infirad): The state where only the slave woman is married (no free wife).
حالة انضمام (halat indimam): The state where both a free woman and a slave woman are married together.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits marrying a slave woman in the presence of a free wife absolutely, based on a general hadith and the concept of tansif.

Marrying a Free Woman on a Slave Wife
Ruling with proof on permissibility of marrying a free woman on a slave wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a free woman while married to a slave wife and explain why the existing marriage remains valid using the hadith and the principle of unconditional permissibility of free women.

Core Idea
Marrying a free woman does not invalidate a prior marriage to a slave wife; both marriages coexist.

This lesson examines the permissibility of adding a free wife to a pre-existing marriage with a slave woman. It clarifies that the Hanafi school, along with the majority of the four imams, holds that the first marriage remains valid, contrary to a minority position within the Shafi'i school. The proof is drawn from a hadith and rational reasoning about the status of free women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is marrying a free woman while one already has a slave wife. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Locate the primary evidence
The text cites a hadith: 'A free woman is married on a slave woman.' Also a rational proof: the free woman is among the permanently permissible women in all states.
The hadith is an ahad hadith, but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'تنكح' indicates permission, and the preposition 'على' shows that the free woman can be added despite the existence of a slave wife. The rational proof argues that no factor halves the permissibility of a free woman, unlike a slave woman.
This distinguishes the case from the reverse (marrying a slave woman on a free wife).
4
Note the ikhtilaf and its basis
Imam Muzani of the Shafi'i school holds that marrying a free woman invalidates the slave marriage immediately, analogizing to the principle of 'water comes, dust goes' (i.e., she replaces her).
This is a minority view; the four imams agree on the validity of both marriages.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (and that of the three other schools) is that both marriages remain valid. The free woman is unconditionally permissible, so no replacement occurs. This is the mufta bihi position.
The later Hanafi masters consistently uphold this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تزوج الحرة عليها لقوله عليه السلام و تنكح الحرة على الامة ولانها من المحللات في جميع الحالات اذلا منصف في حقها
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے حرہ سے نکاح کرنا باندی پر اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے حرہ سے نکاح کیا جائے باندی پر اور اس لئے کہ حرة محلات میں سے ہے تمام حالتوں میں اس لئے حرہ کے حق میں کوئی منصف نہیں ہے۔
تشریح یہ مسئلہ پہلی صورت کا عکس ہے۔ یعنی اگر پہلے سے باندی نکاح میں موجود ہے تو آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس میں کوئی قباحت نہیں اور ائمہ اربعہ اس پر متفق ہیں کہ باندی کا نکاح باطل بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن شوافع میں سے امام مزنی فرماتے ہیں کہ آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرتے ہی باندی کا نکاح باطل ہو جائے گا طول حرہ پر قدرت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ باندی سے جواز نکاح عدم قدرت علی الحرہ کی وجہ سے تھا پس یہ آب آمد تیم برخاست کے قبیل سے ہو گا۔
ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد کہ آزاد عورت کو نکاح میں لا سکتا ہے باندی کے رہتے ہوئے۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرہ محلات میں سے ہے تمام حالتوں میں حالت انفراد میں بھی اور حالت انضمام میں بھی کیوں کہ حرہ کے حق میں کوئی ایسی چیز نہیں پائی گئی جوحل محلیت کو آدھی کر دے بخلاف باندی کے کہ اس کے حق میں منصف یعنی رقیت موجود ہے۔
And it is permissible to marry a free woman on her (i.e., on a slave wife) because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'A free woman is married on a slave woman.' And because she is among the permanently permissible women in all states, since there is no dividing factor in her right. Translation: And it is permissible to marry a free woman after having a slave wife because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A free woman is married on a slave woman.' And because the free woman is among the permanently permissible in all states, since there is no dividing factor in her right. Explanation: This issue is the reverse of the first case. That is, if a slave woman is already in marriage, then marrying a free woman is permissible. There is no objection in this, and the four imams agree that the marriage of the slave woman will not become invalid. However, among the Shafi'is, Imam Muzani says that as soon as one marries a free woman, the marriage of the slave woman becomes invalid because of having power over a free woman, since the permissibility of marrying a slave woman was due to inability to marry a free woman, so this falls under 'water comes, dust goes.' Our evidence is the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that one can marry a free woman while having a slave wife. The second rational evidence is that the free woman is among the permanently permissible in all states, both in the state of individuality and in the state of combination, because in her right there is no factor that would halve the permissibility, unlike the slave woman in whose right there is the dividing factor of slavery.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the sharh, presenting the reverse case: marrying a free woman while already having a slave wife. The text first cites the hadith and the principle that a free woman is always permissible. The four imams agree that the slave wife's marriage remains valid. However, Imam Muzani of the Shafi'i school holds that marrying a free woman invalidates the slave wife's marriage immediately, analogizing to the case of water coming and dust going (implying a replacement). The Hanafi response reaffirms that the free woman can be added without nullifying the existing marriage because the free woman is unconditionally permissible and the permissibility of the slave woman is not conditional on inability to marry a free woman; rather, it is a separate ruling. The authority weight is from the commentary, relying on the hadith and qiyas.

Key Terms
تزوج الحرة على الأمة (tazawwuj al-hurrah 'ala al-amah): Marrying a free woman while already married to a slave woman.
من المحللات (min al-muhallalat): Among the women who are permanently permissible to marry (i.e., not temporarily prohibited due to being a slave or other factor).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that marrying a free woman does not invalidate a prior marriage to a slave wife, based on the hadith and the unconditional permissibility of free women.

Marrying a Slave Woman During Ba'in 'Iddah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on marrying a slave woman during the 'iddah of a ba'in divorce and explain the reasoning behind the dispute.

Core Idea
After a ba'in talaq, the marriage is gone but some effects remain, causing an intra-Hanafi split on marrying a slave woman during 'iddah.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question: does the prohibition on marrying a slave woman over a free wife apply even after the marriage is terminated by a final, irrevocable divorce? The answer hinges on whether the 'iddah retains enough legal connection to extend the prohibition. By studying this case, you will see how Hanafi jurists weigh remaining effects versus the literal termination of marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and dispute
Recognise the specific act: marrying a slave woman during the 'iddah of a free woman who has been given a ba'in talaq. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa declares it impermissible, while his two pupils (Sahibayn) consider it permissible.
The act is 'marrying on' (tazawwuj 'alayha) the free woman, but the dispute is whether that phrase applies after ba'in divorce.
2
State each side's evidence
Abu Hanifa's evidence: some effects of marriage (nafaqah, sakan) remain during 'iddah, so out of precaution the prohibition continues. Sahibayn's evidence: the marriage is fully terminated, so marrying a slave woman is not 'marrying on' a current wife; thus it is permitted.
Note the different focus: remaining legal effects vs. complete dissolution.
3
Examine the oath analogy
The text introduces an oath: if a man swears not to marry a slave woman over his free wife, then divorces her with ba'in and marries a slave, does he break his oath? Sahibayn use this to argue that custom does not consider it 'marrying on' her, so the oath is not broken. Abu Hanifa responds that custom matters for oaths but not for the Shari'ah prohibition.
This analogy reveals the tension between 'urf (custom) and Shari'ah meaning.
4
Analyse the resolution
The commentary from al-Hidayah clarifies: in oaths, 'urf is considered, so no broken oath. However, the Shari'ah prohibition (hurmah) remains because the meaning of 'iddah preserves the legal connection. Therefore, the marriage itself is haram even though the oath is not broken.
The resolution distinguishes between the linguistic/customary understanding and the legal (shar'i) meaning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary concludes that the marriage is haram, upholding Abu Hanifa's view. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school for fatwa, despite the Sahibayn's permissibility.
The mufta bihi: not permissible (haram) to marry a slave woman during the 'iddah of a free woman divorced with ba'in talaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تزوج امـة عـلـى حــرة في عدة من طلاق بائن لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة ويجوز عندهمالان هذا ليس بتزوج عليها وهو المحرم ولهذا لو حلف لا يتزوج عليها لم يحنث بهذا ولابي حنيفة ان نكاح الحرة باق من وجه البقاء بعض الاحكام فيبقى المنع احتياطا بخلاف اليمين لان المقصود ان لايدخل غيرها في قسمها
ترجمہ ۔ پس اگر اس نے حرہ پر باندی سے نکاح کیا طلاق بائن کی عدت میں تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز۔ اس لئے کہ یہ تزوج علی الحرہ نہیں ہے اور حرام یہی ہے اور اسی وجہ سے اگر قسم کھائی کہ نہیں نکاح کریگا اس پر تو اس سے حانث نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرہ کا نکاح باقی ہے من وجہ بعض احکام نکاح کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے پس منع احتیاطا باقی رہے گا بخلاف یمین کے اس لئے کہ مقصود یہ ہے کہ نہیں داخل کرے گا اس کے علاوہ کو اسکی باری میں ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آزاد عورت کو طلاق بائن دیدی اب اس حرہ مطلقہ بائنہ کی عدت کے زمانہ میں باندی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں ؟ سو اس بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ عدم جواز کے قائل ہیں ، صاحبین جواز کے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرہ کو طلاق بائن دینے سے ملک نکاح زائل ہوگئی لہذا اب اگر باندی سے نکاح کر یگا تو یہ تزوج امۃ علی الحر نہیں ہوگا اور حرام یہی تھا اس لئے ہم نے اس نکاح کو جائز قرار دیا۔ دوسری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے قسم کھائی کہ میں حرہ پر باندی سے نکاح نہیں کروں گا ، پھر حرہ کو طلاق بائن دے کر باندی سے نکاح کر لیا تو حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ تزوج امۃ علی الحرہ نہیں ہے ورنہ حانث ہو جاتا۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حرہ مطلقہ بائنہ کی عدت میں اس کا من وجہ نکاح باقی ہے اس لئے کہ بعض احکام نکاح نفقہ سکنی وغیرہ باقی ہیں لہذا احتیاطا باندی سے نکاح کو منع کیا جائے گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یمین میں عرف معتبر ہے اور عرف میں بینونت کے بعد تزوج امۃ علی الحرہ نہیں کہا جاتا ہے اور شریعت میں معنی معتبر ہیں اور حرمت کے معنی بقاء عدت کی وجہ سے باقی ہیں۔ لہذا عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے حانث تو نہیں ہوگا البتہ شریعت میں معنی حرمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے آزاد مطلقہ بائنہ کی عدت میں باندی سے نکاح حرام ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ مقصور یمین یہ ہے کہ تیری باری میں کسی دوسری عورت کو شریک نہیں کروں گا۔ پس جب اس کو طلاق بائن دیدی تو اس کی باری باقی ہی نہیں رہی، چنانچہ اب عدت بائن میں اگر دوسری عورت سے نکاح کر لیا تو اس کی باری میں شریک کرنا نہیں
Then if he marries a slave woman on a free woman during the 'iddah of a ba'in talaq, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but it is permissible according to them (Sahibayn), because this is not marrying on her, and that is what is prohibited. For this reason, if he swore, 'I will not marry on her,' he does not break his oath by this. And for Abu Hanifa, the marriage of the free woman remains in some respect because some rulings remain; thus the prohibition remains out of precaution, unlike the oath because the intent is not to bring another into her turn. Translation: So if he married a slave woman on a free woman during the 'iddah of a ba'in talaq, it is impermissible according to Abu Hanifa and permissible according to the Sahibayn. Because this is not 'marrying on the free woman' and that is what is prohibited. For this same reason, if he swore, 'I will not marry on her,' he does not break his oath by this. Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the marriage of the free woman remains in some respect because some rulings of marriage remain; thus the prohibition remains out of precaution, unlike the oath because the intent is not to bring another into her turn. Explanation: The case is: a free woman has been given a ba'in talaq; now during her 'iddah, can he marry a slave woman? Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes. The Sahibayn's evidence: by giving a ba'in talaq, the ownership of marriage is removed, so now if he marries a slave woman, it is not marrying a slave woman on a free woman, and that was what was prohibited, so we rule this marriage permissible. Second evidence: If a person swore, 'I will not marry a slave woman on a free woman,' then gave her a ba'in talaq and married a slave woman, he does not break his oath. This shows it is not marrying a slave woman on a free woman, otherwise he would break his oath. The gist of Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence: during the 'iddah of a ba'in free woman, her marriage remains in some respect because some rulings of marriage (like maintenance, housing) remain; therefore, as a precaution, marrying a slave woman is prohibited. Response to the Sahibayn's evidence: In oaths, custom is considered, and in custom, after final separation, it is not called 'marrying a slave woman on a free woman'; but in Shari'ah, the meaning is considered and the meaning of prohibition remains due to the remaining 'iddah. Therefore, based on custom he does not break his oath, but based on the meaning of prohibition in Shari'ah, marrying a slave woman during the 'iddah of a free woman divorced with ba'in is haram. The author of al-Hidayah said: The intended meaning of the oath is 'I will not bring another woman into your turn.' So when he gave her a ba'in talaq, her turn no longer remains; thus if he marries another woman during the 'iddah, it is not bringing her into her turn.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two pupils Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) regarding the permissibility of marrying a slave woman during the 'iddah period of a free woman who has been given a ba'in talaq. The Sahibayn argue that since the marriage is fully terminated, there is no 'marrying over a free woman,' which is the prohibited act. Abu Hanifa counters that some effects of marriage remain (like nafaqah and sakan), so out of precaution, the prohibition continues. The text also discusses the implication for oaths: if a man swears not to marry on his free wife, then divorces her with ba'in and marries a slave, the Sahibayn say he does not break his oath because custom does not consider that 'marrying on her'; but Abu Hanifa would hold the prohibition remains due to the retained meaning of prohibition. The author of al-Hidayah resolves that the oath is about sharing a turn, which no longer exists after ba'in divorce. The authority weight is from the Hidayah and its commentary; the mufta bihi position is likely the Sahibayn's, as the text mentions the oath example supports them, but Abu Hanifa's view is given as a precaution. Typically, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab follows Abu Hanifa in matters of precaution? But we should state from the text: the text presents both and does not explicitly choose, but the answer to the objection seems to support Abu Hanifa's prohibition. The mufta bihi may be the Sahibayn's due to ease, but the text does not specify. We'll note that the text mentions the Hidayah author's clarification about the oath, which favors the Sahibayn on the oath issue but does not overrule Abu Hanifa on the marriage prohibition. Actually, the final statement: 'لہذا عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے حانث تو نہیں ہوگا البتہ شریعت میں معنی حرمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے آزاد مطلقہ بائنہ کی عدت میں باندی سے نکاح حرام ہوگا' indicates the final ruling is prohibition. So Abu Hanifa's view is upheld. We'll state the mufta bihi as Abu Hanifa's view (prohibition) because it says 'اگرچہ حانث نہیں ہوگا مگر نکاح حرام ہوگا' meaning the marriage itself is haram even though the oath is not broken. That is the conclusion of the commentary.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): A final divorce that separates the couple completely; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage.
من وجه (min wajh): In some respects or aspects; used to indicate that something remains partially.
تزوج عليها (tazawwuj 'alayha): Marrying another woman over an existing wife (collecting them in marriage).

In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position follows Abu Hanifa: marrying a slave woman during the 'iddah of a free woman divorced with ba'in talaq is haram.

Nikah — Marriage

Validity of a Slave Marriage When a Free Wife Is Present: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i-Muzani
Inter-madhhab dispute on slave marriage validity with free wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a slave marriage remains valid upon marrying a free woman and evaluate the Shafi'i-Muzani counter-argument based on analogy to tayammum.

Core Idea
A slave marriage remains valid even after marrying a free woman – the hadith and principle of complete lawfulness override analogy.

This passage presents a classical inter-madhhab dispute: whether a free man who marries a slave woman and later marries a free woman has his first marriage invalidated. The Hanafi school, along with the majority of Imams, affirms the continued validity of the slave marriage. Imam Muzani of the Shafi'i school argues that the slave marriage becomes invalid by analogy to tayammum ending when water appears. We will examine both positions and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the status of a slave marriage when a free wife later enters the marriage.
The Hanafi position is that the marriage remains valid and is not invalidated.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize Imam Muzani of the Shafi'i school and his claim that the slave marriage becomes invalid upon marriage to a free woman.
Muzani's view is based on the idea that the original permission was conditional on inability to marry a free woman.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Muzani's reasoning: he uses an analogy (qiyas) to tayammum – just as tayammum breaks when water appears, so the slave marriage ends when ability to marry a free woman is realized.
This is a qiyas from the permission for slave marriage being similar to the permission for tayammum.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi refutation: first, a direct prophetic hadith permits retaining the slave marriage; second, the analogy fails because a free woman's lawfulness is complete and not diminished by the presence of a slave co-wife, whereas a slave woman's lawfulness is inherently half due to slavery.
The hadith takes precedence over analogy, and the rational proof shows the disanalogy between tayammum and slave marriage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
See the practical consequence: under Hanafi, a man can remain married to both; under Muzani's view, the slave marriage must be renewed if the man wants to continue it.
The difference affects the validity of the slave marriage in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكات ۴۳ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم میں کوئی قباحت نہیں اور ائمہ اربعہ اس پر متفق ہیں کہ باندی کا نکاح باطل بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن شوافع میں سے امام مزنی فرماتے ہیں کہ آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرتے ہی باندی کا نکاح باطل ہو جائے گا طول حرہ پر قدرت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ باندی سے جواز نکاح عدم قدرت علی الحرہ کی وجہ سے تھا پس یہ آب آمد تیم برخاست کے قبیل سے ہو گا۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد کہ آزاد عورت کو نکاح میں لا سکتا ہے باندی کے رہتے ہوئے۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرہ محلات میں سے ہے تمام حالتوں میں حالت انفراد میں بھی اور حالت انضمام میں بھی کیوں کہ حرہ کے حق میں کوئی ایسی چیز نہیں پائی گئی جوحل محلیت کو آدھی کر دے بخلاف باندی کے کہ اس کے حق میں منصف یعنی رقیت موجود ہے۔
There is no objection in this and the four Imams are agreed that the marriage of a slave woman is not invalidated. But among the Shafi'is, Imam Muzani says that as soon as one marries a free woman, the marriage of the slave woman becomes invalid because of the ability to marry a free woman; since the permissibility of marrying a slave woman was due to inability to marry a free woman, so this is like the case of water appearing and tayammum breaking. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم that one can marry a free woman while having a slave woman. The second rational proof is that a free woman is a lawful partner in all states, both alone and in combination, because there is nothing found in her case that halves her lawfulness, unlike the slave woman where the half (slavery) exists.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Muzani of the Shafi'i school. The core issue is whether the marriage of a slave woman remains valid after her free husband marries a free woman. The Hanafis, along with the other three Imams, hold that the slave marriage remains valid. Imam Muzani argues that since the original permission to marry a slave woman was conditional on inability to marry a free woman, once that inability disappears (by marrying a free woman), the slave marriage should be invalidated, similar to how tayammum breaks when water becomes available. The Hanafi response is based on two proofs: first, a prophetic hadith stating that one can marry a free woman while retaining a slave wife; second, rational reasoning that a free woman's lawfulness as a spouse is complete and not diminished by the presence of a slave co-wife, while a slave woman's lawfulness is inherently half due to her slavery. Therefore, the marriage of the slave woman remains intact.

Key Terms
باندی (bāndī): A female slave (amah) who is owned by a master.
حرہ (ḥurrah): A free woman who is not a slave.
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a free man marries a slave woman and later marries a free woman, what is the status of the first marriage to the slave woman?
A) It becomes invalid automatically.
B) It remains valid and both marriages are upheld.
C) It becomes temporarily suspended until the free marriage ends.
D) It is nullified only if the free woman objects.

Key Takeaway
A slave marriage remains valid even after the husband marries a free woman, because the hadith and the principle of complete lawfulness of the free wife override the analogy to tayammum.

Marrying a Slave Woman During a Free Woman's Bain Iddah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on marrying a slave during a free woman's bain iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on marrying a slave woman during a free woman's bain iddah, explain their respective proofs, and apply the ruling to a comparable scenario.

Core Idea
After a bain divorce, remaining iddah effects can still prohibit a new marriage — caution vs literal dissolution.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi debate: does the iddah period after an irrevocable divorce retain enough marriage effects to prevent a man from marrying a slave woman? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that caution requires prohibiting it, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider it permissible. The dispute turns on the interpretation of what constitutes "marrying over her" and the role of custom versus legal meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What is the legal status of marrying a slave woman during the iddah of a free woman after a bain divorce?
Note the focus is on a slave woman, not a free woman.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
State Abu Hanifa's view (impermissible) and the Sahibayn's view (permissible). Recognize this as an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
Both positions are recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue: the marriage is fully dissolved by bain divorce, so there is no 'marrying over her'. They support this with an oath example.
If one swears not to marry over her, then divorces bain and marries a slave, the oath is not broken.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that some legal effects of marriage (nafaqah, suknah) remain during iddah, so the prohibition continues out of caution. He distinguishes oaths (follow custom) from legal rulings (follow underlying meaning).
The remaining effects are not full marriage ties but are significant enough to preserve the prohibition.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: according to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is invalid; according to Sahibayn, it is valid. Note the tarjih tendency toward Abu Hanifa's caution.
The fatwa may differ based on circumstances and later Hanafi preferences.

گا۔ پس جب اس کو طلاق بائن دیدی تو اس کی باری باقی ہی نہیں رہی، چنانچہ اب عدت بائن میں اگر دوسری عورت سے نکاح کر لیا تو اس کی باری میں شریک کرنا نہیں پایا جائے گا لہذا حانث بھی نہیں ہو گا۔
If he marries a slave woman over a free woman during the iddah of a divorc bain, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but it is permissible according to them (the two companions). Because this is not a 'marriage over her' which is prohibited. For this reason, if he swore not to marry over her, he would not be breaking his oath. According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage of the free woman remains in some respects due to the remaining of some rulings, so the prohibition remains out of caution, unlike the oath because the intent is not to bring another into her turn.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the permissibility of marrying a slave woman during the iddah of a free woman who has been given a divorc bain. The key issue is whether the remaining effects of the original marriage (such as nafaqah and housing during iddah) are sufficient to prohibit a new marriage with a slave woman. The Sahibayn argue that since the marriage ties are severed by the bain divorce, there is no 'marriage over her' which is the prohibited act. They support their view with an oath example: if a man swears not to marry over her, then divorces her bain and marries a slave woman, he does not break his oath because customary understanding does not consider it as marrying over her. Abu Hanifa responds by emphasizing that although the marriage is dissolved, some legal effects remain during iddah, so out of caution the prohibition should continue. The text then provides a detailed commentary reconciling the positions, noting that in oaths custom is considered, but in legal rulings the underlying meaning of remaining marital ties is considered, leading to prohibition in the viewed ruling.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bāʾin): A divorce that irrevocably severs the marriage ties, as opposed to raj'i revocable divorce.
عدت (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.
تزوج علی الحرہ (tazwij ʿalā al-ḥurrah): Marrying another woman over an existing free wife, which is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The remaining effects of a bain divorce during iddah can trigger the prohibition of marrying over a free woman according to Abu Hanifa, highlighting the role of caution in Hanafi fiqh.

The Maximum Number of Wives for a Free Man: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the permissible number of wives for a free man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissible number of wives (including slave women) and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
A free man may marry up to four wives, whether free or slave — the general Quranic text overrides necessity-based restrictions.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: how many wives, particularly slave women, may a free man marry simultaneously? The Hanafi school holds that the Quranic permission for up to four wives applies equally to free and slave women, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that marrying a slave woman is only a necessity-based concession limited to one. Understanding this dispute clarifies the principles of textual interpretation (amm vs. khass) and the role of necessity (darura) in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a free man may marry up to four wives, including slave women, based on Quran 4:3 and the hadith of Ghilan ibn Salama.
The total number of wives (free or slave) cannot exceed four.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i allows only one slave wife, reasoning that marrying a slave is a necessity-based concession (like eating carrion), limited to the minimum needed.
Necessity here is defined as inability to afford a free wife.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the Hanafi response: the Quranic word 'women' (nisa) includes both free and slave women, so the general permission applies. The analogy to carrion is rejected because the permission for slave marriage is not conditioned on dire necessity.
The text also rejects extremist views (Rafidah allowing nine, Khawarij allowing eighteen).
4
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: a Hanafi may take up to four slave wives (within the total), while a Shafi'i may take only one.
This difference impacts fatwa in historical contexts where slavery existed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کہ ظہار میں۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے تعدد ازواج کے بارے میں جو اختلاف تھا اس کو بالدلائل بیان فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ احناف کے نزدیک آزاد مرد بیک وقت چار عورتوں سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے چاروں آزاد ہوں یا چاروں باندی یا بعض آزاد اور بعض باندی ہوں۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس جز میں اختلاف ہے کہ اگر باندی سے نکاح کرے تو صرف ایک باندی سے کر سکتا ہے زائد سے نہیں۔ روافض نو (۹) تک کی اجازت دیتے ہیں اور خوارج اٹھارہ تک کی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے پہلے ان حضرات کی دلیل کو بیان فرمایا جو چار کی اجازت دیتے ہیں۔ دلیل میں آیت پیش کی ہے یہ آیت بیان عدد میں نص ہے اور عدد کی صراحت زیادتی کیلئے مانع ہے۔ لہذا چار سے زائد عورتیں ایک مرد آزاد کیلئے حلال نہیں ہوں گی۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک آیت میں لفظ وا داد کے معنی میں ہے جو تخییر کے لئے ہے۔ اب مطلب ہوگا کہ ان اعداد میں سے کوئی بھی عدد اختیار کر لو دو کا یا تین کا یا چار کا سب درست ہیں ۔ روافض نے واؤ کو جمع کیلئے مانا اور تینوں اعداد کو جمع کر کے نو کی اجازت دیدی۔ خوارج نے کہا کہ منی وثلث ورباع میں تکرار کے معنی ہیں چنانچہ منی کے معنی ہیں دو، ثلث کے معنی ہیں تین تین، رباع کے معنی ہیں چار چار۔ ان سب کو جمع کیا جائے تو اٹھارہ ہو جاتے ہیں، لہذا انہوں نے اٹھارہ عورتوں سے نکاح کی اجازت دیدی۔ بعد کے یہ دونوں قول لغو ہیں۔ ان کی طرف التفات نہ کیا جائے ۔ مذہب حق کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جسکو تر مندی نے نقل کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے کہ غیلان بن سلمہ اسلام لایا تو اس کے پاس دس عور تیں تھیں پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حکم دیا کہ ان میں سے چار چھانٹ لے اور باقی چھوڑ دے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی سے نکاح ضرورہ ثابت ہے لہذا ابقدر ضرورت ہی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ اور ضرورت پوری ہو جاتی ہے ایک باندی سے۔ لہذا ایک سے زائد باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ ضرورت میں مردار کو حلال کیا گیا، لہذائر دار اتنی مقدار حلال ہوگا جس سے زندہ رہ سکے، پیٹ بھر کر یا طالب لذت بن کر کھانا حرام ہے۔ لیکن ہم نے جو آیت پیش کی ہے وہ امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہوگی ، کیونکہ آیت میں لفظ نساء مذکور ہے اور لفظ نساء جس طرح آزاد کو شامل ہے اسی طرح امتہ منکوحہ کو بھی شامل ہے جیسا کہ
For a free man, he may marry four free women or slave women, and he may not marry more than that, due to the saying of Allah: 'marry what seems good to you of women, two, three, or four.' And specification of the number forbids increase beyond it. Al-Shafi'i said: he may only marry one slave woman, because according to him it is based on necessity. The proof against him is what we have recited, because the married slave woman is included in the word 'women' as in zihar.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the maximum number of wives a free man can have, particularly concerning slave women. The Hanafi school, based on the Quranic verse (4:3) which allows up to four wives, holds that a free man can marry up to four women, whether free or slave. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a slave wife is only permissible out of necessity, so only one slave wife is allowed, analogizing to the permissibility of eating carrion in necessity—only enough to survive. The Hanafi response is that the Quranic word 'women' (nisa) includes both free and slave women, as seen in the context of zihar (a form of divorce). The text also mentions deviant views: Rafidah allowed up to nine, Khawarij up to eighteen, but these are rejected. The correct view is supported by a hadith from Tirmidhi where the Prophet ordered Ghilan ibn Salama to keep only four of his ten wives upon embracing Islam. The passage thus establishes the Hanafi position that a free man may marry up to four wives, including slave women, and that the Shafi'i limitation to one slave wife is untenable due to the general application of the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
آزاد (āzād): A free man (not a slave).
باندی (bāndī): A female slave (amah).
ضرورت (żarūrat): Necessity; a legal concept that permits otherwise prohibited acts under duress.
نساء (nisa'): Women; the Quranic term used in verse 4:3.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Free Man May Marry Up to Four Women, Free or Slave
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum number of slave wives a free man may marry and explain the Quranic evidence and the response to the Shafi'i dispute.

Core Idea
A free man may marry up to four women, free or slave, because the Quran's 'nisa' includes both and the count is explicit.

The Hanafi school permits a free man to marry up to four wives, whether free or slave, based on the general wording of Quran 4:3. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts slave wives to one, viewing their marriage as a necessity. This lesson examines the evidence from both sides and the Hanafi rebuttal using linguistic analogy from the verse on zihar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a free man may marry up to four women, and these may include free women, slave women, or a mix, as long as the total does not exceed four.
The ruling is derived from Quran 4:3 and supported by hadith.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a free man may marry only one slave woman. He considers marrying a slave woman a necessity, so only one suffices.
Shafi'i bases his view on qiyas with carrion in necessity.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: since slave marriage is a necessity, it is limited to the minimum required, just as carrion is only permitted to save life, not for pleasure.
The analogy rests on the concept of necessity (darura).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts by pointing to the Quranic word 'nisa' (women) in 4:3, which linguistically includes both free and slave women. This is confirmed by the verse on zihar (58:3) where 'nisa' clearly includes slave wives.
The Hanafi response uses a textual proof (dalil naqli) from the Quran itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi free man may marry multiple slave wives (up to four total), while a Shafi'i free man may marry only one slave wife.
This difference affects actual marriage contracts and family structure.

وللحران يتزوج اربعا من الحرائر و الاماء و ليس له ان يتزوج اكثر من ذلك لقوله تعالى فانكحوا ما طاب لكم من النساء مثنى وثالث ورباع والتنصيص على العدد يمنع الزيادة عليه وقال الشافعي لا يتزوج الا امة واحدة لأنه ضرورى عنده والحجة عليه ماتلونا اذ الامة المنكوحة ينتظمها اسم النساء كما في الظهار ترجمه آزاد مرد کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ نکاح کرے چار عورتوں سے آزاد ہوں یا باندی اور جائز نہیں اس کیلئے کہ وہ اس سے زائد سے نکاح کرے باری تعالیٰ کے قول فانكحوا ... الآیه کی وجہ سے یعنی نکاح کرو ان سے جو عور تیں تم کو بھلی لگیں دو دو سے تین تین سے چار چار ہے۔ اور عدد کی صراحت اس پر زیادتی کو منع کرتی ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ نہ نکاح کرے مگر ایک باندی سے اس لئے کہ باندی کا نکاح ان کے نزدیک ضرورۃ ثابت ہے۔ اور حجت امام شافعی کے خلاف وہ آیت ہے جو ہم نے تلاوت کی اس لئے کہ امتہ منکوحہ کو لفظ نساء شامل ہے جیسا کہ ظہار میں۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے تعدد ازواج کے بارے میں جو اختلاف تھا اس کو بالدلائل بیان فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ احناف کے نزدیک آزاد مرد بیک وقت چار عورتوں سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے چاروں آزاد ہوں یا چاروں باندی یا بعض آزاد اور بعض باندی ہوں۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس جز میں اختلاف ہے کہ اگر باندی سے نکاح کرے تو صرف ایک باندی سے کر سکتا ہے زائد سے نہیں۔ روافض نو (۹) تک کی اجازت دیتے ہیں اور خوارج اٹھارہ تک کی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے پہلے ان حضرات کی دلیل کو بیان فرمایا جو چار کی اجازت دیتے ہیں۔ دلیل میں آیت پیش کی ہے یہ آیت بیان عدد میں نص ہے اور عدد کی صراحت زیادتی کیلئے مانع ہے۔ لہذا چار سے زائد عورتیں ایک مرد آزاد کیلئے حلال نہیں ہوں گی۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک آیت میں لفظ وا داد کے معنی میں ہے جو تخییر کے لئے ہے۔ اب مطلب ہوگا کہ ان اعداد میں سے کوئی بھی عدد اختیار کر لو دو کا یا تین کا یا چار کا سب درست ہیں ۔ روافض نے واؤ کو جمع کیلئے مانا اور تینوں اعداد کو جمع کر کے نو کی اجازت دیدی۔ خوارج نے کہا کہ منی وثلث ورباع میں تکرار کے معنی ہیں چنانچہ منی کے معنی ہیں دو، ثلث کے معنی ہیں تین تین، رباع کے معنی ہیں چار چار۔ ان سب کو جمع کیا جائے تو اٹھارہ ہو جاتے ہیں، لہذا انہوں نے اٹھارہ عورتوں سے نکاح کی اجازت دیدی۔ بعد کے یہ دونوں قول لغو ہیں۔ ان کی طرف التفات نہ کیا جائے ۔ مذہب حق کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جسکو تر مندی نے نقل کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے کہ غیلان بن سلمہ اسلام لایا تو اس کے پاس دس عور تیں تھیں پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حکم دیا کہ ان میں سے چار چھانٹ لے اور باقی چھوڑ دے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی سے نکاح ضرورہ ثابت ہے لہذا ابقدر ضرورت ہی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ اور ضرورت پوری ہو جاتی ہے ایک باندی سے۔ لہذا ایک سے زائد باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ ضرورت میں مردار کو حلال کیا گیا، لہذائر دار اتنی مقدار حلال ہوگا جس سے زندہ رہ سکے، پیٹ بھر کر یا طالب لذت بن کر کھانا حرام ہے۔ لیکن ہم نے جو آیت پیش کی ہے وہ امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہوگی ، کیونکہ آیت میں لفظ نساء مذکور ہے اور لفظ نساء جس طرح آزاد کو شامل ہے اسی طرح امتہ منکوحہ کو بھی شامل ہے جیسا کہ کفارہ ظہار کے موقع پر فرمایا اللذين يظاهرون من نسائھم ۔ یہاں نساء سے آزاد اور باندی دونوں مراد ہیں چنانچہ آزاد بیوی سے ظہار کر لیا تب بھی کفارہ ظہار واجب ہے اور امتہ منکوحہ سے ظہار کیا تب بھی کفارہ ظہار لا زم ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And for the free man, it is permissible that he marry four from free women and slave women, and it is not permissible for him to marry more than that because of the saying of the Exalted: 'Then marry what seems good to you of women, two and three and four' (4:3). Specification of the number prevents increase upon it. And al-Shafi'i said: He should not marry except one slave woman because it is a necessity according to him. And the proof against him is what we have recited, for the slave woman who is married is included in the word 'women' (nisa') as in the case of zihar. Translation: It is permissible for a free man to marry four women, whether free or slave, and it is not permissible for him to marry more than that due to the verse 'fankihu...' i.e., marry the women that please you, two by two, three by three, four by four. The specification of the number prevents increase. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He should not marry except one slave woman because marrying a slave woman is established only by necessity according to him. And the proof against Imam al-Shafi'i is the verse we recited, because the married slave woman is included in the word 'women' (nisa'), as in the case of zihar. Commentary: In this expression, the author has explained with proofs the difference of opinion concerning plurality of wives. Thus, according to the Hanafis, a free man may marry four women at one time, all free, all slave, or some free and some slave. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the difference is in this part: if one marries a slave woman, he may marry only one slave woman, not more. The Rawafid permit up to nine, and the Khawarij permit up to eighteen. The author of al-Hidayah first mentioned the proof of those who permit four. The verse is cited as evidence; this verse is explicit in specifying the number, and specification of the number prevents increase. Therefore, more than four women are not permissible for a free man. According to these scholars, the 'waw' in the verse is for takhyir (choice). So the meaning is: choose any of these numbers, two or three or four, all are valid. The Rawafid took the 'waw' as for conjunction and combined the three numbers to permit nine. The Khawarij said that 'mathna, thulath, ruba' indicate repetition, so mathna means two each, thulath means three each, ruba means four each; summing these gives eighteen, so they permitted eighteen. Both these opinions are baseless; no attention should be paid to them. The true school is also supported by the hadith transmitted by al-Tirmidhi: Ghaylan ibn Salamah embraced Islam and he had ten wives, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded him to select four and divorce the rest. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that marriage with a slave woman is established by necessity, so only as much marriage as is necessary is permissible. Necessity is fulfilled by one slave woman, so marrying more than one slave woman is not permissible, just as carrion is made permissible in necessity only to the extent needed to stay alive; eating to fill the stomach or for pleasure is forbidden. However, the verse we have presented is a proof against Imam al-Shafi'i because the word 'nisa' (women) is mentioned in the verse, and the word 'nisa' includes free women and also the married slave woman, just as at the occasion of the expiation of zihar, Allah said: 'Those who make zihar to their wives (nisa')' (58:3). Here 'nisa' refers to both free and slave, so if one makes zihar to a free wife, expiation is obligatory, and if one makes zihar to a married slave woman, expiation also becomes obligatory. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a proof from the Quran and a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that a free man may marry up to four women, and these may be free, slave, or a mix, as long as the total does not exceed four. The primary proof is the Quranic verse (4:3) which explicitly limits to four, and the hadith of Ghaylan ibn Salamah where the Prophet ordered him to keep only four. Imam al-Shafi'i permits only one slave wife because he considers marrying a slave woman a necessity, like eating carrion in dire need. The Hanafi response is that the word 'women' (nisa') in the verse includes both free and slave women, as proven by the verse on zihar. The commentary also dismisses the opinions of the Rawafid (who allow nine) and Khawarij (who allow eighteen) as baseless. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
نساء (nisa'): Women; in this context, used generally to include both free women and slave women.
أمة (amah): A female slave who is lawful to marry.
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce where a husband compares his wife to his mother's back, requiring expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many slave women may a free man marry simultaneously?
A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
A free Hanafi man may marry up to four women, free or slave, because the Quran's term 'nisa' includes both and the numerical limit is explicit and binding.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Slave's Marriage Limit and Bain Divorce Effect on Wife Count
Ruling with proof for slave's marriage limit and dispute with Malik; also sub-issue on bain divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave may marry at most two wives, explain the qiyas proof based on the tanseef principle, and apply the rule that a bain divorce still occupies a wife-slot during iddah, thereby preventing a new marriage until the iddah expires.

Core Idea
Slavery halves blessings: a slave can only marry two; bain divorce does not clear the slot until iddah ends.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two connected issues: the maximum number of wives for a male slave, and the effect of a bain divorce on the count of wives for a free man. Both involve inter-madhhab disputes: Hanafis versus Malikis on the slave question, and Hanafis versus Shafi'is on the iddah occupation. The Hanafi positions rely on the principle that slavery halves entitlements and that iddah preserves marital occupancy. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings and the parties in dispute
The passage covers two separate but related rulings. First, the maximum wives for a slave: Hanafi says two, Maliki says four. Second, for a free man who gives a bain divorce: Hanafi says he must wait for iddah to marry a fourth; Shafi'i says he may marry immediately.
2
Slave marriage limit: follow the Hanafi qiyas
The Hanafi proof is a qiyas jali (clear analogy). The asl (original case) is the free man, who may marry four wives. The illa (effective cause) is the honor of freedom. Since slavery halves blessings, the slave's entitlement is half, i.e., two wives.
The principle 'al-raqq munassif' is central.
3
Examine the Maliki objection
Imam Malik argues that marriage is a human right unaffected by slavery. The Hanafi response is that slavery does affect legal capacity, as evidenced by ijma and the hadith of Umar.
The Maliki view is based on the human aspect, while Hanafis emphasize the legal limitation.
4
Bain divorce: understand the Hanafi view on iddah occupancy
According to the Hanafi school, even after a bain divorce, the woman remains in iddah. During this period, she is still considered one of the four wives for the purpose of the marriage count. Therefore, marrying a fourth before her iddah ends would effectively result in five wives.
This is based on the idea that iddah preserves the marital bond for certain legal effects.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that bain divorce severs the marriage entirely, so the iddah does not occupy a slot. Thus, a free man may marry a fourth immediately after issuing a bain divorce to one of his four wives.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a man can have five wives during the iddah period.

نے فرمایا کہ جائز ہے اس لئے کہ غلام نکاح کے حق میں آزاد کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک یہاں تک کہ نکاح کا مالک ہوگا بغیر مولی کی اجازت کے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے که رقیت تنصیف کر دینے والی ہے۔ چار میں سے ایک کو طلاق بائن دیدی تو اس کے لئے چوتھی سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گذر جائے۔ اور اس میں اختلاف ہے امام شافعی کا اور یہ نظیر ہے نکاح اخت فی عدت الاخت کی ۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں غلام کے لئے تعدد ازواج کا حکم بیان کیا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دو عورتوں سے نکاح جائز ہے زیادہ سے اجازت نہیں۔ امام مالک آزاد کی طرح غلام کے لئے بھی چار کی اجازت دیتے ہیں۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ نکاح کا اختیار ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بات پر سب کا اتفاق ہے کہ رقیت نعمتوں میں تنصیف کر دیتی ہے اور عورتوں کا حلال ہونا بھی اللہ کی طرف سے نعمت ہے لہذا اس نعمت میں بھی تنصیف ہوگی۔ پس جب آزاد کے
