بیبیاں حلال کی گئیں اور آزاد کا حال غلام کے حال سے اشرف ہے تو آزاد کے لئے چار اور غلام کے لئے دو حلال کی گئیں تا کہ شرف حریت کو ظاہر کیا جاسکے احناف کے مذہب کی تائید حدیث عمر سے بھی ہوتی ہے قال لا يتزوج العبد اكثر من اثنین اور عطاء نے صحابہ کرام کا اجماع نقل کیا ہے کہ غلام دو عورتوں سے زائد نہیں رکھ سکتا ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) لیکن اگر آپ اشکال کریں کہ فانكحوا ما طاب لكم آیت مطلق ہے آزاد اور غلام سب کو شامل ہے تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ اجماع ان الرق منصف سے آیت کو مقید کر دیا گیا۔ لہذا آیت صرف آزاد کو شامل ہوگی ، غلام کو نہیں۔ اس کے بعد مصنف نے یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا کہ اگر آزاد مرد نے اپنی چار بیویوں میں سے ایک کو طلاق بائن دیدی تو جبتک وہ مطلقہ بائنہ اپنی عدت نہ گزارے اس وقت تک یہ شخص چوتھی عورت سے شادی نہ کرے ورنہ اسکے نکاح میں پانچویں عورت جمع ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ چوتھی سے نکاح کرلے کیونکہ طلاق بائن کی وجہ سے وہ بالکلیہ زوجیت سے نکل گئی ۔ لہذا پانچ عورتوں کا جمع کرنا لازم
And it is not permissible for the slave to marry more than two. And Malik said it is permissible because in the matter of marriage he is like a free man according to him, to the extent that he owns [the right to marry] without the permission of the master. And our proof is that slavery halves [entitlements]. So the slave marries two and the free man four to manifest the honor of freedom. If a free man gives one of the four a bain divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth until her iddah expires, and there is a difference of opinion with al-Shafi'i, and this is analogous to marrying a sister during the iddah of a sister... Translation: It is not permissible for a slave to marry more than two women. Imam Malik said it is permissible because the slave is, in the matter of marriage, like a free man according to him, to the extent that he may even own the right to marry without the master's permission. And our proof is that slavery halves [entitlements]. So the slave marries two and the free man four to manifest the honor of freedom. If a free man gives one of the four a bain divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth until her iddah expires. And there is a difference of opinion with Imam al-Shafi'i, and this is analogous to marrying a sister during the iddah of a sister. Commentary: In this expression, the author has stated the ruling concerning plurality of wives for the slave. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible to marry two women, not more. Imam Malik permits four for the slave as for the free. Imam Malik's proof is that in marriage matters, the slave is like the free because marriage is among the properties of humanity, and slavery has no entry into humanity; all men are equal, free or slave. This is why the slave has the right to marry without the master's permission. Our proof is that there is consensus that slavery halves blessings, and the permissibility of women is a blessing from Allah, so this blessing is also halved. Thus, since four women are permissible for the free at one time, half of that, i.e., two women, are permissible for the slave. And if one reflects, indeed in the Shariah blessings differ in condition. Thus, the Prophet (peace be upon him) was the noblest in rank, so nine wives were made permissible for him; and the free man's condition is nobler than the slave's, so four are made permissible for the free and two for the slave to manifest the honor of freedom. The Hanafi school is also supported by the hadith of Umar: 'A slave should not marry more than two.' And Ata' reported the consensus of the Companions that a slave cannot have more than two women. But if you object that the verse 'fankihu ma taba lakum' is general, including both free and slave, we will respond that the consensus (that slavery halves) restricts the verse. Therefore, the verse applies only to the free, not the slave. After this, the author mentioned this ruling: if a free man gives one of his four wives a bain divorce, he should not marry a fourth woman until that divorced woman completes her iddah; otherwise, a fifth woman would be collected in his marriage. Imam al-Shafi'i says he may marry the fourth because due to bain divorce, she has completely left the marriage bond, so there is no collection of five.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings with disputes. First, the ruling on the maximum number of wives for a male slave: according to the Hanafi school, a slave may marry at most two women because slavery halves entitlements (the principle 'al-raqq munassif'). Imam Malik argues that the slave is like a free man in marriage, even allowing marriage without the master's permission. The Hanafi response is based on consensus and the principle that blessings are halved for slaves, and also on the hadith of Umar and the ijma of the Companions. The verse on marrying four (4:3) is interpreted as applying only to free men due to this restriction. Second, the sub-issue: if a free man gives one of his four wives a bain divorce, he cannot marry a fourth woman until the divorced woman's iddah expires, because otherwise he would effectively have five wives during the iddah period. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the bain divorce severs the marriage entirely, so no iddah occupation. The Hanafi view is that the iddah period counts the woman as part of the four, so a new marriage would result in five. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions are the Hanafi views.

Key Terms
رق (riqq): Slavery, a legal status that reduces certain rights and entitlements.
تنصیف (tanseef): Halving; the principle that a slave's entitlements are half of a free man's.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): An irrevocable divorce that severs the marriage tie immediately.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum number of wives a male slave may have at one time?
A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a slave may marry only two wives due to the halving effect of slavery, and a free man must wait for his divorced wife's iddah to expire before marrying a fourth after a bain divorce.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on a Slave's Number of Wives
Inter-madhhab dispute on slave's marriage limit with proof and sub-issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's maximum number of wives, explain the evidence from the hadith of Umar and ijma, and evaluate the Maliki and Shafi'i positions on the related issue.

Core Idea
Slavery halves the permissible number of wives: a slave may marry only two, while a free man may marry four.

This passage addresses a key issue in Hanafi marriage law: the limit on polygamy for slaves. The Hanafi school, relying on the principle that slavery halves legal capacities, holds that a slave may marry only two wives. This lesson will explore the Hanafi position, the opposing Maliki view, and the supporting evidence from hadith and ijma. It also covers a related ruling on the prohibition of remarrying after a final divorce until the 'iddah expires.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on a slave's marriage limit.
Identify the ruling: a slave may marry only two wives simultaneously. Note the hukm level (haram for more than two) and the underlying principle (al-raqq munassif).
This is the mufta bihi position supported by hadith and ijma.
2
Identify the opposing school and their evidence.
Imam Malik permits four wives for a slave, equating him to a free man in marriage matters. His evidence includes the general Quranic verse and the idea that marriage is a human right not diminished by slavery.
Maliki position is based on the unrestricted nature of the marriage contract.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: the halving principle and the hadith.
The Hanafi proof consists of: (1) The principle that slavery halves blessings, analogous to halving testimony and punishment. (2) The hadith of Umar (لا يتزوج العبد اكثر من اثنین) and the ijma of the Companions as narrated by Ata. Consider the strength of this evidence (hadith is ahad, thubut zanni, but dalala qati).
The hadith directly prohibits, and ijma reinforces.
4
Examine the sub-issue of talaq bain and remarriage before 'iddah.
If a free man divorces one of his four wives with a final divorce (talaq bain), he cannot marry a fourth woman until her 'iddah expires, otherwise he would have five wives simultaneously. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing the marriage bond is severed completely. Understand the analogy to marrying a sister during her sister's 'iddah.
This sub-issue illustrates how 'iddah maintains the count of wives even after divorce.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Under Hanafi law, a slave is limited to two wives; under Maliki, up to four. For the sub-issue, the difference is whether the 'iddah period counts toward the limit. Identify which position is mufta bihi and why.
The Hanafi view is supported by strong evidence and is the operative ruling for fatwa.

اس کے بعد مصنف نے یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا کہ اگر آزاد مرد نے اپنی چار بیویوں میں سے ایک کو طلاق بائن دیدی تو جبتک وہ مطلقہ بائنہ اپنی عدت نہ گزارے اس وقت تک یہ شخص چوتھی عورت سے شادی نہ کرے ورنہ اسکے نکاح میں پانچویں عورت جمع ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ چوتھی سے نکاح کرلے کیونکہ طلاق بائن کی وجہ سے وہ بالکلیہ زوجیت سے نکل گئی ۔ لہذا پانچ عورتوں کا جمع کرنا لازم نہیں آئیگا اور یہ نکاح الاخت فی عدت الاخت کی نظیر ہے جسکی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی۔
It is not permissible for a slave to marry more than two. Malik said: it is permissible because in matters of marriage he is like a free man in his view, even he can contract marriage without the master's permission. Our evidence is that slavery halves, so a slave marries two and a free man four, to manifest the honor of freedom. If a free man divorces one of the four with a final divorce (bain), it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth until her 'iddah expires. There is a difference of opinion with al-Shafi'i, and this is analogous to marrying a sister during the 'iddah of a sister. [Translation of the rest of the Urdu commentary follows similar patterns, explaining the proofs and disputes.]
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the maximum number of wives a slave may have simultaneously. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that a slave may marry only two wives. Imam Malik permits four, equating the slave with a free man in marriage matters. The Hanafi evidence is that slavery halves the permissible number of wives, just as it halves other legal capacities. This is supported by a narration from Umar (رضي الله عنه) that a slave should not marry more than two, and by the consensus of the Companions as narrated by Ata. The passage also discusses a related ruling: if a free man divorces one of his four wives with a final divorce, he cannot marry a fourth until that woman's 'iddah expires, otherwise he would have five wives simultaneously. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, arguing that since the divorce is final, the woman is no longer his wife, so he can marry a fourth immediately. The author analogizes this to the prohibition of marrying a sister during the 'iddah of her sister.

Key Terms
الرق منصف (al-raqq munassif): The principle that slavery halves certain legal rights and duties
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): A final divorce that severs the marital bond completely, unlike raj'i divorce
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a slave may marry only two wives, based on the halving principle and supported by hadith and ijma.

Marriage with a Woman Pregnant from Zina
Intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage to a woman pregnant from zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf on marrying a woman pregnant from zina, explain the evidence of each side, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A pregnancy from zina does not prevent marriage — the adulterer has no lineage rights to protect.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school: Can a man marry a woman who is pregnant from his own or another's zina? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule the marriage is valid, while Abu Yusuf considers it invalid. We will analyze their proofs, focusing on the concept of lineage rights and the effective cause (illa) in the original case of a lawful pregnancy.

Guided Path
1
State the act and the two positions
Identify the act (marriage to a woman pregnant from zina) and note the split: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad say jā'iz (valid) with prohibition of intercourse until delivery; Abu Yusuf says the marriage is fāsid (invalid).
The consensus case of pregnancy from a lawful husband (thābit al-nasab) is batil by consensus; distinguish it.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's qiyas
Abu Yusuf analogizes to a woman pregnant from a lawful marriage: both pregnancies are respected (the fetus committed no crime), so the same ruling of invalidity should apply. Identify the original case (asl) and the common illa (respect for the pregnancy).
The asl is the unanimous prohibition of marrying a woman with a lawful pregnancy.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the qiyas
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reject the analogy by distinguishing the illa: in the original case, the prohibition is due to the right of the lawful father (صاحب الماء), not mere respect. The adulterer has no such right, so the analogy fails.
This is a difference in how the illa is identified (tahrīr al-manāt).
4
Identify the direct textual evidence
The majority also cite the general permission of marriage (Quran: 'احل لكم ما وراء ذلكم'). Since a pregnant woman from zina is not among the explicitly prohibited categories, she is included in the general permission.
Textual authority (dalīl naqlī) overrides the qiyas in this view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The majority view (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The practical effect: the marriage is valid but intercourse must wait until delivery. Under Abu Yusuf's view, the marriage would need to be annulled.
Imam al-Shafi'i allows both marriage and intercourse immediately, but this is not the Hanafi position.

زنا سے حاملہ کے ساتھ نکاح کا حکم
قال وان تزوج حُبلى من زنا جاز النكاح ولا يطأها حتى تضع حملها وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف النكاح فاسد وان كان الحمل ثابت النسب فالنكاح باطل بالاجماع لابي يوسف ان الامتناع في الاصل لحرمة الحمل وهذا الحمل محترم لانه لا جناية منه ولهذا لم يجز اسقاطه ولهما انها من المحللات بالنص وحرمة الوطى كيلا يسقى ماؤه زرع غيره والامتناع فى ثابت النسب لحق صا. الماء ولا حرمة للزاني

تشریح زنا سے اگر کوئی عورت حاملہ ہوئی ہے تو اس سے جواز نکاح عدم جواز نکاح کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک نکاح جائز ہے البتہ وضع حمل تک وطی کرنا درست نہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نکاح ہی درست نہیں ہوا۔ اور امام شافعی جواز نکاح اور جواز ولی دونوں کے قائل ہیں اور اگر حمل ثابت النسب ہے مثلاً حاملہ معتدۃ الغیر ہے تو اس صورت میں نکاح باطل ہے بالا تفاق اور اگر کسی شخص نے کسی عورت سے زنا کیا وہ عورت اس سے حاملہ ہوگئی پھر اسی زانی سے نکاح کر لیا تو نکاح بھی جائز ہے اور ولی بھی حلال ہے بالا تفاق ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حمل اگر ثابت النسب ہے تو عدم جواز نکاح احترام حمل کی وجہ سے ہے اور حمل من الت نا بھی محترم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حمل کی طرف سے کوئی جنایت نہیں ۔ جنایت جو کچھ ہے زانی اور مزنیہ کیطرف سے ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ حمل کو ساقط کرنا نا جائز ہے، البتہ ہمارے زمانے میں ساقط کرنا جائز ہے ( حاشیہ ہدایہ ) پس جب اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ میں عدم جواز نکاح کی جو علت ہے وہی علت فرع یعنی مقیس میں بھی موجود ہے تو پھر مقیس میں بھی مقیس علیہ کا حکم لگا دیا جائے گا ، یعنی عدم جواز نکاح کا علت مشترکہ احترام حمل ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حاملہ من الزنا محلات میں سے ہے اور نص یعنی احل لکم ماوراء ذالکم سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ حاملہ من الزنا کا ذکر محرمات کے بیان میں نہیں کیا ہے اور جو محلات میں سے ہو اس کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ لہذا حاملہ من الزنا کے ساتھ بھی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر آپ کو یہ اشکال پیدا ہو جائے کہ حاملہ ثابت النسب کا ذکر بھی محرمات کے بیان میں نہیں ہے تو کیا وجہ ہے کہ اس کو احل لكم ما وراء ذالکم کے تحت داخل نہیں کیا گیا۔ اور حاملہ ثابت النسب سے نکاح کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا گیا۔ جواب، حاملہ ثابت
He said: And if a man marries a woman who is pregnant from zina, the marriage is valid, and he should not have intercourse with her until she delivers. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: the marriage is invalid (fasid). If the pregnancy is of established lineage (thabit al-nasab), then the marriage is invalid (batil) by consensus. Abu Yusuf's evidence: the prohibition in the original case (of marrying a pregnant woman from a lawful marriage) is due to respect for the pregnancy, and this pregnancy is also respected because it committed no crime; hence abortion is not allowed. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) evidence: she is among those made permissible by the text, and the prohibition of intercourse is to avoid mixing lineages. The prohibition in the case of established lineage is due to the right of the father of the child, and the adulterer has no respect. [The Urdu commentary further elaborates the reasons.]
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of marriage with a woman pregnant from zina. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that such a marriage is valid (jā'iz), though intercourse is prohibited until the woman gives birth. Abu Yusuf considers the marriage invalid (fāsid). The core of the dispute lies in the 'illa (effective cause) for prohibiting marriage with a pregnant woman in the primary case (a woman pregnant from a lawful husband): Abu Yusuf sees it as respect for the life of the fetus, which applies equally to a pregnancy from zina because the fetus is innocent. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that the prohibition in the primary case is to protect the lineage rights of the lawful father, and since the adulterer has no such rights, the marriage is permissible. They further cite the general permission of marriage (Quran 4:24) and note that a pregnant woman from zina is not explicitly excluded. The passage also clarifies that if the pregnancy is of established lineage (e.g., from a lawful husband, such as a woman in 'iddah from another man), marriage is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
حمل من زنا (haml min zina): Pregnancy resulting from unlawful sexual intercourse (zina)
حمل ثابت النسب (haml thābit al-nasab): Pregnancy attributed to a lawful father (e.g., from a valid marriage or 'iddah)
نكاح فاسد (nikāh fāsid): An irregular marriage that does not fulfill essential conditions but may be rectified or separated
مقیس علیہ (maqīs 'alayh): The original case in qiyas analogical reasoning
صاحب الماء (ṣāḥib al-mā'): The lawful father whose lineage right is protected

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling on marrying a woman who is pregnant from zina?
A) The marriage is invalid (bātil)
B) The marriage is valid (jā'iz) but intercourse must wait until delivery
C) The marriage is valid and intercourse is allowed immediately
D) The marriage is invalid (fāsid)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, marriage to a woman pregnant from zina is valid, but intercourse is delayed until birth; the adulterer has no lineage rights to protect.

Marriage with a Woman Pregnant from Zina: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage with a zina-pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with a woman pregnant from zina, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Marriage valid, intercourse haram until delivery — father's right, not pregnancy's sanctity, determines ruling.

The Hanafi school holds that marrying a woman pregnant from zina is valid, but sexual relations are strictly prohibited until delivery. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Yusuf dissents, arguing the marriage itself is invalid. We will analyze the proofs on both sides, focusing on qiyas and the identification of the effective cause ('illah).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
What is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad? (valid marriage, prohibited intercourse)
The marriage is sahih but intercourse is haram until delivery.
2
Identify the Opposing View
What does Abu Yusuf hold? (marriage is fasid)
He considers the contract invalid from the start.
3
Examine the Proofs
On what basis does each side argue? Abu Yusuf uses qiyas on established lineage; the majority uses general Quranic permission and the hadith prohibiting irrigating another's crop.
The key is the 'illah: sanctity of pregnancy vs right of the father.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
What practical difference does this ikhtilaf make? (validity of marriage vs immediate separation)
If valid, the woman becomes a wife with rights; if fasid, separation is required.

Source Text

كتاب النكاح
۴۶
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
نہیں آئیگا اور یہ نکاح الاخت فی عدت الاخت کی نظیر ہے جسکی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی۔
زنا سے حاملہ کے ساتھ نکاح کا حکم
قال وان تزوج حُبلى من زنا جاز النكاح ولا يطأها حتى تضع حملها وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف النكاح فاسد وان كان الحمل ثابت النسب فالنكاح باطل بالاجماع لابي يوسف ان الامتناع في الاصل لحرمة الحمل وهذا الحمل محترم لانه لا جناية منه ولهذا لم يجز اسقاطه ولهما انها من المحللات بالنص وحرمة الوطى كيلا يسقى ماؤه زرع غيره والامتناع فى ثابت النسب لحق صا. الماء ولا حرمة للزاني
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا ایسی عورت سے جو زنا سے حاملہ ہوئی ہے تو یہ نکاح جائز ہے اور اس سے وطی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ وضع حمل ہو جائے اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ نکاح فاسد ہے اور اگر حمل ثابت النسب ہے تو بالا تفاق نکاح باطل ہے۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل (مقیس علیہ ) میں نکاح سے رکنا احترام حمل کی وجہ سے ہے اور یہ عمل بھی محترم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس حمل کی طرف سے کوئی جنایت نہیں اور اسی وجہ سے اس کو ساقط کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حاملہ من الزنا محلات میں سے ہے، نص سے ثابت ہے۔ اور حرمت وطی اس لئے ہے تا کہ اس کا پانی اس کے غیر کی کھیتی کو سیراب نہ کرے اور ثابت النسب میں نکاح سے رکنا صاحب ماء کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اور زانی کا کوئی احترام نہیں۔
تشریح زنا سے اگر کوئی عورت حاملہ ہوئی ہے تو اس سے جواز نکاح عدم جواز نکاح کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک نکاح جائز ہے البتہ وضع حمل تک وطی کرنا درست نہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نکاح ہی درست نہیں ہوا۔ اور امام شافعی جواز نکاح اور جواز ولی دونوں کے قائل ہیں اور اگر حمل ثابت النسب ہے مثلاً حاملہ معتدۃ الغیر ہے تو اس صورت میں نکاح باطل ہے بالا تفاق اور اگر کسی شخص نے کسی عورت سے زنا کیا وہ عورت اس سے حاملہ ہوگئی پھر اسی زانی سے نکاح کر لیا تو نکاح بھی جائز ہے اور ولی بھی حلال ہے بالا تفاق ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حمل اگر ثابت النسب ہے تو عدم جواز نکاح احترام حمل کی وجہ سے ہے اور حمل من الت نا بھی محترم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حمل کی طرف سے کوئی جنایت نہیں ۔ جنایت جو کچھ ہے زانی اور مزنیہ کیطرف سے ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ حمل کو ساقط کرنا نا جائز ہے، البتہ ہمارے زمانے میں ساقط کرنا جائز ہے ( حاشیہ ہدایہ ) پس جب اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ میں عدم جواز نکاح کی جو علت ہے وہی علت فرع یعنی مقیس میں بھی موجود ہے تو پھر مقیس میں بھی مقیس علیہ کا حکم لگا دیا جائے گا ، یعنی عدم جواز نکاح کا علت مشترکہ احترام حمل ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حاملہ من الزنا محلات میں سے ہے اور نص یعنی احل لکم ماوراء ذالکم سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ حاملہ من الزنا کا ذکر محرمات کے بیان میں نہیں کیا ہے اور جو محلات میں سے ہو اس کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ لہذا حاملہ من الزنا کے ساتھ بھی نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر آپ کو یہ اشکال پیدا ہو جائے کہ حاملہ ثابت النسب کا ذکر بھی محرمات کے بیان میں نہیں ہے تو کیا وجہ ہے کہ اس کو احل لكم ما وراء ذالکم کے تحت داخل نہیں کیا گیا۔ اور حاملہ ثابت النسب سے نکاح کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا گیا۔ جواب، حاملہ ثابت النسب باری تعالیٰ کے قول ولا تعزموا عقدة النكاح حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجلہ کے تحت داخل ہے یعنی نہ ارادہ کرو نکاح کا یہاں تک کہ اپنی مقررہ عدت کی انتہا کو پہنچ جائے ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی عورت خاوند سے جدا ہوگئی تو جب تک عدت میں کسی کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ اس سے نکاح کرے۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے لہذا وضع حمل سے
پہلے نکاح نہ کرے ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) ۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ حاملہ من الزنا جب محلات میں سے ہے تو پھر وقوع نکاح کے بعد ولی کیوں حرام کی گئی ؟ جواب: - ولی اس لئے حرام کی گئی تا کہ اپنے پانی سے غیر کی کھیتی کو سیراب کرنالازم نہ آئے اس لئے کہ یہ حرام ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يسقى ماءه زرع غیرہ ۔ یعنی جو شخص اللہ اور یوم آخرت پر ایمان لائے وہ اپنے پانی سے اپنے غیر کی کھیتی کو سیراب نہ کرے، مراد یہ ہے کہ حوامل سے وطی نہ کرے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ تسلیم نہیں کہ فساد نکاح احترام حمل کی وجہ سے ہے بلکہ وہ صاحب ماء کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اور زانی کا کوئی احترام نہیں اس کے فعل حرام کا ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
If he marries a woman pregnant from zina, the marriage is valid and he shall not have intercourse with her until she delivers. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said the marriage is invalid. If the pregnancy is of established lineage, then the marriage is invalid by consensus. Abu Yusuf's proof: the prohibition in the original case is due to the sanctity of the pregnancy, and this pregnancy is also sacred because there is no crime from it, hence its abortion is not permitted. Their proof: she is from those permitted by the text, and the prohibition of intercourse is so that his water does not irrigate another's crop; the prohibition in case of established lineage is due to the right of the one whose water it is, and the fornicator has no sanctity.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on marrying a woman who is pregnant from zina. The positions: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the marriage is valid, but intercourse is prohibited until delivery. According to Abu Yusuf, the marriage itself is invalid (fasid). If the pregnancy is of established lineage (e.g., from a lawful husband or from a previous marriage where paternity is fixed), then all agree the marriage is invalid. The commentary explains the proofs: Abu Yusuf compares this case to the case of a pregnant woman with established lineage (which prohibits marriage due to sanctity of the pregnancy). He argues that the 'illa (effective cause) is the sanctity of the pregnancy, which exists in both cases. Therefore, the same ruling (invalidity) should apply. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the 'illa is not respect for the pregnancy but the right of the one who is the father. The fornicator has no such right, so the analogy fails. They rely on the general permission in the Quran (أحل لكم ما وراء ذلككم) and restrict intercourse only to avoid mixing lineages. The hadith of the Prophet (من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يسقى ماءه زرع غيره) is cited to prohibit intercourse but not the marriage itself. The passage also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i permits both the marriage and intercourse (since he considers the woman fully permissible as long as she is not in iddah). The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., marriage is valid but intercourse is haram until delivery.

Key Terms
حبلى من زنا (hubalā min zinā): A woman who is pregnant as a result of fornication/adultery.
ثابت النسب (thābit al-nasab): Pregnancy where the lineage of the child is legally established, such as from a lawful husband or from a previous marriage.
علت (‘illah): The effective cause or legal rationale that links the original case to the new case in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on marrying a woman pregnant from zina?
A) The marriage is invalid (fasid).
B) The marriage is valid but intercourse is prohibited until delivery.
C) The marriage is valid and intercourse is permissible immediately.
D) The marriage is suspended until the child is weaned.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the validity of the marriage contract and the permissibility of intercourse; marrying a woman pregnant from zina is valid but intercourse is haram until delivery to protect lineage.

Marriage with a Captive Pregnant Woman: The Ruling of Fasid
Ruling on marrying a pregnant captive woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a pregnant captive woman and explain why the marriage is fasid.

Core Idea
A marriage with a pregnant captive woman is fasid because her pregnancy has established lineage.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: if a man marries a woman taken captive from dar al-harb who is pregnant, the marriage is fasid (irregular). This ruling is based on the principle that the pregnancy has an established lineage (thabit al-nasab), and the four schools of law agree on this. Understanding this case helps clarify the boundaries of valid marriage and the importance of lineage certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying a pregnant woman who has been taken captive from enemy territory. The ruling is that the marriage is fasid (irregular).
Fasid means the contract is defective; it does not produce legal effects.
2
Understand the cause (illa)
The cause is that the pregnancy has established lineage (thabit al-nasab) from her previous husband. This makes the woman as if she is still in a marriage or iddah, thus the new marriage is invalid.
The lineage is from the harbi husband before captivity.
3
Recognize the consensus
The text states that the four schools of law agree on this ruling, indicating it is not a disputed matter.
Even though the woman is now a captive, her previous marriage's lineage is respected.
4
Contrast with other cases
This ruling applies specifically to a captive from dar al-harb. It does not apply to a woman whose pregnancy is from zina or whose pregnancy is from a Muslim husband in dar al-Islam.
If the pregnancy is from zina, the marriage is valid because there is no established lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قید ہو کر آنے والی حاملہ سے نکاح کا حکم
فان تزوج حاملا من السبى فالنكاح فاسد لانه ثابت النسب وان زوج ام ولده وهي حامل منه فالنكاح باطل لانها فراش لمولاها حتى يثبت نسب ولدها منه من غير دعوة فلو صح النكاح لحصل الجمع بين الفراشين الا انه غير متأكد حتى ينتفى الولد بالنفى من غير لعان فلا يعتبر مالم يتصل به الحمل ترجمہ . پس اگر نکاح کیا ایسی حاملہ سے جو دار الحرب سے گرفتار ہو کر آئی ہے تو نکاح فاسد ہے اس لئے کہ یہ حمل ثابت النسب ہے اور اگر نکاح کیا اپنی ام ولد کا ( کسی دوسرے سے ) اور حال یہ کہ وہ حاملہ ہے مولیٰ سے تو نکاح باطل ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کی فراش ہے حتی کہ اس کے ولد کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا مولیٰ سے بغیر دعوای نسب کے۔ پس اگر نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو جمع بین الفراشین حاصل ہوگا مگر یہ کہ وہ غیر قوی ہے یہاں تک کہ ولد منتفی ہو جائے گا نفی کر دینے سے، بغیر لعان کے پس نہیں معتبر ہو گا جب تک کہ اس کے ساتھ
حمل متصل نہ ہو ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایسی عورت سے نکاح کیا جو دار الحرب سے گرفتار کر کے لائی گئی ہے اور وہ حاملہ ہے تو نکاح فاسد ہوگا۔ آئمہ اربعہ کا اس پر اتفاق ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کے شوہر حربی سے اسکے عمل کا نسب ثابت ہے اور ثابت النسب سے نکاح فاسد
ہوتا ہے۔
دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کی ام ولد حاملہ ہے اسی کے پانی سے۔ پھر مولیٰ نے اس ام ولد کا کسی دوسرے سے نکاح کر دیا تو یہ نکاح باطل ہے کیونکہ یہ ام ولد اپنے مولیٰ کی فراش ہے۔ چنانچہ اس کے والد کا نسب مولیٰ سے بغیر دعوی نسب کے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے ۔اب اگرام ولد کے نکاح کو درست قرار دیدیا جائے تو جمع بین الفراشین لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ مولیٰ کی فراش ہے ام ولد ہونے کہ وجہ سے اور
شوہر کی فراش ہوگی نکاح کی وجہ سے اور جمع بین الفراشین باطل ہے کیونکہ جمع بین الفراشین کی صورت میں نسب مشتبہ ہو جائے گا۔
If he marries a woman pregnant from captivity (sabi), the marriage is fasid because her pregnancy is of established lineage. And if he marries his own umm walad while she is pregnant from him, the marriage is batil because she is the firash of her master; her child's lineage is established without claim. So if the marriage were valid, it would result in combining two beds (firashayn), except that it is not strong; even if the child is repudiated by disavowal without li'an, it is not considered unless the pregnancy is connected.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings regarding pregnant women in specific situations. First: If a man marries a woman who was taken captive from dar al-harb (enemy territory) and she is pregnant, the marriage is fasid (invalid). This is because the pregnancy is of established lineage (thabit al-nasab) from her former husband, and consensus of the four schools holds that marriage to a woman with established lineage is invalid. Second: If a man (master) marries his own umm walad (a slave who has borne him a child) to another man while she is pregnant from him, such a marriage is batil (void). The reasoning is that the umm walad is considered the master's firash (bed/marriage-like relationship) such that the child's lineage is automatically established to the master without need for a claim. If the marriage to another man were valid, it would create a conflict between two firashes (the master's and the husband's), which is impermissible because it would cause confusion of lineage. The text notes that this second marriage is batil, not merely fasid, because of the stronger connection. The passage also mentions that even if the husband disavows the child, it is not effective unless the pregnancy is connected to him, but this is a nuanced point. The overall ruling: marriage with a woman whose pregnancy is of established lineage is fasid, and marriage of an umm walad pregnant by her master to another man is batil.

Key Terms
سبی (sabī): Captive taken from dar al-harb (enemy territory).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on marrying a pregnant woman taken captive from dar al-harb according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid
B) Fasid
C) Batil
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Marrying a pregnant captive woman is fasid because her pregnancy has established lineage, making her ineligible for marriage until the iddah ends.

Marriage of a Pregnant Umm Walad to Another Man: Batil
Ruling on marrying a pregnant umm walad to another man.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a master's marriage of his pregnant umm walad to another man is batil (void) and how the concept of firash prevents this.

Core Idea
An umm walad is her master's firash; marrying her to another is batil because it combines two conflicting beds.

This lesson addresses a different but related scenario: a master arranges a marriage for his own umm walad (a slave who has borne him a child) while she is pregnant from him. The Hanafi school rules this marriage as batil (void), not merely fasid. The key concept is that the umm walad is considered the master's 'firash' (marriage bed) such that her child's lineage is automatically attributed to the master without need for a claim. Any attempt to create a second marriage bed would lead to confusion of lineage (jam' bayn al-firashayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a master contracting the marriage of his own pregnant umm walad to another man. The ruling is that the marriage is batil (void ab initio).
Batil means the contract has no legal effect at all.
2
Understand the reasoning: the concept of firash
The umm walad is the master's firash because she has borne his child, establishing a bond of paternity. This gives the master exclusive rights regarding paternity.
Firash is not the same as marriage; it is a status that prevents others from claiming paternity.
3
Recognize the consequence: jam' bayn al-firashayn
If the marriage were valid, the woman would have two firashes: one from the master (through the child) and one from the husband (through marriage). This combination is impermissible because it causes uncertainty of paternity.
The text says the prohibition is strong, and even disavowal without li'an does not resolve it unless the pregnancy is not connected.
4
Distinguish from the first case
In the first case (captive pregnant woman), the marriage was fasid due to established lineage but not batil, because the woman's prior bond was not as strong as an umm walad's firash.
The umm walad's connection is stronger, making the marriage batil.

قید ہو کر آنے والی حاملہ سے نکاح کا حکم
فان تزوج حاملا من السبى فالنكاح فاسد لانه ثابت النسب وان زوج ام ولده وهي حامل منه فالنكاح باطل لانها فراش لمولاها حتى يثبت نسب ولدها منه من غير دعوة فلو صح النكاح لحصل الجمع بين الفراشين الا انه غير متأكد حتى ينتفى الولد بالنفى من غير لعان فلا يعتبر مالم يتصل به الحمل ترجمہ . پس اگر نکاح کیا ایسی حاملہ سے جو دار الحرب سے گرفتار ہو کر آئی ہے تو نکاح فاسد ہے اس لئے کہ یہ حمل ثابت النسب ہے اور اگر نکاح کیا اپنی ام ولد کا ( کسی دوسرے سے ) اور حال یہ کہ وہ حاملہ ہے مولیٰ سے تو نکاح باطل ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کی فراش ہے حتی کہ اس کے ولد کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا مولیٰ سے بغیر دعوای نسب کے۔ پس اگر نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو جمع بین الفراشین حاصل ہوگا مگر یہ کہ وہ غیر قوی ہے یہاں تک کہ ولد منتفی ہو جائے گا نفی کر دینے سے، بغیر لعان کے پس نہیں معتبر ہو گا جب تک کہ اس کے ساتھ
حمل متصل نہ ہو ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایسی عورت سے نکاح کیا جو دار الحرب سے گرفتار کر کے لائی گئی ہے اور وہ حاملہ ہے تو نکاح فاسد ہوگا۔ آئمہ اربعہ کا اس پر اتفاق ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کے شوہر حربی سے اسکے عمل کا نسب ثابت ہے اور ثابت النسب سے نکاح فاسد
ہوتا ہے۔
دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کی ام ولد حاملہ ہے اسی کے پانی سے۔ پھر مولیٰ نے اس ام ولد کا کسی دوسرے سے نکاح کر دیا تو یہ نکاح باطل ہے کیونکہ یہ ام ولد اپنے مولیٰ کی فراش ہے۔ چنانچہ اس کے والد کا نسب مولیٰ سے بغیر دعوی نسب کے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے ۔اب اگرام ولد کے نکاح کو درست قرار دیدیا جائے تو جمع بین الفراشین لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ مولیٰ کی فراش ہے ام ولد ہونے کہ وجہ سے اور
شوہر کی فراش ہوگی نکاح کی وجہ سے اور جمع بین الفراشین باطل ہے کیونکہ جمع بین الفراشین کی صورت میں نسب مشتبہ ہو جائے گا۔
If he marries a woman pregnant from captivity (sabi), the marriage is fasid because her pregnancy is of established lineage. And if he marries his own umm walad while she is pregnant from him, the marriage is batil because she is the firash of her master; her child's lineage is established without claim. So if the marriage were valid, it would result in combining two beds (firashayn), except that it is not strong; even if the child is repudiated by disavowal without li'an, it is not considered unless the pregnancy is connected.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings regarding pregnant women in specific situations. First: If a man marries a woman who was taken captive from dar al-harb (enemy territory) and she is pregnant, the marriage is fasid (invalid). This is because the pregnancy is of established lineage (thabit al-nasab) from her former husband, and consensus of the four schools holds that marriage to a woman with established lineage is invalid. Second: If a man (master) marries his own umm walad (a slave who has borne him a child) to another man while she is pregnant from him, such a marriage is batil (void). The reasoning is that the umm walad is considered the master's firash (bed/marriage-like relationship) such that the child's lineage is automatically established to the master without need for a claim. If the marriage to another man were valid, it would create a conflict between two firashes (the master's and the husband's), which is impermissible because it would cause confusion of lineage. The text notes that this second marriage is batil, not merely fasid, because of the stronger connection. The passage also mentions that even if the husband disavows the child, it is not effective unless the pregnancy is connected to him, but this is a nuanced point. The overall ruling: marriage with a woman whose pregnancy is of established lineage is fasid, and marriage of an umm walad pregnant by her master to another man is batil.

Key Terms
سبی (sabī): Captive taken from dar al-harb (enemy territory).
فراش (firāsh): The legal marriage bed or the relationship that establishes paternity; used here to denote the master's exclusive right to the umm walad.
جمع بین الفراشین (jam‘ bayn al-firāshayn): Combining two marriage beds (i.e., having two women in one's protection simultaneously in a way that causes lineage confusion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a man marrying his own pregnant umm walad to another man?
A) The marriage is valid because the umm walad is a slave.
B) The marriage is makruh but valid.
C) The marriage is batil because she is the master's firash.
D) The marriage is fasid and can be rectified by a new contract.

Key Takeaway
Marrying a pregnant umm walad to another man is batil because she is the master's firash, and combining two firashes is impermissible.

Marrying a Pregnant Captive and Marrying One's Umm Walad: Two Invalid Contracts
Explains invalidity of two marriages due to pregnancy-related lineage issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fasid and batil marriage in the context of pregnant women, and explain the causal reasoning (talil) based on lineage and firash.

Core Idea
A pregnant captive's marriage is fasid due to established lineage; marrying a pregnant umm walad is batil due to combining two firash.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's matn presents two distinct rulings that illustrate how the status of pregnancy affects marriage validity. The first case involves a captive woman whose pregnancy is attributed to a previous husband; the second involves a master who attempts to marry his own umm walad while she carries his child. Understanding the difference between fasid (irregular) and batil (void) is crucial for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The text begins with two conditional scenarios: (1) marrying a pregnant captive woman, and (2) marrying one's own pregnant umm walad. Note that the rulings differ: the first is fasid, the second is batil.
Case 1: تزوج حاملا من السبى (marries a pregnant captive). Case 2: زوج ام ولده وهي حامل منه (marries his umm walad who is pregnant from him).
2
Locate the causal reasoning (talil)
For each case, the author provides a reason introduced by 'lianna' (because). In case 1: 'liannahu thabit al-nasab' (because the lineage is established). In case 2: 'liannaha firash' (because she is a conjugal bed).
These reasons explain why the contract is invalid.
3
Distinguish the degrees of invalidity
The first marriage is fasid (irregular) – it can be rectified? Actually, the text says fasid, but the reason is thabit al-nasab, which is a permanent defect? In Hanafi, fasid in nikah means the contract is not valid but can be renewed after the defect is removed (e.g., after delivery). The second is batil (void from the start) because it involves combining two firash.
Fasid: irregular, can be corrected. Batil: void, no effect.
4
Understand the exception regarding firash weakness
The text notes that the firash of an umm walad is weak (ghayr muta'akkid). This means that if no pregnancy is connected, the firash is not considered, and the marriage could potentially be valid. The final clause 'fala yu'tabar ma lam yattasil bihi al-haml' indicates that the firash is only relevant when pregnancy is present.
This clarifies why the second ruling applies only when the umm walad is pregnant from the master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تزوج حاملا من السبى فالنكاح فاسد لانه ثابت النسب وان زوج ام ولده وهي حامل منه فالنكاح باطل لانها فراش لمولاها حتى يثبت نسب ولدها منه من غير دعوة فلو صح النكاح لحصل الجمع بين الفراشين الا انه غير متاكد حتى ينتفى الولد بالنفى من غير لعان فلا يعتبر مالم يتصل به الحمل
If he marries a pregnant woman from the captives, then the marriage is invalid because the pregnancy is of established lineage. And if he marries his umm walad while she is pregnant from him, then the marriage is void because she is a conjugal bed (firash) for her master, so that the lineage of her child is established from him without a claim of lineage. If the marriage were valid, it would result in combining two conjugal beds, except that it is not strong such that the child can be disowned by denial without li'an. So it (the conjugal bed) is not considered unless pregnancy is connected to it.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings regarding marrying pregnant women. First, if a man marries a captive woman from dar al-harb who is already pregnant, the marriage is fasid (invalid) because the child's lineage is already established with her previous husband (a harbi). Second, if a man marries his own umm walad (a slave woman who has borne his child) to someone else while she is pregnant from him, the marriage is batil (void) because she is considered his firash (conjugal bed) – her child's lineage is established without any claim. However, the firash of an umm walad is weak, so if the child is denied by the master without li'an, it is excluded. This exception explains an objection: why is the marriage not void even when she is not pregnant? The answer is that the firash is weak, so it is only considered valid when pregnancy is connected.

Key Terms
ثابت النسب (thābit al-nasab): A pregnancy whose lineage is established and recognized, thus preventing marriage due to potential confusion of lineage.
فراش (firāsh): The conjugal bed of a master over his umm walad, which gives him rights over the child's lineage without a claim.
جمع بين الفراشين (jam‘ bayn al-firāshayn): Combining two conjugal beds, which is invalid because it creates confusion in lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the marriage of a man to his pregnant umm walad is batil?
A) Because she is already married to someone else
B) Because she is his firash
C) Because pregnancy prevents marriage
D) Because the child would be illegitimate

Key Takeaway
The ruling against marrying a pregnant woman hinges on whether the pregnancy has established lineage or creates a conflict of conjugal beds, not merely on the fact of pregnancy itself.

Marrying a Slave Woman After Intercourse: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istibra'
Determines validity of marriage and permissibility of intercourse before istibra' with disagreement among Hanafi imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of marrying a previously-intercourse slave girl and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the new husband's intercourse before istibra'.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid; only the new husband's intercourse before istibra' is disputed among Hanafi imams.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a master who has had intercourse with his slave girl then marries her off. The marriage is valid because the slave girl is not a conjugal bed for the master. However, can the new husband have intercourse with her before she completes istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle)? The two leading imams, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, permit it, while Imam Muhammad disapproves. Let's dissect their reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the initial ruling
The act is a master marrying off his slave girl after having intercourse with her. The initial ruling is that the marriage is valid (jā'iz).
2
Understand the basis for validity
The slave girl is not a firāsh (conjugal bed) for the master; even if she bears a child, lineage is not established without a claim. Hence, her womb is not considered occupied by his water.
This is a key distinction from a wife.
3
Note the master's obligation: istibra' for preservation
The master should perform istibra' to protect his water (i.e., avoid mixing his seed with another's). This is recommended, not obligatory.
The text says 'must' in the sense of strong recommendation.
4
Recognize the new husband's position according to the Shaykhayn
Once the marriage is valid, the husband may have intercourse with her before istibra', according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is the primary view presented in the text.
5
Analyze the opposing view of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad disapproves (makruh) of intercourse before istibra' because of the possibility that the master's water still occupies the womb, analogous to the case of purchasing a slave girl.
He does not declare it haram, but advises caution.
6
Evaluate the reasoning of the Shaykhayn
They argue that the very validity of marriage is a sign (amāra) that the womb is empty; therefore, istibra' is not commanded even as a recommendation. In purchase, however, validity does not indicate emptiness, so istibra' is required.
This clarifies why marriage and purchase are treated differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن وطى جاريته ثم زوجها جاز النكاح لانها ليست بفراش لمولاها فانها لو جاءت بولد لا يثبت نسبه من غير دعوة الا ان عليه ان يستبرأها صيانة لمائه واذا جاز النكاح فللزوج ان يطأها قبل الاستبراء عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لا احب له ان يطأها قبل ان يستبرأها لانه احتمل الشغل بماء المولى فوجب التنزه كما في الشراء ولهما ان الحكم بجواز النكاح امارة الفراغ فلايؤمر بالاستبراء لا استحبابا ولا وجو با بخلاف الشراء لانه يجوز مع الشغل
He said: And whoever has intercourse with his slave girl and then marries her off, the marriage is valid because she is not a conjugal bed for her master. For if she comes with a child, his lineage is not established without a claim. However, he must perform istibra' to preserve his water. When the marriage is valid, the husband may have intercourse with her before istibra' according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: I do not like for him to have intercourse with her before istibra' because there is a possibility of occupancy by the master's water, so it is necessary to abstain as in the case of purchase. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the ruling of validity of marriage is a sign of emptiness (of the womb), so he is not commanded to perform istibra', neither as recommended nor obligatory, unlike purchase because it is valid even with occupancy.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of marrying a slave girl whom the master has previously had intercourse with. The marriage is valid because the slave girl is not considered a firm firash (conjugal bed) – her child's lineage is not established without a claim. However, it is recommended for the master to perform istibra' (wait for one menstrual cycle) to avoid mixing his water with another's. There is a dispute among Hanafi imams regarding whether the new husband may have intercourse before istibra': Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow it, while Imam Muhammad discourages it. The reasoning is that validity of marriage indicates the womb is empty, so istibra' is not required even as a recommendation; in contrast, purchase can occur even with a occupied womb, so istibra' is necessary. The commentary also notes that Shafi'i and Ahmad require istibra' before marriage, and Zufar requires three menstrual cycles.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibri'): The act of waiting for one menstrual cycle to ensure the womb is empty of another's child or fluid.
فراش (firāsh): Conjugal bed that establishes lineage without claim. A slave girl is not firash for her master unless she becomes umm walad.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the two leading imams of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, it is not allowed under any circumstances
B) Yes, it is permissible
C) Only after one menstrual period
D) Only after three menstrual periods

Key Takeaway
The marriage of a slave girl after her master's intercourse is valid; the new husband may have intercourse before istibra' according to the two Shaykhs, but Imam Muhammad advises waiting to avoid doubt.

Weakness of Ummu Walad's Farash Explained
Answering an objection about ummu walad's farash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the farash of an ummu walad as weak and differentiate it from the farash of a free wife.

Core Idea
The farash of an ummu walad is weak and only operative during pregnancy, making her marriage to another valid without istibra'.

In Hanafi fiqh, the concept of farash (legal bed) determines lineage and affects the validity of subsequent marriages. A common objection is that an ummu walad (slave who bore her master's child) cannot marry another because she occupies the master's farash. This passage clarifies that her farash is inherently weak and only considered when she is pregnant, allowing her marriage to be valid. The evidence lies in the ability to repudiate her child without li'an (mutual imprecation), unlike a free wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the passage and state the objection being answered: that marriage of an ummu walad to another should be invalid because combining two farash (master's and husband's) would occur.
The objection assumes the farash is strong like a free wife's.
2
Extract the distinction
The answer distinguishes between strong and weak farash. Locate the terms 'qawi' (strong) and 'da'if' (weak) in the translation.
The ummu walad's farash is weak, not strong.
3
Analyze the evidence
The passage gives evidence: a master can repudiate the child of an ummu walad without li'an. Understand why this proves weakness of farash.
For a free wife, li'an is required to deny paternity, showing her farash is strong and cannot be easily broken.
4
Determine the operative condition
The farash of an ummu walad is considered only when pregnancy is connected. If she is not pregnant, her farash is not operative.
This is why marriage is valid without istibra'.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a master who wants to marry his ummu walad to another. Is the marriage valid? According to the Hanafi school, yes, because her farash is weak and she is not pregnant (or even if she might be, the farash is not strong enough to block marriage).
Some scholars like Zufar require three istibra' periods; Hanafi disagrees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا انه غير متاكد سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جب ام ولد مولی کا فراش تھے غیر حاملہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی نکاح باطل ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ اب بھی جمع بین الفراشین لازم آئے گا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ام ولد مولی کا فراش تو ضرور ہے لیکن قومی نہیں ضعیف ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ام ولد کا بچہ نفی کر دینے سے منتھی ہو جائے گا بغیر لعان کے بخلاف حرہ منکوحہ کے کہ اس کے بچہ کی نفی اگر کی گئی تو لعان واجب ہوگا ۔ پس ام ولد کا فراش ہونا اس وقت معتبر ہو گا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ حمل متصل ہو اور اگر حمل متصل نہیں تو فراش ہونا بھی معتبر نہیں ہوگا۔
This is the answer to an objection from 'ghayr mutaakkid'. The objection is: When an ummu walad is the master's farash, even in the case of being non-pregnant, the marriage should be invalid because joining of two farash would still occur. The answer is: The ummu walad is indeed the master's farash, but it is not strong; it is weak. For this reason, the child of an ummu walad is repudiated without li'an, unlike a free wife, for whom repudiation of her child requires li'an. Thus, the ummu walad's being a farash is considered only when pregnancy is connected to it; if pregnancy is not connected, then her being a farash is not considered.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage addresses a hypothetical objection concerning the marriage of an ummu walad (a slave girl who has borne her master's child). The objection claims that since she is the master's farash (legal bed), marrying her to another should be invalid due to the conflict of two farash. The answer clarifies that the ummu walad's farash is weak (da'if), not like that of a free wife. Evidence: if the master repudiates her child, it is done without li'an (mutual imprecation), whereas a free wife requires li'an. Therefore, her farash is only operative when she is pregnant; otherwise, it is negligible. This justifies the validity of her marriage to another.

Key Terms
فراش (firāsh): The legal bed that establishes lineage without claim; used for a woman with whom the man has a marital or slave-concubinage relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the farash of an ummu walad considered weak?
A) Because she is a slave
B) Because her child's lineage is established without claim
C) Because her child can be repudiated without li'an
D) Because she is not married

Key Takeaway
The ummu walad's farash is weak and conditional on pregnancy, allowing her marriage to another without istibra'.

Marriage to a Zaniyah: Istibra' and Intercourse
Ruling on intercourse before istibra' when marrying a zaniyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on intercourse before istibra' when marrying a zaniyah, and explain the rational argument behind each view.

Core Idea
For the Shaykhayn, a valid marriage itself indicates an empty womb; Muhammad requires precaution due to possible pregnancy.

This passage extends a previous intra-Hanafi dispute from slave girls to free women caught in zina. The same rational arguments apply: does the validity of marriage itself dispense with the need for istibra', or must one wait to avoid mixing lineages? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single usul principle (istiṣḥāb or ihtiyāṭ) yields different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the common scenario
Identify the factual situation: a man sees a woman committing zina, then marries her. The question is whether he may have intercourse before performing istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle to ensure no pregnancy from zina).
2
Identify each imam's position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) hold it is permissible to have intercourse immediately. Imam Muhammad holds it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) until after istibra'.
The term 'حل' (halal) in the text indicates permissibility, while 'لا احب' indicates dislike, not prohibition.
3
Trace the rational argument (dalil aqli)
The Shaykhayn argue that a valid marriage itself is an indication that the womb is empty of another man's child, because marriage is built on certainty of lineage. Muhammad argues that zina creates a possibility of pregnancy, so precaution (ihtiyāṭ) requires waiting.
This is a qiyas on the earlier slave-girl case: the same reasoning applies.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the Shaykhayn's view, the husband may consummate immediately; under Muhammad's view, he should wait one menstrual cycle to avoid confusion of lineage.
The difference is in the ruling of immediate intercourse, not the validity of marriage.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the relied-upon view for fatwa, as it is the stronger and more prevalent opinion in the school.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah often sides with the Shaykhayn unless there is a clear reason to prefer Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كذا اذا رأى امرأة تزنى فتزوجها حل له ان يطاءها قبل ان يستبرأها عندهما وقال محمد لا احب له ان يطأها مالم يستبرأها والمعنى ما ذكرنا

Similarly, if he sees a woman committing zina and then marries her, it is permissible for him to have intercourse with her before istibra' according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: I do not like for him to have intercourse with her until he performs istibra'. And the meaning is what we mentioned. Translation: And when he saw a woman that she commits zina, then he married her, then it is permissible for him to have intercourse before istibra' according to the two shaykhs. According to the two shaykhs, it is permissible to have intercourse even before istibra'. Imam Muhammad said: Without istibra', intercourse is not liked by me. The proofs of both parties are the same as mentioned in the previous issue.

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to a woman caught in zina. The same intra-Hanafi dispute applies: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow intercourse before istibra', while Imam Muhammad discourages it. The reasoning is identical: for the Shaykhayn, the validity of the marriage (which requires a clear womb) indicates emptiness; for Muhammad, the possibility of pregnancy from zina necessitates precaution. The commentary notes that the proofs are exactly those discussed earlier for the slave girl case.

Key Terms
زنا (zinā): Illicit sexual intercourse that does not create legal lineage.
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period (usually one menstrual cycle) to ensure the womb is empty of another man's child before intercourse with a new master or husband.
شيخين (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Mut'ah Marriage is Invalid
Ruling and proof that mut'ah marriage is invalid, with response to Imam Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah marriage and explain why it is invalid, distinguishing the Hanafi position from Imam Malik's view.

Core Idea
Mut'ah marriage is invalid because the Companions' consensus abrogated its original permissibility.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on mut'ah (temporary marriage) from a Hanafi perspective. The Hanafi school, along with the majority, holds that mut'ah is invalid (batil). The key proof is the consensus (ijma') of the Companions, which abrogated its early permissibility. We will also explore Imam Malik's dissenting view and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules mut'ah marriage as invalid (batil).
This is the ruling found in the Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that mut'ah is permissible because it was originally allowed and no abrogator appeared.
Imam Malik's view is based on the absence of an explicit abrogating text.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that mut'ah was permissible in early Islam and remains so until a clear abrogator is found.
No explicit verse or hadith unequivocally prohibits mut'ah; Malik's position relies on this absence.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the consensus of the Companions (including Ibn Abbas's retraction) established abrogation.
Ijma' is a definitive proof (qat'i) and can abrogate a prior ruling.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis deem the contract void with no legal effect, while Malikis treat it as a valid marriage.
This affects inheritance, divorce, and legitimacy of children.

And mut'ah marriage is invalid. It is that one says to a woman: 'I will enjoy you for such a period for such an amount of wealth.' Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on mut'ah marriage (temporary marriage). The Hanafi position, shared by all major imams except Malik, is that it is invalid. The proof: although mut'ah was permissible in early Islam, it was abrogated by the consensus (ijma') of the Companions. The commentary notes that even Ibn Abbas, who initially held it permissible, later retracted and joined the consensus. Imam Malik's argument that no explicit abrogator exists is countered by the fact that the Companions' consensus itself is a binding evidence of abrogation. The passage ends mid-sentence with a potential objection regarding the nature of the consensus.

Key Terms

Mut'ah marriage is invalid in the Hanafi school due to the consensus of the Companions, which abrogated its early permissibility.

The Ruling on Marrying a Woman Seen Committing Zina: Is Istibra' Required?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istibra'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding istibra' in this case and explain the basis of each position.

Core Idea
Marriage itself indicates an empty womb – the Shaykhayn see no need for istibra'; Muhammad disagrees.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. A man witnesses a woman committing zina and then marries her. Must he wait for one menstrual period (istibra') before intercourse? The answer differs among the Hanafi imams, revealing deeper principles about the presumption of purity and the role of marriage in dispelling doubt.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn). They hold that intercourse is permissible without istibra'.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that istibra' is recommended (makruh tanzihi to omit) before intercourse.
Muhammad's view is a minority within the Madhhab.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Muhammad argues: there is a possibility the woman is pregnant from zina, so precaution (istibra') is advisable to avoid uncertainty.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Shaykhayn respond: marriage is legislated only when the womb is free from any legitimate impediment; the validity of the marriage itself indicates emptiness, so no extra precaution is needed.
The reasoning is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the man has intercourse without istibra', according to Shaykhayn it is permissible (mubah); according to Muhammad it is makruh tanzihi. The practical difference lies in the sinfulness of the act.
The mufta bihi is the Shaykhayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كذا اذا رأى امرأة تزنى فتزوجها حل له ان يطاءها قبل ان يستبرأها عندهما وقال محمد لا احب له ان يطأها مالم يستبرأها والمعنى ما ذكرنا
ترجمہ اور جب دیکھا کسی عورت کو کہ وہ زنا کرتی ہے پھر اس سے نکاح کیا تو اس کیلئے ولی حلال ہے استبراء سے پہلے شیخین کے نزدیک اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ میں اس کیلئے پسند نہیں کرتا کہ اس سے وطی کرے جب تک کہ استبراء نہ کرالے اور دلیل وہی ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی۔ تشریح ایک عورت کو زنا کرتے ہوئے دیکھا، پھر اس سے نکاح کر لیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک استبراء سے پہلے ہی وطی کرنا حلال ہے۔ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ بغیر استبراء کے وطی کرنا میرے نزدیک پسندیدہ نہیں ہے فریقین کے دلائل وہی ہیں جن کا ذکر اس سے پہلے مسئلہ میں ہو چکا ۔
And likewise, if he saw a woman committing zina and then married her, it is permissible for him to have intercourse with her before performing istibra' according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: I do not like for him to have intercourse with her until he performs istibra'. And the meaning is what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a man who marries a woman he witnessed committing zina. The issue is whether he must perform istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle to ensure the womb is empty) before intercourse. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that istibra' is not required because the act of marriage itself serves as an indicator of an empty womb, as marriage is only legislated when the womb is free from any legitimate impediment. Imam Muhammad disagrees, arguing that there is a possibility the woman may be pregnant from the zina, so istibra' is recommended to avoid uncertainty. The previous passage (mentioned in the book) contains the detailed proofs. The commentator explains that the difference of opinion is based on whether marriage indicates emptiness of the womb (Shaykhayn) or whether precaution requires istibra' (Muhammad). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Shaykhayn, as it is the basis of the fatwa.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting for one menstrual period to ensure the womb is free from pregnancy before intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He cannot marry her at all.

Key Takeaway
When a man marries a woman he saw committing zina, the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) allows immediate intercourse because the marriage contract itself indicates the womb is free.

Why Nikah Mut'ah is Invalid: The Hanafi Proof
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of mut'ah marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school deems nikah mut'ah invalid (bāṭil) and haram, and to evaluate the opposing view attributed to Imam Malik using the proof of consensus (ijma') and the retraction of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Mut'ah marriage is invalid because the Companions' consensus permanently forbade it.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: the validity of temporary marriage (nikah mut'ah). The Hanafi school, along with the majority, rules it invalid and haram. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents an opposing view attributed to Imam Malik, who allegedly considered it permissible based on original permissibility. We will explore the Hanafi response, which relies on the consensus of the Companions (ijma' al-sahaba) and the decisive retraction of Ibn Abbas. By the end, you will understand why this consensus constitutes a binding proof and how the Hanafi position is upheld.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: nikah mut'ah is invalid (bāṭil) and haram. Define mut'ah as a marriage for a fixed duration in exchange for payment.
The Hanafi school is unanimous on this.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
The passage attributes to Imam Malik the view that mut'ah is permissible because it was originally allowed and no clear abrogator (nāsikh) appeared. Understand the logic: original permissibility remains until abrogated.
Note: later commentators correct this attribution as erroneous.
3
Follow the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi response cites two proofs: (1) the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) at Khaybar forbidding mut'ah, and (2) the consensus of the Companions after Ibn Abbas retracted his permissive view. 'Abrogation is established by the consensus of the Companions.'
The proof is qaṭ'ī (definitive) in both transmission and meaning.
4
Analyze the opponent's argument and the Hanafi rebuttal
The opponent argues that no abrogator appeared. The Hanafi rebuttal: the abrogating evidence did appear—the Prophet's prohibition and the Companions' consensus. Ibn Abbas's retraction removes any doubt about the consensus. Even though Ibn Abbas initially held a permissive view, when informed of the Prophet's prohibition by 'Ali, he returned to the majority view.
This establishes the consensus as complete.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi school, any marriage contract with a fixed time limit is invalid; the children are not legitimate, and the contract is akin to fornication. The Maliki school, despite the attribution in Al-Hidayah, actually holds the same prohibition, as evidenced by Imam Malik's own narration of the forbidding hadith in the Muwaṭṭa'.
Thus, the difference is resolved: all four Sunni schools prohibit mut'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونكاح المتعة باطل و هو ان يقول لامرأة اتمتع بك كذا مدة بكذا من المال و قال مالك هو جائز لانه كان مباحا فيبقى الى ان يظهر ناسخة قلنا ثبت النسخ باجماع الصحابة و ابن عباس صح رجوعه الى قولهم فتقرر الاجماع
ترجمہ اور نکاح متعہ باطل ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کہے کسی عورت سے کہ میں تجھ سے اتنی مدت اتنے مال کے بدلہ نفع اٹھاؤں گا اور امام مالک نے فرمایا نکاح متعہ جائز ہے اس لئے کہ متعہ مباح تھا ، پس باقی رہے گا یہاں تک کہ کوئی ناسخ ظاہر ہو۔ ہم کہیں گے کہ اجماح صحابہ سے شیخ ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور ابن عباس کا رجوع بھی ثابت ہو چکا قول صحابہ کی جانب پس اجماع ثابت ہے۔ تشریح متعہ کسی عورت سے اتمتع بک کذا مدة بكذا من المال کہنا ہے یعنی مقررہ مال کے بدلے معینہ مدت تک نفع اٹھانا. تمام ائمہ متعہ کی حرمت کے قائل ہیں۔ علاوہ امام مالک کے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ابتدائے اسلام میں متعہ مباح تھا لہذا اس کی اباحت اس وقت تک باقی رہے گی جب تک کوئی ناسخ نہ آ جائے اور ناسخ اب تک آیا نہیں ۔ لہذا مباح رہے گا۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ متعہ کی حرمت پر صحابہ کا اجماع ہے وہ تاریخ بن جائے گا مگر اس پر یہ اشکال ہوگا کہ حرمت متعہ پر صحابہ کے اجماع کو نقل کرنا صحیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ اجماع کے زمانہ میں ابن عباس متعہ کے جواز کے قائل تھے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ایک مرتبہ حضرت علیؓ نے ابن عباس سے کہا کہ کیا آپ کو معلوم نہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خیبر کے دن متعہ کو حرام کر دیا تھا، ابن عباس نے یہ سن کر اپنے قول سے رجوع کیا، اور جواز متعہ کے سلسلہ میں اپنے قول سے توبہ کی۔ پس جب ابن عباس بھی رجوع فرما چکے تو حرمت متعہ پر اجماع ثابت ہو گیا۔
متعہ خیبر سے پہلے حلال تھا لیکن خیبر کے دن حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پالتو گدھوں کے گوشت اور معتہ النساء کو حرام کر دیا۔ پھر فتح مکہ کے سال یوم اوطاس میں تین دن کیلئے حلال کیا گیا ، پھر چوتھے دن قیامت تک کیلئے حرام کر دیا گیا۔ اس موقع پر یہ واضح کر دینا بھی ضروری ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام مالک کے مذہب کو نقل کرنے میں غلطی کی یا سہو ہو گیا کیونکہ مالکیہ کی کسی کتاب میں جواز متعہ کو بیان نہیں کیا گیا۔ علاوہ ازیں امام مالک نے اپنی موطا میں حضرت علی کی حدیث نقل کی ہے: ان رسول الله نهى عن متعة النساء و عن لحوم الحمر الاهلية من خيبر (عینی شرح ہدایہ) اور حضرت امام مالک کی عادت ہے کہ وہ اپنی موطا میں وہی حدیث روایت کرتے ہیں جو ان کا مذہب ہوتی ہے۔ پس اس حدیث کو موطا میں جگہ بنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ امام مالک بھی حرمت متعہ کے قائل ہیں۔
And mut'ah marriage is invalid. It is when a man says to a woman: 'I will enjoy you for such a period for such an amount of wealth.' Malik said: It is permissible because it was permissible originally, so it remains until an abrogator appears. We say: Abrogation is established by the consensus of the Companions, and Ibn Abbas's return to their statement is established, so consensus is confirmed.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of nikah mut'ah (temporary marriage for a fixed period in exchange for a specified payment). The Hanafi position, along with the majority, is that it is absolutely invalid (bāṭil) and haram. The text presents the view of Imam Malik as reported in Al-Hidayah, who allegedly considered it permissible on the basis that it was originally allowed and no clear abrogator has appeared. The Hanafi response is that the abrogation is established by the consensus (ijma') of the Companions, including the eventual return of Ibn Abbas to the majority view. The commentary notes a potential error in Al-Hidayah's attribution to Imam Malik, pointing out that the Maliki school does not permit mut'ah and that Imam Malik himself narrated a hadith forbidding it. The commentator clarifies the historical sequence: mut'ah was permitted before Khaybar, then forbidden, then temporarily allowed at the Conquest of Makkah, then permanently forbidden. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is that mut'ah is invalid and akin to fornication. The key proof is the consensus of the Companions after Ibn Abbas retracted his permissive view.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A temporary marriage contract for a fixed duration in exchange for payment, considered invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the Hanafi position that mut'ah is invalid?
A) A verse from the Qur'an explicitly forbidding it
B) The consensus of the Companions after Ibn Abbas's retraction
C) Juristic preference (istihsan)
D) A single hadith from one Companion

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah marriage is invalid because the Companions' consensus, after Ibn Abbas's retraction, definitively established its prohibition.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Temporary Marriage (Nikah Muwaqqat) is Invalid: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nikah muwaqqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nikah muwaqqat and identify the key difference between Imam Zufar's position and the majority view.

Core Idea
A marriage with a fixed time limit is invalid because the intention of mut'ah taints the contract, regardless of wordings or witnesses.

Nikah muwaqqat (temporary marriage) is a contract of marriage for a specified duration, using proper words like 'tazawwajtu' and witnesses. Despite its formal similarity to permanent marriage, the Hanafi school declares it invalid (batil) because the time limit reveals an underlying intent of mut'ah. However, a notable intra-Hanafi difference exists: Imam Zufar considers it valid, treating the time limit as a void condition rather than a part of the contract. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and the final mufta bihi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What type of marriage contract is discussed? What is the hukm according to the majority?
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule nikah muwaqqat as batil.
2
Understand Imam Zufar's argument
What is Zufar's dalil? He argues that invalid conditions (like a time limit) do not invalidate the marriage; only the condition is void.
Zufar analogizes it to a marriage with a condition 'I will not divorce you for a month'—the condition is void but the marriage stands.
3
Analyze the majority's response
Why do the majority reject Zufar's analogy? Because in nikah muwaqqat, the time limit is not a condition added after the contract but is integrated into the offer and acceptance itself.
The majority say the contract itself is limited, not just a condition attached to an unlimited contract.
4
Apply the usul rule: 'al-ibratu fi al-uqud li al-ma'ani'
The consideration in contracts is of meanings. Since the meaning of nikah muwaqqat is mut'ah, it is invalid despite proper words and witnesses.
This is the core Hanafi principle: the substance (meaning) prevails over the form (wording).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The majority view (batil) is the mufta bihi; Zufar's view is considered marjuh (weak).
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the majority, no legal effects arise; under Zufar, it would be a valid permanent marriage.

And the temporary marriage is invalid, such as when he marries a woman with the testimony of two witnesses for ten days. Zufar said: It is valid and binding because marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions. And our proof is that it carries the meaning of mut'ah, and the consideration in contracts is of meanings. There is no difference whether the set duration is long or short because the setting of time is what designates the aspect of mut'ah, and it has been found.

Commentary
This passage discusses nikah muwaqqat (temporary marriage with a fixed time limit, e.g., ten days, using proper words like 'tazawwajtu' and witnesses). The difference from mut'ah is that muwaqqat uses the word 'nikah' and includes witnesses, but the Hanafi ruling is that it is still invalid. Imam Zufar argues that it is valid because marriage contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions; the condition is void but the marriage remains. The Hanafi response is that the time limit is not a mere condition but an integral part of the offer and acceptance, so the marriage is based on a limited duration and thus resembles mut'ah in meaning. The majority of Hanafi jurists (including the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad) agree that such a marriage is invalid. The relied-upon position is that any marriage with a fixed time limit is void.

Key Terms
النكاح المؤقت (al-nikah al-muwaqqat): A marriage contracted for a specific duration, using the word 'nikah' with witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it lacks witnesses
B) Because it uses the wrong wording
C) Because it carries the meaning of mut'ah
D) Because the time limit is too long

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that nikah muwaqqat is batil hinges on the principle that the substance of the contract (its meaning) determines its validity, not merely the outward form.
