Correction of a Misattribution: Imam Malik and the Prohibition of Mut'ah
Defends ijma on mut'ah prohibition and corrects Hidayah's Maliki attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mut'ah, explain the consensus after Ibn Abbas's retraction, and correct the erroneous attribution of permissibility to Imam Malik using the Muwatta evidence.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is prohibited by consensus; Ibn Abbas retracted, and Imam Malik agreed, contrary to a mistake in Al-Hidayah.

This passage addresses two crucial points: first, it defends the consensus of the Companions on the prohibition of mut'ah by recounting how Ibn Abbas retracted his earlier permission after being reminded of the Prophet's prohibition. Second, it corrects a historical error in Al-Hidayah where Imam Malik was mistakenly said to permit mut'ah, showing that Imam Malik actually includes the prohibition hadith in his Muwatta, which proves his agreement with the majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection and the Hanafi Response
Understand that some claim the consensus (ijma) on mut'ah's prohibition is invalid because Ibn Abbas initially held it permissible. The Hanafi response is that Ibn Abbas retracted after Ali informed him of the Prophet's prohibition at Khaybar, thus removing the only dissenting voice.
This retraction is key to establishing the consensus.
2
Trace the Abrogation History of Mut'ah
The passage outlines the legal history: mut'ah was originally permitted, then prohibited at Khaybar, then briefly permitted during the Conquest of Mecca, and finally prohibited permanently. Recognize that multiple abrogations occurred with the final prohibition being definitive.
This history reinforces the finality of the prohibition.
3
Examine Misattribution to Imam Malik
The author of Al-Hidayah reportedly attributed the permissibility of mut'ah to the Maliki school. However, the passage argues that this is a mistake because no Maliki book mentions permissibility, and Imam Malik narrated the prohibition hadith in his Muwatta, following his habit of including only hadiths that agree with his school.
Imam Malik's own Muwatta serves as evidence against the misattribution.
4
Confirm the Hanafi and Maliki Consensus
Conclude that both the Hanafi and Maliki schools, and indeed all Sunni schools, hold mut'ah to be prohibited. The correction in the commentary ensures accurate transmission of madhhab positions.
This step emphasizes the importance of accurate textual transmission.

Source Text

كتاب النكاح
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
پر صحابہ کے اجماع کو نقل کرنا صحیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ اجماع کے زمانہ میں ابن عباس متعہ کے جواز کے قائل تھے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ایک مرتبہ حضرت علیؓ نے ابن عباس سے کہا کہ کیا آپ کو معلوم نہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خیبر کے دن متعہ کو حرام کر دیا تھا، ابن عباس نے یہ سن کر اپنے قول سے رجوع کیا، اور جواز متعہ کے سلسلہ میں اپنے قول سے توبہ کی۔ پس جب ابن عباس بھی رجوع فرما چکے تو حرمت متعہ پر اجماع ثابت ہو گیا۔
متعہ خیبر سے پہلے حلال تھا لیکن خیبر کے دن حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پالتو گدھوں کے گوشت اور معتہ النساء کو حرام کر دیا۔ پھر فتح مکہ کے سال یوم اوطاس میں تین دن کیلئے حلال کیا گیا ، پھر چوتھے دن قیامت تک کیلئے حرام کر دیا گیا۔ اس موقع پر یہ واضح کر دینا بھی ضروری ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام مالک کے مذہب کو نقل کرنے میں غلطی کی یا سہو ہو گیا کیونکہ مالکیہ کی کسی کتاب میں جواز متعہ کو بیان نہیں کیا گیا۔ علاوہ ازیں امام مالک نے اپنی موطا میں حضرت علی کی حدیث نقل کی ہے: ان رسول الله نهـى عـن متعة النساء و عن لحوم الحمر الاهلية من خيبر ( عینی شرح ہدایہ) اور حضرت امام مالک کی عادت ہے کہ وہ اپنی موطا میں وہی حدیث روایت کرتے ہیں جو ان کا مذہب ہوتی ہے۔ پس اس حدیث کو موطا میں جگہ بنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ امام مالک بھی حرمت متعہ کے قائل ہیں۔
Book of Nikah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 4. It is not correct to cite the consensus of the Companions (for the prohibition of mut'ah) because in the time of that consensus, Ibn Abbas was of the view that mut'ah is permissible. The answer to this is that once Ali ibn Abi Talib said to Ibn Abbas: 'Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah forbade mut'ah on the day of Khaybar?' Upon hearing this, Ibn Abbas retracted his statement and repented of his opinion regarding the permissibility of mut'ah. Thus, when Ibn Abbas himself retracted, the consensus on the prohibition of mut'ah is established. Mut'ah was permissible before Khaybar, but on the day of Khaybar, the Prophet forbade the meat of domestic donkeys and mut'ah with women. Then, in the year of the conquest of Mecca, on the day of Awtas, it was made permissible for three days, then on the fourth day it was forbidden until the Day of Judgment. At this point it is also necessary to clarify that the author of Hidayah made a mistake or lapse in attributing the opinion to Imam Malik, because in none of the Maliki books is the permissibility of mut'ah mentioned. Moreover, Imam Malik narrated in his Muwatta the hadith of Ali: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade mut'ah with women and the meat of domestic donkeys at Khaybar.' And it is the habit of Imam Malik to narrate in his Muwatta only those hadiths that conform to his school. Thus, placing this hadith in the Muwatta is evidence that Imam Malik also held the prohibition of mut'ah.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof against the temporary marriage (mut'ah), correcting a common misconception about its consensus (ijma) and a mistake in the attribution of Imam Malik's position.

The text begins by addressing an objection: some may claim that consensus on the prohibition of mut'ah cannot be cited because Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) initially held it permissible. The response is that Ali ibn Abi Talib informed Ibn Abbas of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) prohibition at Khaybar, upon which Ibn Abbas immediately retracted and repented. Since the only dissenting voice was withdrawn, the consensus on prohibition is firmly established.

Next, the passage recounts the history of the ruling: mut'ah was originally permissible, then prohibited at Khaybar along with donkey meat; then temporarily allowed for three days during the Conquest of Mecca at Awtas, and finally prohibited forever on the fourth day of that occasion. This sequence demonstrates multiple abrogations, with the final prohibition being permanent.

Finally, the author points out an error in the text of Al-Hidayah, where Imam al-Malik was incorrectly said to permit mut'ah. The commentary refutes this by noting: (1) no Maliki book mentions permissibility, (2) Imam Malik includes in his Muwatta the hadith of Ali prohibiting mut'ah, and (3) Imam Malik's practice is to include only those hadiths that agree with his school. Therefore, Imam Malik held mut'ah to be prohibited. The correction aligns the Hanafi commentary with the Maliki position for accuracy.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): Temporary marriage for a fixed period in exchange for a dower, prohibited by the Prophet and consensus.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions on the prohibition of mut'ah after Ibn Abbas retracted.
موطا (Muwatta): The hadith compilation of Imam Malik, which includes the hadith of Ali prohibiting mut'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The revelation of a Quranic verse
B) Ali reminding him of the Prophet's prohibition at Khaybar
C) The general consensus of the Companions
D) A fatwa from Imam Malik

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is prohibited by definitive evidence and consensus; the misattribution to Imam Malik is unfounded and must be corrected.

Nikah — Marriage

Why Time-Limited Marriage (Nikah Muwaqqat) is Invalid
Ruling on time-limited marriage with intra-Hanafi dispute and reasoning based on meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates a time-limited marriage and distinguish between the majority view and the view of Imam Zufar, including the underlying reasoning based on ma'ani al-'uqud.

Core Idea
A marriage fixed for a period is invalid because its meaning is mut'ah, which is prohibited; form does not override essence.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi dispute on whether a marriage contract with a fixed duration is valid. The majority holds it is invalid (batil) because it mirrors mut'ah, while Imam Zufar argues it is a valid marriage with an invalid condition. By understanding the Hanafi principle that contracts are judged by their meanings (ma'ani), you will grasp why the majority view prevails and how to apply this principle in modern contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify that the ruling for nikah muwaqqat is batil (invalid) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, including the author of Hidayah.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Recognize Imam Zufar's view that it is valid and binding, based on the principle that marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions (shart fasid).
Zufar analogizes to a marriage with the condition not to divorce.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the key rebuttal: the time limitation is not a condition but part of the offer and acceptance, making the contract itself temporary and thus equivalent to mut'ah.
Contracts are judged by their meanings, not words (al-'ibrah fi al-'uqud lil-ma'ani).
4
Examine the examples given
Study the analogies (wakalah after death, kafalah/hawalah) that illustrate how meaning overrides form in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Identify the practical consequence: if someone contracts a time-limited marriage, it is completely invalid (majority) vs. valid without the condition (Zufar). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view, supported by Hidayah.
The narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad and similar from Abu Hanifa are not relied upon.

والنكاح المؤقت باطل مثل ان يتزوج امرأة بشهادة شاهدين عشرة ايام وقال زفر هو صحيح لازم لان النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة ولنا انه اتى بمعنى المتعة والعبرة في العقود للمعاني ولا فرق بين ما اذا ملة التاقيت او قصرت لان التاقيت هو المعين لجهة المتعة و قد وجد

تشریح نکاح موقت یہ ہے کہ کوئی شخص دو گواہوں کی موجودگی میں ایک مدت محدود کیلئے نکاح کرے، ہمثلا دس دن کیلئے ایک سال کیلئے وغیرہ وغیرہ۔ نکاح موقت اور نکاح متعہ میں فرق دو طرح سے ہے۔ اول یہ کہ نکاح موقت میں لفظ تزوج مذکور ہوتا ہے متعہ میں نہیں ، دوم یہ کہ موقت میں شہادت شاہدین ہوتی ہے متعہ میں نہیں ۔ عام فقہاء نکاح موقت کی حرمت کے قائل ہیں علاوہ امام زفر کے۔ امام زفر جواز کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل امام زفر کی یہ ہے کہ نکاح موقت نکاح ہے اور صرف اس میں وقت محدود کی شرط لگا دی گئی ۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود شروط فاسدہ باطل ہو جاتی ہیں۔ مثلاً کسی شخص نے اس شرط پر نکاح کیا کہ ایک ماہ کے بعد طلاق نہیں دوں گا تو یہ شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور نکاح درست ہوگا ۔ اور ایک ماہ کے بعد بھی شوہر کو طلاق دینے کا حق حاصل رہے گا۔ لیکن امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وقت محدود شرط نہیں بلکہ ایجاب وقبول ہی اس وقت تک کیلئے ہے اور ایسا جاب و قبول صحیح نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح موقت میں متعہ کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ نکاح موقت کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ کچھ روز نفع اٹھاؤں گا اور عقود میں معانی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے نہ کہ الفاظ کا۔ مثلا کسی نے کسی شخص کو کہا کہ تو میرے مرنے کے بعد میرا وکیل ہے تو وہ ویسی ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر کہا کہ تو میری زندگی میں میرا وصی ہے تو وکیل ہو جائیگا یا آپ نے پڑھا ہوگا کہ کفالہ بشرط براۃ اصیل حوالہ ہے۔ اور حوالہ بشرط عدم براۃ اصیل کفالہ ہے۔ پس جب عقود میں معانی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور نکاح موقت میں متعہ کے معنی پائے گئے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جس پر متعہ صادق آجائے وہ باطل ہے، لہذا ا نکاح موقت بھی باطل ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نکاح موقت میں جو مدت ذکر کی جائے وہ دراز ہو یا کم ، دونوں صورتوں میں بطلان کا حکم ہوگا کیونکہ وقت محدود کرنا ہی جہت متعہ کو معین کرنے والا ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ در حقیقت یہ حسن بن زیاد کے قول سے احتراز ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر اتنی طویل مدت ذکر کر دی جس میں دونوں زندہ نہیں رہ سکتے تو اس صورت میں نکاح درست ہو گا اس لئے کہ اب یہ تابید کے معنی میں ہوگا۔ ابوحنیفہ سے بھی ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Time-limited marriage is invalid. Example: a man marries a woman with two witnesses for ten days. Zufar said it is valid and binding because marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions. Our proof: it carries the meaning of mut'ah, and consideration is given to the meanings in contracts. There is no difference whether the period is long or short, because the specification of time is what indicates the intent of mut'ah, and that exists. Explanation: Time-limited marriage is a marriage for a fixed period, e.g., ten days or one year, with two witnesses. There are two differences between time-limited marriage and mut'ah: first, in time-limited marriage the word 'tazawwaj' is used, while in mut'ah it is not; second, in time-limited marriage there is testimony of two witnesses, while in mut'ah there is not. The majority of jurists consider it invalid, except Imam Zufar who considers it permissible. Zufar's proof: it is a marriage with a condition of time, and marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions; the condition becomes void while the marriage remains. For example, if one marries with the condition not to divorce for a month, the condition is void but the marriage is valid. Our response: the limitation of time is not a condition; rather, the offer and acceptance are themselves for that period, and such an offer and acceptance are not valid. Our proof is that time-limited marriage contains the meaning of mut'ah, because the intent is to enjoy for a few days, and consideration is given to meanings, not words, in contracts. For example, if one says, 'You are my agent after my death,' it becomes valid agency; or if one says, 'You are my executor during my lifetime,' it becomes agency. Similarly, kafalah with the condition of release of the principal is hawalah, and hawalah with the condition of non-release of the principal is kafalah. Thus, when meanings are considered and time-limited marriage carries the meaning of mut'ah, and the rule is that whatever is called mut'ah is invalid, therefore time-limited marriage is invalid. The author of Hidayah says whether the period is long or short, it is invalid because specifying time indicates mut'ah. This refutes the opinion of Hasan ibn Ziyad, who said if a very long period is specified such that both cannot live, it becomes valid since it implies permanence. A similar narration from Abu Hanifa exists. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of time-limited marriage (nikah muwaqqat). The text begins with the Hanafi position (majority): such a marriage is invalid (batil). It defines it as a marriage with a fixed period, e.g., ten days, with two witnesses.

Then it presents the dissenting view of Imam Zufar, who argues that it is a valid marriage with an invalid condition; since marriage is not nullified by invalid conditions (only the condition is void), the marriage remains sound. As an analogy, he cites a man who marries with the condition not to divorce for a month — the condition is void but the marriage is valid.

The Hanafi response refutes Zufar by stating that the limitation of time is not a mere condition extrinsic to the contract; rather, the offer and acceptance are themselves confined to that period. Thus, it is not a condition but an integral part of the subject matter. Therefore, the marriage is invalid from the outset. The core reasoning is that time-limited marriage shares the meaning (ma'na) of mut'ah (pleasure marriage), which is prohibited. In Hanafi law, contracts are evaluated by their underlying meanings, not merely by verbal forms. Examples are given: if someone says 'You are my agent after my death,' it is considered agency (wakalah) because the meaning is delegation; similarly, kafalah with condition of release of the principal becomes hawalah. Hence, if the meaning is mut'ah, the contract is invalid.

The text also clarifies a nuance from Hasan ibn Ziyad (a narrator of rare transmissions): if the period is extremely long (e.g., 100 years), it may be considered valid as it implies permanence. A similar narration from Abu Hanifa exists, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that any temporal limitation, short or long, invalidates the marriage. This is the position of the author of Hidayah.

Thus, the lesson underscores that a marriage intended for a limited time is equivalent to mut'ah and therefore invalid, regardless of the length of duration or the use of proper witnesses or wording.

Key Terms
نکاح موقت (nikah muwaqqat): A marriage contract with a specified duration, considered invalid in the Hanafi school because it shares the meaning of mut'ah.
متعہ (mut'ah): Temporary marriage for a fixed period without witnesses or using specific words; prohibited by consensus.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is invalid according to Shariah but does not necessarily invalidate the contract in all cases (e.g., in marriage, the condition is void but the marriage may remain valid).
معانی العقود (ma'ani al-'uqud): The underlying meanings and intentions of contracts, which take precedence over literal wording in determining the legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (majority), why is a time-limited marriage (nikah muwaqqat) invalid?
A) Because it lacks two witnesses
B) Because the word 'mut'ah' is used
C) Because it carries the meaning of mut'ah
D) Because a condition of time invalidates all conditions

Key Takeaway
Time-limited marriage is invalid because it carries the meaning of mut'ah; contracts are judged by their underlying meanings, not by form.

Partial Validity in a Single Marriage Contract
Ruling with proof and qiyas jali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that when a man marries two women in one contract, one lawful and one unlawful, the lawful marriage is valid and the unlawful one is batil, and explain the distinction from sale contracts using qiyas.

Core Idea
Invalidity is limited to the invalidating factor—it does not spill over to the valid part.

This passage addresses a key scenario where a single marriage contract includes both a lawful and an unlawful woman. The Hanafi school rules that the lawful marriage is valid and the unlawful one is invalid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, contrasting it with an analogous case in sale contracts, and notes an intra-madhhab difference on the mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
A man marries two women in one contract. One is lawful (halal) and the other is unlawful (haram). The ruling is that the lawful marriage is sahih and the unlawful one is batil.
This is the core ruling from the passage.
2
Apply the principle of butlan bi qadr al-mubtil
Invalidity is limited to the extent of the invalidating factor. Since the prohibition applies only to one woman, only that marriage is invalid.
The invalidating factor does not transfer to the other.
3
Contrast with the sale of a free man and slave
In sale, combining a free man and a slave makes the entire contract invalid because the buyer must accept or reject wholly (tafriq al-safqah prohibited) and accepting the free man as a condition for the slave is an invalid condition.
Marriage is severable; sale is indivisible.
4
Identify the illa (effective cause) of the difference
In sale, the invalidity arises from the nature of the transaction requiring indivisibility. In marriage, each woman is a separate subject, so the invalidity is confined.
The qiyas is by shabahah (similarity) but the far' is distinguished by the illa.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on mahr
Abu Hanifa: entire specified dower goes to the lawful wife. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: divided according to mahr al-mithl of each.
This is a subsidiary dispute; the main ruling on validity is agreed upon.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ایک عقد میں دو عورتوں سے نکاح کیا اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا نکاح اس سے حلال نہیں تو وہ عورت جس کا نکاح حلال ہے اس کا نکاح درست ہو گا اور دوسری کا نکاح باطل ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ منبطل ان دونوں میں سے ایک میں ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ غلام اور آزاد کو بیچ میں جمع کیا اس لئے کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس عقد میں آزاد کے حق میں عقد قبول کرنا شرط ہے۔ پھر جمیع مسمی اس عورت کیلئے ہے جس کا نکاح حلال ہے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تقسیم کیا جائے گا دونوں کے مہر مثل پر اور یہ مسئلہ مبسوط کا ہے۔ تشریح ایک شخص نے عقد واحد میں دو عورتوں سے نکاح کیا ان دونوں میں سے ایک اس کیلئے حلال ہے اور ایک حرام ہے قرابت نسب یا رضاعت یا کسی اور وجہ سے تو حکم یہ ہے کہ جو حلال تھی اس کا نکاح درست ہو جائے گا اور جوحرام تھی اس کا باطل ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ کہ بطلان بقدر مبطل ہوتا ہے اور مبطل صرف ایک میں ہے نہ کہ دوسری میں لہذا جس میں مبطل نکاح موجود ہے اس کا نکاح باطل ہو جائے گا اور جس میں مبطل نکاح موجود نہیں اس کا درست ہو گا۔ بخلاف اس کے کہ اگر کسی نے عقد بیع میں آزاد اور غلام دونوں کو جمع کر دیا تو ان دونوں میں بیج باطل ہوگی۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ جب آزاد اور غلام دونوں کو ایک عقد میں جمع کیا تو مشتری دونوں میں بھیج کو قبول کرے یا دونوں میں چھوڑ دے، یہ جائز نہیں کہ کچھ میں قبول کرے اور کچھ میں قبول نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس میں تفریق صفقہ ہے اور تفریق صفقہ حرام ہے۔ پس جب دونوں میں قبول کرے گا تو غلام میں عقد قبول کرنے کیلئے آزاد میں عقد کا قبول کرنا شرط ہوگا اور چونکہ آزاد کل بیع نہیں ہے اس لئے مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ غیر مبیع میں عقد قبول کرنا بیع کیلئے شرط ہے۔ اور یہ شرط فاسد ہے جس کا عقد تقاضا نہیں کرتا اور یہ پہلے معلوم ہو چکا کہ شرط فاسد کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیع و شرط سے
And whoever marries two women in one contract, one of whom it is not lawful for him to marry, then the marriage of the woman who is lawful is valid, and the marriage of the other is invalid, because the invalidating factor is in one of them, unlike when he combines a free man and a slave in a sale, because the sale becomes invalid due to the invalid conditions, and acceptance of the contract in the free man is a condition in it. Then all the named dower is for the woman whose marriage is lawful according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is divided according to the dower of the like (mithl) of each. This is the principle issue. Translation: And whoever marries two women in one contract, and one of them is not lawful for him, then the woman whose marriage is lawful, her marriage is valid, and the other's marriage is invalid, because the invalidating factor is in one of them, unlike when a free man and a slave are combined in a sale, because sale is invalidated by invalid conditions, and acceptance of the contract in the free man is a condition in it. Then all the named dower is for the woman whose marriage is lawful according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions (Sahibayn) it is divided according to the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) of each, and this is the principle issue. Explanation: A person marries two women in one contract, one lawful and the other unlawful due to lineage, fosterage, or other reason. The ruling: the lawful marriage is valid, the unlawful is invalid. The proof is that invalidity is only to the extent of the invalidating factor, and the invalidating factor is only in one, not the other. Therefore, the one with the invalidating factor becomes invalid, and the one without remains valid. This is unlike if someone combines a free man and a slave in a sale contract; then the sale is invalid for both. The reason for the difference: when a free man and a slave are combined in one sale, the buyer must either accept the entire contract or reject it entirely; he cannot accept part and reject part because that is splitting the transaction (tafriq al-safqah), which is prohibited. Thus, if he accepts both, then for the sale of the slave to be valid, the acceptance of the contract for the free man is a condition, and since the free man is not part of the subject of sale, this amounts to making the acceptance of a non-sold item a condition for the sale, which is an invalid condition (shart fasid), and it is established that an invalid condition invalidates the sale. Because the Prophet (?)
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on a specific marriage scenario: a man marries two women in a single contract, one of whom is lawful for him and the other unlawful (e.g., due to kinship, fosterage, or other prohibition). The Hanafi ruling, as presented, is that the lawful marriage is valid and the unlawful one is invalid. The contract is severable; the invalidating factor (the prohibited relationship) is confined to one woman and does not affect the other.

The text compares this to the case of selling a free man and a slave together in one sale contract. In that case, the entire sale is invalid because the buyer must accept or reject the whole contract—splitting the transaction (tafriq al-safqah) is prohibited. Moreover, for the slave's sale to be valid, acceptance of the free man (who is not lawful to sell) would be a condition, which is an invalid condition rendering the sale invalid.

In contrast, in marriage, the invalidity is limited to the prohibited spouse. The reason is that the marriage contract does not require indivisibility in the same way as sale. Each marriage is a separate relationship, and the prohibition only applies to one specific individual.

The text also includes a secondary intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mahr. According to Abu Hanifa, the entire specified dower (mahr musamma) goes to the lawful wife. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), the dower is divided between the two women proportionally based on their respective mahr al-mithl (standard dower). This is a point of difference within the school, and the text states this is the "principle issue" (مسئلة الاصل) from the book al-Mabsut.

The explanation further clarifies the reasoning: invalidity is proportionate to the invalidating factor (batalan biqadr al-mubtil). Since the invalidating factor exists only in one, only that one is invalid. The comparison with sale shows that the rules differ due to the nature of the transaction. Thus, the lesson underscores the Hanafi approach of partial validity in marriage contracts involving multiple parties.

Key Terms
عقد واحد (aqd wahid): A single contract encompassing multiple subjects, here two women in marriage.
بطلان بقدر مبطل (butlan bi qadr mubtil): Invalidity is limited to the extent of the invalidating factor; it does not spill over to unaffected parts.
تفریق صفقہ (tafriq al-safqah): Splitting a single transaction by accepting part and rejecting part, which is prohibited in sale.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): Standard dower comparable to that of women similar to the bride in family and status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The mahr is given to the unlawful wife as compensation
D) The mahr is forfeited entirely

Key Takeaway
In a single marriage contract with multiple women, invalidity is limited to the prohibited spouse; the lawful marriage remains valid, and the mahr distribution is subject to intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Marrying Two Women in One Contract: Validity and Dower Dispute
Explains ruling when two women married together, one lawful, one not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying two women in one contract where one is unlawful, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over mahr distribution.

Core Idea
Marrying two women in one contract: the lawful marriage is valid, the unlawful is void; the dower goes entirely to the lawful wife according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic case of a marriage contract that includes two women, one of whom is unlawful for the husband. The ruling distinguishes between the validity of the marriages and the distribution of the dower. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (the Sahibayn) on how to apportion the named dower. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to analyze how partial invalidity affects contractual obligations and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues
The passage addresses two separate but connected issues: (1) the validity of the two marriages, and (2) the distribution of the specified dower (mahr musamma). First, extract the ruling on validity: the marriage of the lawful woman is valid (sahih), that of the unlawful woman is void (batil). The reason given is that the invalidating factor is confined to one party.
Note that the contract is a single 'uqdah, but the ruling treats each marriage separately in terms of validity.
2
Understand the analogy with sale
The passage contrasts this case with a sale combining a free man and a slave. In that sale, the entire contract becomes void because accepting the contract for the free man (who cannot be sold) is a condition that invalidates the whole. In marriage, corrupt conditions do not invalidate the marriage; only the condition becomes void. This distinction is crucial for justifying why the lawful marriage remains valid.
The key is that in marriage, the contract is more resilient: fasid conditions are excised without destroying the valid part.
3
Locate the dower dispute
After establishing validity, the passage presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement on dower. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the entire named dower (mahr musamma) goes to the lawful wife. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the dower is divided proportionally based on the customary dower (mahr al-mithl) of both women.
This dispute is recorded as a well-known original issue (mas'alah al-asl) in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the proof of each position
Abu Hanifa's proof: The contract is valid only for the lawful woman; the mention of the unlawful woman is void, so the entire consideration (dower) belongs to the valid marriage. The Sahibayn's proof: The dower was named as a consideration for the sexual access (private parts) of both women; since the contract for the unlawful woman is void, the consideration must be divided according to the value of each.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: in Abu Hanifa's view, the husband pays the full named dower to the lawful wife; in the Sahibayn's view, he pays a portion to each (based on mahr al-mithl).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the later Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa. This means in practice, the lawful wife receives the entire specified dower.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah does not explicitly give tarjih, but later fatwa collections adopt Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن تزوج امرأتين فى عقدة واحدة واحداهما لا يحل له نكاحها صح نكاح التي حل نكاحها وبطل نكاح الاخرى لان المبطل فى احداهما بخلاف ما اذا جمع بين حرو عبد فى البيع لانه يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وقبول العقد فى الحر شرط فيه ثم جميع المسمى للتى حل نكاحها عند ابي حنيفة وعندهما يقسم على مهر مثليهما وهي مسئلة الاصل
And whoever marries two women in one contract, one of whom it is not lawful for him to marry, the marriage of the one lawful for him is valid, and the marriage of the other is void, because the invalidating factor is in one of them, unlike when he combines between a free man and a slave in a sale, because the sale becomes void by corrupt conditions, and accepting the contract in the free man is a condition in it. Then the entire dower belongs to the one whose marriage is lawful according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is divided according to the mahr al-mithl of both, and this is the original issue.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a scenario where a man marries two women in a single marriage contract, but one of the women is unlawful for him to marry (e.g., due to kinship, fosterage, etc.). The ruling is that the marriage of the lawful woman is valid, while the marriage of the unlawful woman is void. The reason is that the invalidity is confined to one party, not affecting the other. This differs from a sale where a free man and a slave are sold together in one contract: in that case, the sale is void entirely because accepting the contract for the free man is a condition, and the corrupt condition invalidates the whole sale. However, in marriage, corrupt conditions do not invalidate the marriage itself; only the condition becomes void. Therefore, the valid marriage remains. Then, regarding the dower (mahr), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the entire specified dower (mahr musamma) goes to the lawful wife, because the contract was intended for her. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the dower is divided proportionally based on the mahr al-mithl (customary dower) of both women, since the dower was mentioned as a consideration for both. Al-Marghinani notes that this issue is recorded in Al-Mabsut (a work of Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
مهر مسمى (mahr musamma): The dower specified in the marriage contract by name and amount.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary dower of a woman similar to the bride in family, beauty, etc.
عقدة واحدة ('uqdah wahidah): A single contract session or a single contractual offer and acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries two women in one contract, one of whom is his sister (unlawful), what is the ruling?
A) Both marriages are void
B) The marriage to the lawful woman is valid, to the sister is void
C) Only the marriage to the sister is valid
D) Both are valid

Key Takeaway
When two women are married in one contract and one is unlawful, the lawful marriage is valid and, per Abu Hanifa, the entire specified dower goes to the lawful wife.

Judge's Ruling Based on False Witnesses: Permissibility of Intercourse
Explains permissibility of intercourse when judge rules on false testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad's positions on the binding effect of a judge's ruling based on false witnesses, and explain the Hanafi proof that the ruling is binding internally.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on apparent proof is binding if internal execution is possible, even if the witnesses are false.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a challenging scenario: a woman falsely claims marriage and the judge rules in her favor based on witnesses. The man knows he never married her. Is intercourse permissible? The Hanafi school is internally divided, and the answer hinges on whether the judge's ruling carries internal binding force. We'll explore the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Read the passage and note the key facts: a woman claims marriage, presents witnesses, judge rules she is his wife, but the man never married her. Identify the two opposing rulings on intercourse.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says intercourse is permissible. Find his proof: the judge's ruling is based on apparent proof (al-hujjah), and since truthfulness is unascertainable, the ruling must be binding both externally and internally.
3
Extract the opposing position and its proof
Muhammad (and Shafi'i) say intercourse is impermissible. Their proof: the witnesses are liars, so the judge erred in proof, analogous to witnesses being slaves or disbelievers, which invalidates the ruling.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the analogy
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: slavery and disbelief are ascertainable facts, but truthfulness is not. Therefore, the analogy fails, and the ruling stands.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the woman may continue the marriage and relations; under Muhammad she must avoid him. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's, as held in the Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من ادعت عليه امرأة انه تزوجها واقامت بيئة فجعلها القاضى امرأته ولم يكن تزوجها وسعها المقام معه و ان تدعه يجامعها وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وهو قول ابى يوسف اولا وفي قوله الاخر وهو قول محمد لا يسعه ان يطأها وهو قول الشافعى لان القاضى اخطأ الحجة اذالشهود كذبة فصار كما اذا ظهرانهم عبيدا و كفار و لأبي حنيفة ان الشهود صدقة عنده وهو الحجة لتعذر الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق بخلاف الكفر والرق لان الوقوف عليهما متيسر و اذا ابتنى القضاء على الحجة وامكن تنفيذه باطنا بتقديم النكاح نفذ قطعا للمنازعة بخلاف الاملاك المرسلة لأن في الاسباب تزاحما فلا امكان والله اعلم
And a woman claimed against him that he married her, and she established evidence (witnesses), so the judge made her his wife, whereas he had not married her. It is permissible for her to stay with him and to allow him to have intercourse with her. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf. In his other opinion, which is the opinion of Muhammad, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her, and this is the opinion of al-Shafi'i, because the judge erred in the proof, as the witnesses are liars, so it becomes like when it becomes apparent that they are slaves or disbelievers. And for Abu Hanifa, that the witnesses are truthful in his view, and that is the proof, because it is impossible to ascertain the truth of truthfulness, unlike disbelief and slavery, because ascertaining them is easy. And when the decision is based on the proof and it is possible to execute it inwardly by presenting the marriage, it is carried out definitively to end the dispute, unlike unconditional possessions because in the causes there is competition, so it is not possible. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a situation where a woman claims a man married her and produces witnesses. The judge, based on this evidence, rules that she is his wife, even though the man never actually married her. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible for the woman to remain with him and to allow him to have intercourse. This is also the first opinion of Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is that the judge's ruling is based on the apparent proof (al-hujjah), which is the witnesses' testimony. Since it is impossible for the judge to know the inner truth of whether the witnesses are truthful or lying, he must act on the apparent. The ruling is therefore valid and must be complied with externally and internally, as long as it is possible to execute it inwardly by assuming a prior marriage. This differs from cases where the cause of ownership is in conflict (e.g., two conflicting sales), where internal execution is not possible. However, the second opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, is that intercourse is not permissible, because the judge erred in the proof (the witnesses are liars). They analogize this to a case where the witnesses are discovered to be slaves or disbelievers, which would invalidate their testimony. Abu Hanifa distinguishes that disbelief and slavery are ascertainable facts, whereas the truthfulness of witnesses is not. Therefore, the judge's ruling is binding.

Key Terms
حجة (hujjah): The legal proof presented to the judge, here the testimony of witnesses.
قضاء (qada'): The judge's ruling or decree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a judge declares a marriage based on false witnesses, what is the ruling on intercourse?
A) Haram
B) Permissible
C) Makruh
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling based on apparent proof is binding externally and, where possible, internally; the truthfulness of witnesses is unascertainable, so the ruling stands even if the witnesses are false.

Judge's Ruling on False Testimony in Marriage: Outward and Inward Effects
Dispute over validity of judge's ruling based on false witnesses in marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between outward (zahiri) and inward (batini) enforcement of a judge's ruling based on false testimony in marriage, and state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i on this issue.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on false testimony is fully effective according to Abu Hanifa, but only outwardly according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a dispute about the legal effect of a judge's ruling when false witnesses are used in a marriage claim. The key question is whether the ruling makes the marriage permissible both in worldly law and before Allah. The Hanafi school has an internal difference, as well as a disagreement with al-Shafi'i. We will examine the proofs and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
A woman falsely claims a man married her and produces false witnesses. The judge rules in her favor, declaring them married. The man had not actually married her. This is the base case for the dispute.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the ruling is effective both outwardly (zahiran) and inwardly (batinan). Outwardly: the husband must pay maintenance and the marriage is recognized for inheritance etc. Inwardly: intercourse is permissible before Allah. This is also the first opinion of Abu Yusuf.
The judge must rely on apparent evidence; he cannot know the inner truth.
3
Identify the opposing position
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the ruling is effective only outwardly. Inwardly, intercourse remains impermissible because the witnesses were false, so the judge erred in proof. This is also the second opinion of Abu Yusuf.
They analogize to cases where witnesses are discovered to be slaves or disbelievers.
4
Analyze the proofs
The opponent's proof: When witnesses turn out to be slaves or kuffar, the ruling is only outward by consensus. Similarly, false witnesses make the judge's proof erroneous, preventing inward effect. Abu Hanifa's response: Slavery and disbelief are outwardly verifiable, but truthfulness is not. The judge cannot know the hidden truth, so he must give full effect to his ruling.
This is a distinction in the nature of the defect (kufr/riqq vs falsehood).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, the man may lawfully have intercourse with the woman; according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, he may not. The marriage is valid in worldly matters in both views.
The dispute is about the permissibility of intercourse, not about maintenance or lineage.

A woman claimed that a man married her, and she produced evidence, so the judge declared her his wife, though he had not married her. It is permissible for her to live with him and let him have intercourse. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf. In his second opinion, and it is the opinion of Muhammad, he is not permitted to have intercourse with her, and this is the opinion of al-Shafi'i, because the judge erred in the proof since the witnesses were false. Thus it is like when it becomes apparent that they were slaves or disbelievers. Abu Hanifa's proof: The witnesses are truthful in the judge's view, and that is the proof, since ascertaining the truth of truthfulness is impossible, unlike disbelief and slavery, which are easily known. When judgment is based on proof and it is possible to execute it inwardly by presuming the marriage, it is enforced to end the dispute, unlike unrestricted claims to ownership (amlak mursalah) because there is conflict of causes, so no possibility. And Allah knows best. Translation: ... [followed by Urdu translation and explanation] ... Explanation of the case: A woman falsely claims a man is her husband and produces false witnesses. The judge rules in her favor. Is the ruling effective? There is ikhtilaf. According to Abu Hanifa, it is effective both outwardly and inwardly. Abu Yusuf's first opinion is same. According to Muhammad, outwardly effective but not inwardly. Abu Yusuf's second opinion is same, and this is al-Shafi'i's opinion. The principle: The judge's ruling based on false testimony in contracts and annulments is effective outwardly and inwardly according to Abu Hanifa. ... Types of property: amlak mursalah (where cause is not mentioned) and amlak muqayyadah (where cause is mentioned). The case here is about amlak muqayyadah. Types of enforcement: outward (zahiri) and inward (batini). Outward: worldly rulings like maintenance; inward: permissibility before Allah. In amlak mursalah, the ruling is outwardly effective only by consensus. In amlak muqayyadah, according to Abu Hanifa it is effective both outwardly and inwardly; according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, only outwardly. Abu Yusuf's first opinion aligns with Abu Hanifa, his second with Muhammad. Muhammad's proof: Since witnesses are false, the judge erred in proof, and an error in proof prevents inward enforcement. So outwardly, the husband must pay maintenance, but intercourse is not permissible for him. Analogy: if witnesses turn out to be slaves or disbelievers, the ruling is outwardly only by consensus. Abu Hanifa's proof: The judge cannot know the inner truth; through formal justice (ta'dil) the witnesses are considered truthful, and that is the proof. When proof is established, judgment is necessary. ... [cut off]
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses a case where a woman falsely claims a man married her and produces false witnesses. The judge rules in her favor. The key question is whether this ruling is effective both outwardly (zahiran) and inwardly (batinan). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the ruling is effective both ways: the marriage is considered valid in worldly matters (e.g., maintenance, inheritance) and also permissible for intercourse in the sight of Allah. The reason is that the judge must rely on external evidence; he cannot know the inner reality. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the ruling is only effective outwardly—the man must pay maintenance but it is not lawful for him to have intercourse because the witnesses were actually false. They analogize to cases where witnesses turn out to be slaves or disbelievers. The commentator then explains the distinction between two types of property claims: amlak mursalah (unrestricted claims without specifying cause) and amlak muqayyadah (claims with a specified cause, like marriage). The present case is of amlak muqayyadah because a specific cause (nikah) is mentioned. The debate also touches on the concept of 'outward enforcement' (affecting worldly legal consequences) versus 'inward enforcement' (affecting religious permissibility). The passage provides both sides' arguments: Muhammad's argument that an error in proof prevents inward enforcement, and Abu Hanifa's argument that the judge's inability to know hidden truths necessitates giving full effect to his ruling based on apparent evidence.

Key Terms
ظاہراً و باطناً (zāhiran wa bāṭinan): Outwardly (in worldly legal consequences) and inwardly (in religious permissibility before Allah).
املاک مرسلہ (amlāk mursalah): Claims of ownership without specifying the cause (e.g., 'this is mine' without mentioning purchase or inheritance).
املاک مقیدہ (amlāk muqayyadah): Claims of ownership with a specified cause (e.g., 'I married her' or 'I bought it').
شہادت زور (shahādah zūr): False testimony; giving false witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a judge rules based on false witnesses that a marriage occurred, is it permissible for the husband to have intercourse with the woman?
A) No, because the witnesses were false
B) Yes, both outwardly and inwardly
C) Yes, but only outwardly, not inwardly
D) It depends on whether the witnesses are slaves or free

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective at least outwardly; the dispute is over inward enforcement, which Abu Hanifa affirms and Muhammad/al-Shafi'i deny.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Judge's Verdict Based on False Testimony: Apparent and Inner Validity
Explaining Hanafi ikhtilaf on verdict based on false witnesses in marriage contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between apparent and inner validity of a judge's verdict based on false testimony and explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf in contracts (amlak muqayyadah) versus property claims (amlak mursalah).

Core Idea
A judge's verdict based on false witnesses can be valid inwardly in marriage contracts according to Abu Hanifa, but only outwardly according to Muhammad.

In this passage, we examine a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: when a judge unknowingly rules based on false testimony, does his verdict have only worldly effect or also religious validity? The answer depends on whether the claim concerns a contract with a specified cause (like marriage) or an unspecified property claim. We will explore the classification of property claims and the two types of execution, then analyze the proofs of the imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The scenario: a woman falsely claims marriage, presents false witnesses, judge rules in her favor. Identify the key elements: false claim, false witnesses, judge's verdict after apparent verification.
2
Classify the property claim
Determine whether the claim is amlak mursalah (cause not mentioned) or amlak muqayyadah (cause mentioned). Here, the cause (marriage) is explicitly claimed, so it is restricted property.
Restricted property: the cause of ownership is specified.
3
Distinguish between nafadh zahiri and batini
Apparent execution: worldly effects (maintenance, custody). Inner execution: permissibility before Allah (halal). Understand that these have different conditions.
Inner execution is more stringent.
4
State the Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and first opinion of Abu Yusuf: verdict valid both ways. Imam Muhammad, second opinion of Abu Yusuf, and Imam Shafi'i: valid only apparently. Note the intra-Hanafi split.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Analyze the proofs
Examine Muhammad's proof (error in evidence prevents inner execution, analogy with slave/disbeliever witnesses) and Abu Hanifa's proof (judge must rely on apparent truthfulness, verdict creates marriage by implication, support from Caliph Ali). Understand the refutation of the analogy.
The key difference: slavery/disbelief have identifiable signs, falsehood does not.

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے ایک مرد پر جھوٹا دعویٰ کر دیا کہ یہ میرا شوہر ہے مجھ سے اس نے شادی کی تھی اپنے اس جھوٹے دعوی پر جھوٹی شہادت بھی پیش کر دی قاضی نے ظاہری شہادت پر عورت کے حق میں فیصلہ دیدیا تو قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ نافذ ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ فیصلہ ظاہرا اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کا قول اول بھی یہی ہے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک ظاہرا تو نافذ ہوگا باطنا نافذ نہیں ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول بھی یہی ہے اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ فقہاء کے یہاں اس مسئلہ کا عنوان ہے:

یعنی جھوٹی گواہی سے قاضی کا فیصلہ عقود و فسوخ میں ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ظاہرا اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ کیا جائے گا۔ املاک کی اقسام... فریقین کے دلائل سے پہلے بطور مقدمہ کے دو باتیں ذہن نشین کر لیجئے ۔ اول یہ کہ املاک کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ املاک مرسلہ اور املاک مقیدہ املاک مرسلہ یہ ہیں کہ ان میں سبب ملک مذکور نہ ہو۔ مثلاً آپ نے کہا کہ یہ باندی میرے لئے ہے اور یہ نہیں بتلا یا کہ خریدی ہے یا وراثت میں ملی ہے یا اور کوئی ذریعہ ہے۔ اور املاک مقیدہ کہتے ہیں کہ سبب ملک مذکور ہو۔ مثلاً آپ نے کہا کہ یہ باندی میری ہے، میں نے اس کو فلاں سے خریدا ہے یا مجھ کو وراثت میں ملی ہے۔ متن کا مسئلہ املاک مقیدہ کے بارے میں ہے کیونکہ اس میں سبب یعنی تزوج مذکور ہے۔ دوسر کی بات یہ کہ نفاذ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ نفاذ ظاہری اور نفاذ باطنی ۔
نفاذ ظاہری تو یہ ہے کہ دنیاوی احکام کا ترتب ہو سکے۔ مثلاً بیوی کا قدرت دینا اور شوہر پر نفقہ اور کسوہ کا واجب ہونا۔ اور نفاذ باطنی یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی کے نزدیک حلت ثابت ہو جائے املاک مرسلہ میں قاضی نے جھوٹی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا تو یہ فیصلہ بالا تفاق ظاہراً نافذ ہوگا باطنا نہیں اور اگر املاک مقیدہ میں جھوٹی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک ظاہر اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ظاہر ا نافذ ہوگا باطنا نہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کا قول اول امام صاحب کے ساتھ ہے اور قول ثانی امام محمد کے ساتھ ہے۔ اس تفصیل کے بعد دلائل سنئے :-
امام محمد کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہوگا چونکہ گواہ جھوٹے ہیں اس لئے قاضی نے حجت میں غلطی کی ۔ اور خطافی الحجت نفوذ باطنی کو منع کرتا ہے۔ لہذا قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ ظاہرا تو نافذ ہوگا جس کے نتیجہ میں شوہر پر نفقہ اور کسوہ واجب ہو گا لیکن باطنا نا فذ نہیں ہوگا جس کی وجہ سے شوہر کے لئے اس عورت سے وطی حلال نہیں ہوگی ۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر شہادت کے بعد شاہدین کا غلام ہونایا کا فر ہونا ظاہر ہواتو ، قاضی نے اگر فیصلہ دیا تھا تو وہ ظاہر آ نافذ ہوگا باطنا نہیں اور اس پر سب کا اجماع ہے۔ لہذا گواہوں کے کاذب ہونے کی صورت میں بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ ظاہر انا فذ ہونا چاہئے ، باطنا نہیں۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ قاضی کا حقیق - صدق پر مطلع ہونا تو متعد رہے البتہ تعدیل وغیرہ سے یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ گواہ قاضی کے نزدیک صادق ہیں اور گواہوں کا صادق ہونا ہی حجت ہے اور جب حجت قائم ہو گئی تو قاضی پر فیصلہ کرنا لازم ہے حتی کہ اگر ایسی صورت میں یہ سمجھے کہ مجھ پر فیصلہ دینا لازم نہیں تو کافر ہوگا اور اگر لازم سمجھے مگر تا خیر کرے تو فاسق ہوگا۔ امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب کہ کفر اور رقیت پر واقف ہونا آسان ہے اس لئے کہ کفار اور غلاموں کو ان کی مخصوص علامتوں سے پہچانا جاسکتا ہے۔
پس جب فیصلہ کی بنیا د جت پر ہے اور حجت پائی گئی تو فیصلہ نافذ کر دیا جائے گالیکن یہاں ایک سوال ہوگا وہ یہ کہ قضا کہتے ہیں اظہار ماکان ثابتاً کو کہ اثبات مالم لیکن کو یعنی قضاء کہتے ہیں ثابت شدہ چیز کو ظاہر کرنا نہ کہ غیر ثابت کو ثابت کرنا ۔ اور مسئلہ مذکورہ میں نکاح ثابت نہیں تھا لہذا باطناً فیصلہ کیسے نافذ کیا جا سکتا ہے؟ ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے ہتقدیم النکاح سے اس اشکال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اقتضاء فیصلہ پر نکاح کو مقدم مان لیا جائے گا، گویا قاضی نے کہا کہ پہلے میں نے تیرا اس مرد سے نکاح کیا پھر تم دونوں کے درمیان اس نکاح کا فیصلہ کر دیا لیکن اس پر اگر کوئی اشکال کرے کہ قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ انشاء عقد نکاح ہے لہذا گواہوں کا ہونا شرط ہونا چاہئے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ بعض کے نزدیک تو شرط ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک شرط نہیں اس لئے کہ یہ انشاء عقد اقتضاء ثابت ہوا ہے اور جو چیز اقتضاء ثابت ہوتی ہے اس میں شرائط کی رعایت نہیں کی جاتی ۔ ہماری تائید میں حضرت علی کا قول بھی ہے، آپ کے سامنے اسی قسم کا واقعہ پیش آیا جو متن میں مذکور ہے آپ نے نکاح کا فیصلہ کر دیا ، اس عورت نے کہا امیر المؤمنین! اس نے مجھ سے نکاح نہیں کیا تھا، حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا شاہد اک زوجاک تیرے دونوں گواہوں نے تیرا نکاح کرنا اورنفذ قطعا للمنازعہ سے نفوذ باطنی کی علت بیان کی ہے کہ بخلاف الا ملاک سے کہتے ہیں کہ املاک مقیدہ کو املاک مرسلہ پر قیاس کیا جائے کیونکہ املاک مرسلہ میں صرف ظاہر ا فیصلہ نافذ ہوگا باطنا نہیں ، دلیل یہ ہے کہ املاک مرسلہ میں سبب ملک مذکور نہیں ہوتا ہے اور ایک ملک کے بہت سے اسباب ہو سکتے ہیں۔ مثلاً سبب ملک شراء بھی ہو سکتا ہے ارث بھی ہبہ اور صدقہ بھی اور تمام اسباب میں مزاحمت ہے پس اگر قاضی ایک سبب کو متعین کر کے فیصلہ دے تو ترجیح بلا مرحج لازم آئے گی اس لئے نفر باطنی ملک کی نہیں۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد سکروڈوی
Explanation: The case is that a woman falsely claimed against a man that 'he is my husband, he married me.' She also presented false witnesses on her false claim. The judge decided in favor of the woman based on apparent testimony. Then is this verdict executable or not? There is disagreement about this. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this verdict is executable both apparently and inwardly. The first opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is the same. According to Imam Muhammad, it is executable apparently but not inwardly. The second opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is also this, and this is the opinion of Imam Shafi'i. Among jurists, the title of this issue is: 'The judge's verdict based on false testimony in contracts and dissolutions is executable according to Abu Hanifa apparently and inwardly.' That is, the judge's verdict based on false testimony in contracts and dissolutions will be executed both apparently and inwardly according to Abu Hanifa. Types of properties... Before the proofs of the two parties, as a preface, note two things: First, properties are of two types: unrestricted properties (amlak mursala) and restricted properties (amlak muqayyada). Unrestricted properties are those in which the cause of ownership is not mentioned. For example, you said 'this slave-girl is mine' but did not state whether bought, inherited, or other means. Restricted properties are those in which the cause of ownership is mentioned. For example, you said 'this slave-girl is mine, I bought her from so-and-so' or 'I inherited her.' The text's issue is about restricted properties because the cause (i.e., marriage) is mentioned. Second, execution has two types: apparent execution and inner execution. Apparent execution means that worldly rulings can follow. For example, giving the wife power and the obligation of maintenance and clothing on the husband. Inner execution means that permissibility (halal) is proven before Allah. In unrestricted properties, when the judge gives a verdict based on false testimony, this verdict is by agreement executed apparently but not inwardly. And if in restricted properties he gives a verdict based on false testimony, then according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] it is executed both apparently and inwardly. And according to Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i, it is executed apparently but not inwardly. First opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is with Imam [Abu Hanifa], and second opinion is with Imam Muhammad. After this detail, hear the proofs: Summary of Imam Muhammad's proof: Since the witnesses are false, the judge erred in the evidence. And error in evidence prevents inner execution. Therefore, the judge's verdict is executed apparently, resulting in maintenance and clothing being obligatory on the husband, but it is not executed inwardly, so intercourse with that woman is not permissible for the husband. Its analogy is if after testimony it becomes apparent that the witnesses were slaves or disbelievers, the judge's verdict if given would be executed apparently but not inwardly, and there is consensus on this. Therefore, in case of false witnesses also the judge's verdict should be executed apparently, not inwardly. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: Since the judge's knowledge of the reality of truth is impossible, but through ta'dil (witness verification) it is established that the witnesses are truthful in the judge's view. And the witnesses being truthful is the evidence. When the evidence is established, it is necessary for the judge to give verdict, such that if in such a case he thinks that it is not necessary for him to give verdict, he becomes a disbeliever, and if he thinks it necessary but delays, he becomes a transgressor. The answer to the analogy of Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i: Awareness of disbelief and slavery is easy because disbelievers and slaves can be recognized by their specific signs. So when the verdict is based on evidence and the evidence is found, the verdict will be executed. But here a question arises: Qada (judgment) is defined as 'manifestation of what was established' not 'establishment of what was not established.' And in the mentioned case, marriage was not established, so how can the verdict be executed inwardly? The author of Hidayah answered this objection with 'by presenting marriage first' (bi taqdim al-nikah). The summary of the answer: The marriage is considered prior to the verdict, as if the judge said: 'First I performed your marriage to this man, then I gave the verdict of this marriage between you.' But if someone objects that this verdict of the judge is a creation (insha') of the marriage contract, therefore the presence of witnesses should be a condition. The answer: According to some, it is a condition, and according to some, it is not, because this creation of the contract is proven by implication (iqtida'), and in what is proven by implication, conditions are not observed. In our support, there is the saying of Hadrat Ali, a similar incident occurred before him mentioned in the text; he gave a verdict of marriage. The woman said, 'O Commander of the Faithful! He did not marry me.' Hadrat Ali said: 'Your two witnesses performed your marriage' (shahidaka zawwajaka). And 'it is executed decisively to end the dispute' (yunfadhu qat'an li al-munaza'a) has been mentioned as the cause of inner execution. Contrary to properties (amlak), because restricted properties are analogized to unrestricted properties, as in unrestricted properties the verdict is only executed apparently, not inwardly. The proof: In unrestricted properties, the cause of ownership is not mentioned, and there can be many causes of ownership. For example, the cause of ownership can be purchase, inheritance, gift, charity, and all causes conflict. So if the judge specifies one cause and gives verdict, then preference without a preponderator (tarjih bila murajjih) would occur, hence there is no inner ownership. And Allah knows best what is right. Jamil Ahmad Sakrodiwi.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a judge's verdict when based on false testimony in a marriage contract. The text follows the author's order: first stating the case (a woman falsely claims marriage, produces false witnesses, judge rules in her favor), then stating the Ikhtilaf (Abu Hanifa holds the verdict valid both apparently and inwardly; Imam Muhammad holds it valid only apparently; Abu Yusuf has two narrations, one with Abu Hanifa and one with Muhammad; Imam Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad). The commentary then divides property into two types: unrestricted (amlāk mursalah, where the cause of ownership is not mentioned) and restricted (amlāk muqayyadah, where the cause is mentioned). The ruling applies to restricted property because the cause (marriage) is specified. Execution is also divided: apparent (worldly effects like maintenance and clothing) and inner (permissibility before Allah). In restricted property, the verdict is executed both ways according to Abu Hanifa; in unrestricted, only apparently by consensus. The author then presents the proofs: Imam Muhammad argues that false witnesses mean the evidence is faulty, so inner execution is blocked, citing consensus on the case where witnesses are later found to be slaves or disbelievers. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the judge can only rely on apparent evidence; if the witnesses appear truthful after verification, he must give judgment, and if he refuses he becomes a disbeliever. The reply to Imam Muhammad's analogy is that slavery and disbelief are easily identifiable, unlike falsehood. A potential objection is addressed: judgment should only manifest what is already established, but here marriage was not established. The solution from al-Hidayah is that the marriage is considered prior to the judgment, meaning the judge is effectively creating the marriage contract (insha') and then executing it. This is allowed because it is proven by implication (iqtida'), and conditions for creating a contract (like witnesses at the time of judgment) are not required due to the nature of implication. Support is drawn from the practice of Caliph Ali, who similarly ruled on a disputed marriage. The text concludes that in unrestricted property, analogizing with restricted is invalid because the cause is indefinite, leading to preference without preponderator.

Key Terms
قضاء القاضي بشهادة الزور (qada' al-qadi bi shahadat al-zur): A judge's verdict issued based on testimony that is actually false, but the judge believes it to be true after apparent verification.
املاک مرسلہ (amlak mursalah): Properties whose cause of ownership is not specified (e.g., merely claiming ownership without mentioning purchase, inheritance, etc.).
املاک مقیدہ (amlak muqayyadah): Properties whose cause of ownership is mentioned (e.g., claiming ownership by stating the specific transaction).
نفاذ ظاہری (nafadh zahiri): Apparent execution: the worldly legal effects of the verdict apply (e.g., maintenance, custody).
نفاذ باطنی (nafadh batini): Inner execution: the ruling is valid in the sight of Allah, making actions permissible (halal) in private conscience.
حجت (hujjah): Evidence or proof that legally justifies a verdict. In this context, the apparent truthfulness of witnesses is considered hujjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a judge gives a verdict based on false testimony in a marriage contract (restricted property), the verdict is:
A) Valid only outwardly (zāhiran) and not inwardly (bāṭinan).
B) Invalid both outwardly and inwardly.
C) Valid both outwardly and inwardly (zāhiran wa bāṭinan).
D) Valid only if the judge knew the witnesses were lying.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a judge's verdict based on false testimony in a contract (restricted property) is valid both outwardly and inwardly according to Abu Hanifa, while according to Imam Muhammad it is only outwardly valid.

Nikah — Marriage

The Hanafi Ruling on Marriage Without a Guardian: Definitions and Scope
Defining terms and stating the primary Hanafi ruling on women contracting marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman marrying without a guardian and identify the key conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
A free, sane, adult woman may marry without a guardian; this is the Hanafi position in the apparent narration.

This lesson introduces the chapter on guardians (awliyā') and compatibility (akfā') in Islamic marriage law. We will first define the key terms wali and kufu', then examine the core Hanafi ruling that a woman with full legal capacity can contract her own marriage. This sets the foundation for understanding the different opinions within and outside the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define key terms: wali and kufu'
Extract the definitions from the text. Wali is derived from wilāyah, meaning authority over others. Kufu' means a peer or equal in social status, religion, etc.
These definitions are essential for understanding the chapter.
2
Identify the ruling
Locate the sentence: 'وينعقد نكاح الحرة العاقلة البالغة برضائها...' This states that the marriage of a free, sane, adult woman is contracted with her consent, even without a guardian.
Note the conditions: free, sane, adult, consenting. Virgin or non-virgin applies.
3
Note the source of the ruling
The text attributes this to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāyah). This indicates it is the established position of the school.
There are other narrations; we will cover them in the next lesson.
4
Understand the basis for permissibility
The text hints at the basis: 'انها تصرفت فى خالص حقها وهى من اهله' — she acts in her pure right and is qualified. This point is cut off, but we can infer the principle: a woman with full capacity has authority over her own marital consent.
The full argument is given in subsequent pages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في الأولياء والاكفاء
ترجمه. .... یہ باب اولیاء اور اکفاء کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح اولیاء جمع ہے ولی کی اور ولی ماخوذ ہے ولایت سے اور ولایت کہتے ہیں تنفيذ الامر على الغير کو۔ یعنی غیر پر حکم نافذ کرنا اکفاء جمع ہے کفو کی اور کفو کہتے ہیں نظیر اور ہمسر کو۔
حره، عاقلہ، بالغہ، باکرہ ہو یا شیبہ، اس کی رضا مندی کیساتھ بغیر ولی کے نکاح درست ہے
وينعقد نكاح الحرة العاقلة البالغة برضائها وان لم يعقد عليها ولى بكرا كانت اوثيبا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف في ظاهر الرواية وعن ابى يوسف انه لا ينعقد الابولى وعند محمد ينعقد موقوفا وقال مالک والشافعي لا ينعقد النكاح بعبارة النساء اصلالان النكاح يراد لمقاصده والتفويض اليهن مخل بها الاان محمد ايقول يرتفع الخلل باجازة الولى ووجه الجواز انها تصرفت فى خالص حقها وهى من اهله لكونها
Chapter on Guardians and Suitability. Translation: This chapter is about guardians and suitability. Explanation: 'Awliya' is plural of 'wali', derived from 'wilayah', and wilayah means executing command over others, i.e., enforcing a ruling on another. 'Akfa' is plural of 'kufu', and kufu means peer or equal. A free, sane, adult woman, whether virgin or non-virgin, with her consent, her marriage is valid without a guardian. And the marriage of a free, sane, adult woman is contracted with her consent, even if no guardian contracts it, whether she is a virgin or non-virgin, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is not contracted except with a guardian. And according to Muhammad, it is contracted but suspended (mawquf). And Malik and Shafi'i said: marriage is not contracted by the expression of women, because marriage is intended for its purposes and delegating to them is detrimental to it, except that Muhammad says the defect is removed by the guardian's permission. And the basis of permissibility is that she is acting in her pure right and she is of its people because...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage introduces Chapter on Guardians and Suitability in marriage. The text defines key terms: 'awliyā' (pl. of wali, from wilāyah meaning authority over others) and 'akfā' (pl. of kufu, meaning equal or match). It then states the ruling: a free, sane, adult woman can marry herself without a guardian, with her consent, whether she is a virgin or previously married. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāyah). There is a weaker narration from Abu Yusuf that a guardian is required. Muhammad says the marriage is suspended (mawqūf) until the guardian permits. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that women cannot contract their own marriage. The text gives a brief reason: marriage is for specific purposes, and delegating it to women is detrimental. Muhammad's view is that the guardian's permission can cure the defect. The permissibility is based on the woman acting in her own right (her pure right), and she is qualified (min ahlihi) to do so. The passage cuts off mid-sentence, so the full argument is not provided here.

Key Terms
ولی (wali): Guardian with authority to contract marriage on behalf of the bride. Here, the term is defined etymologically from wilāyah (authority to enforce commands on others).
کفو (kufu'): A suitable match; equality in social status, lineage, religion, etc., for marriage purposes.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a marriage that is valid but awaits approval (ijāzah) from the guardian to become fully effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāyah) of the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a free, sane, adult woman marrying without a guardian?
A) The marriage is invalid and requires a guardian.
B) The marriage is valid if she consents.
C) The marriage is suspended until the guardian approves.
D) The marriage is only valid for non-virgins.

Key Takeaway
A free, sane, adult woman's marriage is valid with her consent, even without a guardian, according to the apparent Hanafi position.
